Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
8 min
The Condition of Intellect ('Aql) for Narrator Reliability
Defines the condition of intellect for a narrator of hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'aql, identify its role as a condition for narrator reliability, and distinguish between complete and deficient intellect in the context of hadith transmission.

Core Idea
Intellect ('aql) is a condition for narrator reliability; only a sane adult's transmission is accepted.

The Hanafi school lays down four conditions for a narrator to be reliable: intellect, precision, integrity, and Islam. This lesson focuses on the first—intellect. We will explore its definition as a 'light' that enables the transition from sensory perception to intellectual deduction, and why a narrator must possess complete, adult intellect for the report to be considered valid proof (hujja).

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions of narrator reliability
The passage states that a khabar (report) is made hujja (proof) only if the narrator meets four conditions: intellect, precision, integrity, and Islam. List them and note that each is necessary.
This is a standard Hanafi classification (see al-Hidayah).
2
Analyze the definition of 'aql
The author defines 'aql as a 'light in the human body' by which the narrator illuminates the path from sensory perception to intellectual understanding. Describe the analogy: the eye sees a building, then intellect deduces the existence of a builder.
This is a rational (dalil 'aqli) proof, not a textual one.
3
Understand the role of the heart and the instrumentality of intellect
The author clarifies that, according to the people of Islam, the heart (qalb) is the perceiver of intelligibles, and the intellect is its instrument—like an inner eye that perceives after being illuminated by intellect. Contrast this with the philosophers' view that the rational soul perceives.
This affirms an Islamic epistemological stance against pure rationalism.
4
Distinguish between complete and deficient intellect
The passage specifies that the required intellect for narration is the 'complete intellect'—that of a mature adult (baligh). Deficient intellect—found in children, the insane, and mentally deficient persons—does not fulfill the condition.
The text is cut off here, but the implication is that such narrators are not accepted.
5
Relate the condition to legal competence (taklif)
Connect this condition to the Hanafi principle that only a sane adult is mukallaf (legally responsible). Since narration requires understanding and intentional transmission, a narrator must have the capacity for taklif.
This is why the reports of minors and the insane are rejected, unless the minor is discerning (mumayyiz) in some contexts, but the default condition is complete intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما جعل الخبر حجة بشرائط في الراوي وهي أربعة: العقل والضبط والعدالة والإسلام. فالعقل وهو نور في بدن الإنسان يضيء به طريق مبتدأه من حسه منتهى الحواس؟ أي نور يضيء بسبب ذلك نور؟ طريقه يبتدئ بذلك الطريق من مكان ينتهي إلى ذلك المكان درك الحواس مثلاً لو نظر أحد إلى بناء رفيع انتهى درك البصر إلى البناء ثم يبتدي منه طريق إلى أنه لا بد له من صانع ذي علم وحكمة. فمبتدأ العقول هو منتهى الحواس. وهذا فيما كان الانتقال من المحسوس إلى المعقول. وأما إذا كان معقولاً محضاً فإنما يبتدع به طريق العلم من حيث يوجد. فيبتدي المطلوب للطلب فيدركه القلب بتأمله. وفيه تثبيت على أن القلب مدرك والعقل آلة له على طريق أهل الإسلام. فللقلب عين باطنة يدرك بها الأشياء بعد إشراقه بالعقل. كما أن في الملك الظاهر تدرك العين بعد الإشراق بالشمس أو السراج. وعند الحكماء المدرك هو النفس الناطقة بواسطة العقل والحواس الظاهرة أو الباطنة. والشرط الكامل منه أي الشرط في باب رواية الحديث الكامل من العقل وهو عقل البالغ دون القاصر منه وهو عقل الصبي والمعتوه والمجنون لأن الشرع لما لم
And verily, the report (khabar) is made a proof with conditions in the narrator, which are four: intellect, precision, integrity, and Islam. Intellect: it is a light in the human body by which he illuminates the path; its beginning is from his sense, and the end of the senses? For example, if one looks at a tall building, the perception of sight ends at the building, then a path begins from there to deduce that it must have a maker with knowledge and wisdom. So the beginning of intellects is the end of the senses. This is when the transition is from the sensible to the intelligible. But if it is purely intellectual, then the path of knowledge begins from where it exists; the sought thing begins for the seeker, and the heart perceives it by reflection. There is confirmation that the heart is the perceiver and the intellect is an instrument for it according to the way of the people of Islam. For the heart has an inner eye by which it perceives things after being illuminated by the intellect, just as in the outward realm the eye perceives after illumination by the sun or lamp. According to the philosophers, the perceiver is the rational soul through the intellect and the apparent or inner senses. And the complete condition of it, i.e., the condition in the chapter of hadith narration, is the complete intellect, which is the intellect of the adult, not the deficient one, which is the intellect of the child, the insane, and the mentally deficient, because the Law (shar') when it did not...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage introduces the four conditions for a narrator to be considered reliable in transmitting hadith: intellect, precision, integrity, and Islam. It focuses on the definition of 'aql (intellect). Intellect is described as a light in the human body that enables the transition from sensory perception to intellectual understanding. The author provides an example: when seeing a building, the eye perceives it, then the intellect deduces the existence of a builder. This shows that the intellect starts where the senses end. For purely intellectual matters, the heart perceives them through reflection, with the intellect as an instrument. The author contrasts this with the philosophical view that the rational soul is the perceiver. Finally, it states that the required intellect for narration is that of an adult, not a child, insane person, or one mentally deficient, because Islamic legal responsibility (taklif) depends on complete intellect.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): A light enabling transition from sensory to intellectual knowledge, and an instrument for the heart to perceive intelligibles.
الضبط (ad-dabt): Precision: the narrator's ability to accurately memorize and transmit.
العدالة (al-'adala): Integrity: the narrator's uprightness and avoidance of major sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of intellect ('aql) in narration?
A) It is the only condition for accepting hadith
B) It is a light that allows the narrator to deduce rulings from hadith
C) It is an instrument for the heart to perceive intelligible matters and a condition for narrator reliability
D) It is unnecessary because the text is sufficient

Key Takeaway
Complete intellect (adult, sane) is a necessary condition for narrator reliability; deficient intellect disqualifies the narrator.

Definition of 'Adalah and Its Conditions in Hanafi Usul
Defining 'adalah and its conditions, with enumeration of major sins and discussion of deficient integrity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'adalah in the Hanafi usuli context, identify the conditions for its validity, and distinguish between full 'adalah and 'adalah qasirah.

Core Idea
A witness/narrator's 'adalah requires preponderance of religion and intellect over desires; occasional minor sins do not break it.

In the Hanafi school, the concept of 'adalah (integrity) is fundamental for accepting testimony and hadith narration. This passage from a classical usul text defines 'adalah precisely, specifying when a person's integrity is compromised. It also enumerates major sins and introduces the notion of 'adalah qasirah (deficient integrity). Understanding these distinctions is crucial for evaluating the reliability of narrators and witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
Recognize that 'adalah is being defined in the context of witnesses and narrators. The definition is not about general virtue but about legally acceptable integrity.
The passage begins with 'والمُعْتَبَرُ ههنا' referring to the condition considered in this context.
2
Analyze the definition components
Break down the definition: 'preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over the way of desire and lust.' Note that both religion and intellect are weighted together against desire.
3
Determine the effect of sins on 'adalah
Identify the two conditions that cause 'adalah to fall: committing a major sin, or persisting on a minor sin. Understand that occasional minor sins without persistence do not affect 'adalah because complete sinlessness is for prophets.
The text uses 'سَقَطَتْ عَدَالَتُهُ' for falling, and 'لَمْ تَسْقُطْ' for remaining intact.
4
Examine the lists of major sins (kaba'ir)
Note the different reports from companions (Ibn 'Umar, Abu Hurayrah, 'Ali, and others) listing major sins. Observe that there is no single definitive list; the concept is relative.
The relative view is mentioned: 'كُلُّ ذَنْبٍ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا تَحْتَهُ كَبِيرٌ'.
5
Distinguish between full 'adalah and 'adalah qasirah
Understand that 'adalah qasirah is based on apparent Islam and intellect. It is insufficient for hadith narration but accepted for testimony in non-hadd/qisas cases unless challenged by the opponent.
The passage contrasts the weaker basis with the stronger full 'adalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمُعْتَبَرُ ههنا كَمَا لَها وَهُوَ رُجْحَانُ جِهَةِ الدِّيْنِ وَالْعَقْلِ عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْهَوَى والشهوةِ حَتَّى إِذَا ارْتَكَبَ كَبِيرَةً أَوْ أَصَرَّ عَلَى صَغِيْرَةٍ سَقَطَتْ عَدَالَتُهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُصِرَّ عَلَى صَغِيْرَةٍ بَلْ يَلِمُ بِهَا أَحْيَانًا لَمْ تَسْقُطْ عَدَالَتَهُ لأَنَّ الِاحْتِرَازَ عَنْ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالتَّعَذُّرُ فِي حَقِّ عَامَّةِ الْبَشَرِ وَالإِصْرَارُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْكَبِيرَةِ فَيَجِبُ الاِحْتِرَازُ عَنْهُ وَفِي الْكَبَائِرِ اخْتِلافٌ فَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّهَا سَبْعٌ الإِشْرَاكُ بِاللهِ وَقَتْلُ النَّفْسِ الْمُؤْمِنَةِ وَقَذْفُ الْمُحْصَنَةِ [؟] وَالْفِرَارُ مِنَ الزَّحْفِ وَأَكْلُ مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ وَعُقُوقُ الْوَالِدَيْنِ الْمُسْلِمَيْنِ وَالإِلْحَادُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَرَوَى أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ مَعَ ذَلِكَ أَكْلُ الرِّبَا وَعَلَيْهِ أَضَافَ إِلَى ذَلِكَ السَّرِقَةَ وَشُرْبَ الْخَمْرِ وَزَادَ بَعْضُهُمُ الزِّنَا وَاللِّوَاطَ وَالسِّحْرَ وَشَهَادَةَ الزُّورِ وَالْيَمِينَ الْكَاذِبَةَ وَقَطْعَ الطَّرِيقِ وَالْغِيبَةَ وَالْقِمَارَ وَقِيلَ هُمَا أَمْرَانِ إِضَافِيَّانِ فَكُلُّ ذَنْبٍ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا تَحْتَهُ كَبِيرٌ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ مَا فَوْقَهُ صَغِيرٌ دُونَ قُصُورِهَا وَهُوَ مَا ثَبَتَ بِظَاهِرِ الإِسْلامِ وَاعْتِدَالِ العَقْلِ فَإِنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّ كُلَّ مَنْ هُوَ مُسْلِمٌ مُعْتَدِلُ العَقْلِ لا يَكْذِبُ وَيَمْتَنِعُ عَنْ خِلافِ الشَّرْعِ وَلَكِنْ هَذَا لا يَكْفِي لِرِوَايَةِ الحَدِيثِ لأَنَّ هَذَا الظَّاهِرَ يُعَارِضُهُ ظَاهِرٌ آخَرُ وَهُوَ هَوَى النَّفْسِ فَكَانَ عَدْلاً مِنْ وَجْهٍ دُونَ وَجْهٍ إِنَّمَا يَكْفِي هَذَا فِي الشَّاهِدِ فِي غَيْرِ الحُدُودِ وَالقِصَاصِ مَا لَمْ يَطْعُنِ الخَصْمُ فَإِذَا كَانَ فِي الحُدُودِ وَالقِصَاصِ أَوْ طَعَنَ الخَصْمُ فِيهِ لا يَكْفِي هَهُنَا أَيْضًا
And what is considered here is as she has, and it is the preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over the way of desire and lust, such that if he commits a major sin or persists on a minor sin, his integrity falls. And if he does not persist on a minor sin but rather commits it occasionally, his integrity does not fall, because avoidance of all that is from the characteristics of the prophets, and it is difficult for the general people. And persistence on that is like a major sin, so avoidance is obligatory. And there is disagreement concerning major sins: from Ibn 'Umar that they are seven: associating partners with Allah, killing a believing soul, accusing a chaste woman [of adultery?], fleeing from battle, consuming the wealth of an orphan, disobedience to Muslim parents, and apostasy in the Sacred Precinct. And Abu Hurayrah narrated along with that the consuming of usury. And 'Ali added to that theft and drinking wine. And some added to that adultery, sodomy, magic, false testimony, false oath, highway robbery, backbiting, and gambling. And it was said that they are two relative matters: every sin with respect to what is below it is major, and with respect to what is above it is minor, except its deficiency? And it is what is established by the apparent of Islam and moderation of intellect. For the apparent is that every Muslim who is of moderate intellect does not lie and refrains from contravening the Shari'ah. But this is not sufficient for narration of hadith, because this apparent is opposed by another apparent, which is the desire of the soul. So he is 'adl from one aspect and not from another. Rather this is sufficient for testimony in other than hadd and qisas cases as long as the opponent does not challenge. So if it is in hadd or qisas cases, or the opponent challenges him, it is not sufficient here either.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a definition of 'adalah (integrity) in the context of witnesses and narrators. The author states that 'adalah is the preponderance of the aspect of religion and intellect over desires and lust. This is the criterion: if a person commits a major sin or persists on a minor sin, his 'adalah is lost. However, if he commits a minor sin without persistence, his 'adalah remains, because complete avoidance is only possible for prophets. The text then lists various opinions on the major sins (kaba'ir), including the seven according to Ibn 'Umar, with additions from other companions. It also notes that some scholars view sins as relative: a sin can be considered major relative to what is below it and minor relative to what is above it. The author then discusses 'adalah qasirah (deficient integrity), which is based on the apparent Islam and moderation of intellect. This is insufficient for hadith narration because it is outweighed by the desire of the soul. However, for testimony in other than hadd and qisas, it is sufficient as long as the opponent does not raise a challenge.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-'adalah): Preponderance of religion and intellect over desires, resulting in avoidance of major sins and non-persistence on minor sins.
الكبيرة (al-kabirah): A major sin; specifically listed with differing opinions (seven or more).
عدالة قاصرة ('adalah qasirah): Deficient integrity based on apparent Islam and intellect, insufficient for hadith narration but sufficient for testimony except in hadd/qisas cases if not challenged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a person's 'adalah if he commits a minor sin occasionally without persisting?
A) His 'adalah is completely lost.
B) His 'adalah is not lost.
C) His 'adalah becomes qasirah.
D) His 'adalah is only accepted in hadd cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'adalah emphasizes preponderance of religion and intellect, with loss triggered only by major sins or persistence on minor sins, and distinguishes between full 'adalah and 'adalah qasirah for different contexts.

Definition of Islam as Tasdiq and Iqrar
Defining Islam as inner tasdiq and verbal iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Islam as consisting of tasdiq and iqrar according to the Hanafi school, identify the Quranic proof for the distinction between tasdiq and passive acknowledgment, and explain the legal role of iqrar.

Core Idea
Islam = inner voluntary affirmation (tasdiq) + verbal declaration (iqrar); mere recognition is not faith.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text lays out the legal definition of Islam. It emphasizes that being a Muslim requires both inner conviction of the heart and verbal confession. The author clarifies that mere passive acknowledgment (idh'an) of the truth, which can occur even in disbelievers, does not constitute faith. This distinction has important implications for the application of Islamic rulings in areas such as inheritance, marriage, and apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
What are the two elements mentioned for Islam? Locate 'tasdiq' and 'iqrar' in the text.
2
Analyze tasdiq
What does tasdiq mean? How is it different from mere idh'an (passive acknowledgment)? The text says tasdiq is 'attributing truth to the informer voluntarily'.
Voluntary is key.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Why does the author cite Quran 2:146? How does the verse support the distinction between tasdiq and idh'an?
The verse shows disbelievers can have knowledge but still disbelieve.
4
Determine the role of iqrar
Is iqrar a condition or a pillar? The text says 'shartun li ijra al-ahkam aw ruknun mithla al-tasdiq'. What difference does this make?
Legally, condition vs. pillar affects validity.
5
Connect to broader usul principle
How does this definition relate to the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by intentions? How does it affect rulings on apostasy?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإسلامُ وَهُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ وَالإِقْرَارُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى كَمَا هُوَ وَاقِعٌ فَالتَّصْدِيقُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ نِسْبَةِ الصِّدْقِ إِلَى الْمُخْبِرِ [؟] اِخْتِيَارًا لأَنَّ الإِذْعَانَ [؟] قَدْ يَقَعُ فِي قَلْبِ الْكَافِرِ بِالضَّرُورَةِ وَلا يُسَمَّى ذَلِكَ إِيْمَانًا قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ وَحُصُولُ هَذَا الْمَعْنَى لِلْكُفَّارِ مَمْنُوعٌ وَلَوْ سُلِّمَ فَكَفْرُهُمْ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَمَارَاتِ الإِنْكَارِ وَالأَقْرَارُ شَرْطٌ لإِجْرَاءِ الأَحْكَامِ أَوْ رُكْنٌ مِثْلَ التَّصْدِيقِ
And Islam: it is tasdiq (affirmation of truth) and iqrar (verbal acknowledgment) of Allah the Exalted as He is. So tasdiq is an expression of attributing truth to the informer [or: to the One who informs?] voluntarily, because passive acknowledgment [or: conviction] may occur in the heart of a disbeliever by necessity, and that is not called faith. Allah the Exalted said: 'They know him as they know their own sons.' And the occurrence of this meaning for disbelievers is denied, and if it is conceded, their disbelief is on account of signs of denial. And iqrar is a condition for the application of legal rulings, or a pillar like tasdiq.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage defines Islam (in the sense of being a Muslim) as consisting of two components: tasdiq (inner affirmation of the truth) and iqrar (verbal declaration). Tasdiq is an act of will, attributing truth to the informer (the Prophet, conveying from Allah). The text clarifies that mere passive conviction (idh'an) that may occur in a disbeliever's heart out of necessity, such as knowing the truth of the Prophet like they know their own sons, is not called faith (iman). Such knowledge can coexist with disbelief due to signs of denial. The Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:146) is cited to illustrate that disbelievers can recognize the truth but still reject it. Furthermore, iqrar (verbal acknowledgment) is considered a condition for the application of Islamic rulings (like inheritance, marriage, etc.) or a pillar equivalent to tasdiq. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on the integration of inner belief and outer declaration for legal recognition of Islam.

Key Terms
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Voluntary inner affirmation of truth, specifically attributing truth to the informer (Allah and His Prophet).
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Verbal declaration of belief; a condition or pillar for applying Islamic legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that a disbeliever's inner knowledge of the Prophet is not iman?
A) Because it is not accompanied by verbal iqrar.
B) Because it occurs out of necessity and is not voluntary.
C) Because it is based on conjecture.
D) Because it is not confirmed by the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Islam requires both voluntary inner affirmation (tasdiq) and verbal declaration (iqrar); mere knowledge or passive recognition does not constitute faith.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of 'Adalat and Its Levels
Defining 'adalat and its conditions for testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'adalat, identify its conditions (shurut) and preventers (mawani), and distinguish between full 'adalat and deficient 'adalat (al-'adalat al-qasirah) for testimony versus hadith narration.

Core Idea
'Adalat requires avoidance of major sins and persistence on minor sins; deficient 'adalat suffices for testimony but not hadith.

This lesson examines the concept of 'adalat (legal probity) as a condition for accepting testimony and hadith narration in Hanafi usul. The passage defines 'adalat, explains when it is invalidated (persistence on minor sins equals major sins), and introduces the important distinction between full and deficient 'adalat. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating the reliability of witnesses and narrators in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of 'adalat
Read the opening line: 'The name for it in legal terminology is 'adalat.' Note that 'adalat is the quality of being upright and trustworthy, avoiding major sins and not persisting on minor sins.
The definition implies both refrain from major sins and from persistent minor sins.
2
Analyze the condition of persistence on minor sins
The text states that occasional minor sin without persistence does not break 'adalat, but persistent minor sin is equivalent to major sin and invalidates 'adalat. Identify this as a key Hanafi principle.
Persistence (الإصرار) is the key factor; the act itself being minor is not enough to invalidate 'adalat.
3
Examine the enumerations of major sins
The passage lists various narrations of major sins (kaba'ir) from different Companions. Note that these are examples; the exact list is not exhaustively defined. The text also mentions a relative view of major/minor sins.
The disagreement on the exact list does not affect the general principle that major sins invalidate 'adalat.
4
Distinguish full 'adalat from deficient 'adalat
The text introduces 'deficient 'adalat' (al-'adalat al-qasirah), which is established by apparent Islam and sound intellect. This is sufficient for testimony in non-hadd/qisas cases, but insufficient for hadith narration.
The rationale: for hadith, there is a conflicting apparent – carnal desire – so a stricter standard is required.
5
Apply the distinction to testimony and narration
The passage states that deficient 'adalat is acceptable for testimony except in hadd and qisas cases, and only if the opponent does not challenge it. For hadith narration, full 'adalat is required.
This shows a graded approach to 'adalat based on the gravity of the matter.

رہنے کا نام شرعی اصطلاح میں عدالت ہے پس اگر کوئی شخص گناہ صغیرہ پر اصرار ہیں کر تا ہو بلکہ کبھی کبھی مرتکب ہو جاتا ہو تو اس کی عدالت ساتھ نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ صغیر و کبیرہ گناہوں سے مکمل اجتناب و احتر از حضرات انبیاء علیہم السلام کا خاصہ ہے۔ اور عام لوگوں کے لئے نہایت دشوار، اور گناہ صغیرہ پر اصر ان قائم مقام کبیرہ گناہ کے ہے لہذا اس سے بچنا واجب ہے اور گناہ کبیرہ میں اختلاف ہے۔۔ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر سے روایت ہے ۔ وہ سات ہیں۔ اشراک باللہ ، عمل نفس، قذف الحصہ کسی پاکدامن عورت کو زنا کی نسبت لگانا ) فرار عن الزحف (چہار سے بھاگنا ) اكل مال اليتيم ( یتیم کا مال کھانا ) ، عقوق الوالدين للمسلمين (مسلم والدین کے حقوق کی نافرمانی ایسے کام میں جو گناہ کے نہ ہوں) والالحاد فی الحرم حرم شریف میں بے دینی کی طرف مائل ہونا اور حضرت ابو ہر پیر نے اس کے ساتھ اكل الزبوا ( سود کھانا کی روایت کی ہے اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے اس کے ساتھ شرب خمر اور سرقہ (چوری) کا اضافہ کیا ہے اور بعض نے زنا اور لواطت، سحر (جاره) شهادت الزور (جھوٹی گواہی)، یمین کاذبہ (جھوٹی قسم)، قطع الطريق (ڈاکہ زنی)، نجیبت اور قمار (جوا) کا اضافہ کیا ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ گناہ صغیر و کبیر و دونوں امور اضافیہ میں سے ہیں پس ہر گناہ اپنے مافوق کے لحاظ سے صغیرہ اپنے ماتحت کے لحاظ سے کبیرہ ہے۔ دون قصورها القصور استقامت عدالت قاصره) معتبر نہیں ہے اور عدالت قاصرہ وہ ہے جو ظاہر اسلام اور اعتدال عقل سے ثابت ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ ظاہر بات ہے کہ ہر مسلمان معتدل العقل ہوتا ہے۔ جھوٹ نہیں بولتا۔ اور خلاف شرع افعال کرنے سے احتراز کرتا ہے مگر روایت حدیث کے لئے اس قدر کافی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس ظاہر کا دوسرا ظاہر معارض ہے اور وہ خواہش نفسانی ہے، لہذا، ایسا شخص من وجہ عادل ہو گا۔ اور من وجہ عادل نہ ہو گا ہاں اتنی عدالت شہادت کے باب میں کافی ہو گی مگر وہ شہادت حدود و قصاص کے باب میں نہ ہو۔ یہ بھی اس وقت قبول ہوگی جب کے اس کی شہادت پر مخالف مطعون نہ کریں اور جب مسئلہ حدود قصاص کا ہو گا یا گواہ کو خصم طعن و تشنیع کرنا ہو گا تو اتنی عدالت بھی نا کافی ہوگی۔
The name for it in legal terminology is 'adalat. So if a person does not persist in minor sin but occasionally commits it, his 'adalat is not dropped. Because complete avoidance of minor and major sins is the special quality of the prophets, and for common people it is very difficult. And persistence in minor sin is equivalent to major sin, so avoiding it is obligatory. There is disagreement on major sins. It is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar: they are seven: associating partners with Allah, killing a soul, slandering a chaste woman accusing her of adultery, fleeing from battle, consuming the orphan's wealth, disobedience to Muslim parents, and inclining to irreligion in the Sacred Sanctuary. Abu Huraira added consuming usury, and Ali added drinking wine and theft. Some added adultery, sodomy, sorcery, false testimony, false oath, highway robbery, gambling. Some said minor and major sins are relative; every sin is minor relative to what is above it and major relative to what is below it. Deficient 'adalat is not valid. Deficient 'adalat is that which is established by apparent Islam and soundness of intellect. Because it is obvious that every Muslim is of sound intellect, does not lie, and refrains from actions contrary to Sharia. But for transmitting hadith this is not sufficient because this apparent is contradicted by another apparent, which is carnal desire. Therefore such a person is 'adl in one respect and not 'adl in another. However, this much 'adalat is sufficient for testimony except in hadd and qisas. It is also accepted only if the opponent does not challenge his testimony. When the matter is of hadd or qisas, or the opponent will object, then such 'adalat is insufficient.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage defines 'adalat (trustworthiness/justice) for the purpose of testimony and narration. It begins by stating that persistent minor sin is equivalent to major sin and breaks 'adalat, whereas occasional minor sin without persistence does not. It then lists various enumerations of major sins attributed to different Companions, including the well-known seven from Ibn Umar. The text also introduces the concept of 'deficient 'adalat' (al-'adalat al-qasirah), which is based on apparent Islam and outward uprightness. For the purpose of hadith narration, this is insufficient due to potential hidden faults, but for judicial testimony it is acceptable except in hadd and qisas cases, and only if unchallenged by the opponent. The author follows the Hanafi position that 'adalat is a condition for both narration and testimony, but the standard is stricter for narration.

Key Terms
عدالت (ʿadālat): Legal probity; the quality of being upright and trustworthy, avoiding major sins and not persisting on minor sins.
عدالت قاصرہ (ʿadālat qāṣirah): Deficient probity based on apparent Islam and sound intellect, sufficient for testimony in non-hadd/qisas cases if unchallenged.
اصرار (iṣrār): Persistence on a minor sin; elevates the sin to the level of a major sin regarding 'adalat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a person who occasionally commits a minor sin without persistence?
A) His 'adalat is completely invalid.
B) His 'adalat is not invalidated, but he cannot testify in hadd cases with deficient 'adalat.
C) He is considered a fasiq and cannot be a witness at all.
D) His 'adalat is deficient and never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'adalat requires avoidance of major sins and non-persistence on minor sins; deficient 'adalat (apparent uprightness) suffices for testimony in non-hadd/qisas cases but not for hadith narration.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Subject Matter of Reports: Rights of Allah and Rights of Servants
Classification of khabar's subject matter and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the subject matter of a report (khabar) into the five types and identify the conditions for accepting a single report (khabar wahid) in Huquq Allah and Huquq al-Ibad with pure obligation (ilzam mahd).

Core Idea
A single report is accepted broadly in divine rights but requires testimony in pure obligations of servants.

This passage introduces a fundamental classification in Hanafi usul: how we evaluate reports (akhbar) depends on what they are about. Are they about the rights of Allah (worship, punishments) or the rights of human beings (debts, property)? The answer determines whether a single narrator suffices or strict testimony conditions apply, including freedom and the wording 'ashhadu'. This distinction is crucial for understanding how evidence is weighed in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Five Types
Memorize that reports are divided into rights of Allah (punishments and non-punishments) and rights of servants (pure obligation, no obligation, mixed obligation).
This is the foundational classification.
2
Rule for Huquq Allah
Note that in rights of Allah, a single report is generally accepted without condition of number, as the Companions accepted Aisha's single hadith about purification.
Exception: al-Karkhi disagreed for punishments.
3
Conditions for Huquq al-Ibad with Ilzam Mahd
For pure obligations (e.g., debts), the report must meet strict testimony conditions: two witnesses, free, saying 'ashhadu', and having jurisdiction.
This is because it involves imposing a duty on another.
4
Understand the Dispute with al-Karkhi
Al-Karkhi argued that a single report cannot establish hudud because of ambiguity, but the author (following Abu Hanifa) accepts it based on practice of the Salaf.
This dispute shows the range of opinions within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the Rules
Consider a scenario: a single person reports that Zaid owes him money. According to the passage, what conditions must be met for this report to be accepted? Answer: It must be testimony by two free witnesses using 'ashhadu'.
Contrast with a report about a religious obligation, where one reliable person suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The third division: concerning the subject matter of the report in which the report is considered authoritative. It is either rights of Allah, which are two types: punishments and others, or rights of servants, which are three types: that which involves pure obligation, or no obligation at all, or obligation in one way but not another. So these are five types. This division applies to any single report, whether it is a report of the Messenger, his Companions, or common people from the market, and it is from the well-known themes of the majority of the Salaf, following the pride of Islam (Imam Abu Hanifa). If it is from the rights of Allah, then the report of a single person is authoritative, whether it is about acts of worship or punishments or matters combining both or between them, but it is said without the condition of multiple narrators because the Companions accepted the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet' from Aisha alone. And it is said with the condition of multiple narrators because the Prophet did not accept the report of Dhul-Yadain concerning the incompleteness of his prayer until he added another report. Contrary to al-Karkhi regarding punishments: he does not accept a single report in them and does not establish hadd punishments from them because reporting it from the Messenger involves ambiguity, and hadd punishments are fixed by estimation. As for establishing them by clear evidences before the judge, that is permitted by text contrary to analogy, and it is His saying 'So call to witness four of them' and the like. And because hadd punishments are not established by clear evidences; rather their causes are established, while the punishments themselves are established by the Book. And if it is from the rights of servants, involving pure obligation, like a report establishing a right against someone in debts, specific sold items, pledges, or usurped items, then all conditions of reports are required: intellect, uprightness, precision, Islam, with number and the wording of testimony and jurisdiction, that there be two, and that they say 'I testify', and that they have jurisdiction through freedom. When these conditions together with the four common conditions are met, then the report of a single person is accepted before the judge in transactions which impose obligation on the defendant.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a definition/classification of the subject matter (mahall) of a khabar. It divides reports into two main categories: rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-ibad). Rights of Allah are further divided into punishments (hudud, etc.) and non-punishments (ibaadaat). Rights of servants are divided into three: those that involve a pure obligation (ilzam mahd), those with no obligation, and those with obligation from one perspective but not another. This yields five types. For rights of Allah, a single reporter is generally accepted, though there is a difference: some require multiple narrators (as in the hadith of Dhul-Yadain), but the Companions accepted Aisha's single report about ritual purification. al-Karkhi held that in hudud, a single report is not accepted because of ambiguity. For rights of servants with pure obligation (like debts), stricter conditions apply: two witnesses, free, saying 'ashhadu', etc. The passage uses Hanafi usul terminology and references.

Key Terms
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights that belong to Allah, including acts of worship (ibadat) and punishments (uqubat).
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights that belong to human beings, such as debts and property.
الزام محض (ilzam mahd): A pure obligation; a claim that imposes a duty on the defendant without counter-obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a report to be accepted in matters of pure obligation (ilzam mahd)?
A) Just a single reliable narrator.
B) Two witnesses, free, using the word 'ashhadu', with jurisdiction.
C) Four witnesses as for zina.
D) A written document is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The authority of a single report in Hanafi usul depends on its subject matter: broadly accepted in Huquq Allah, but in Huquq al-Ibad with pure obligation, it must meet the conditions of shahada.

The Acceptance of Khabar al-Wahid in Rights of Allah: Classification and Dispute
Explains the third division of the subject matter of khabar and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of subject matter for khabar al-wahid as proof, apply the rule that khabar al-wahid is accepted in rights of Allah without condition of number, and evaluate al-Karkhi's objection regarding punishments.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid is accepted in all rights of Allah, though al-Karkhi excludes hudud due to doubts.

This lesson explores the third classification in usul al-fiqh: the subject matter (mahall) of a khabar that qualifies as proof. The text distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of servants, and within rights of Allah, it addresses the probative value of khabar al-wahid. You will learn the standard Hanafi position, the internal dispute over requiring multiple narrators, and al-Karkhi's specific dissent regarding punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories of mahall
List the five types: rights of Allah (punishments and non-punishments) and rights of servants (pure imposition, no imposition, partial imposition).
This classification is for all khabar al-wahid, not just Prophetic reports.
2
Determine the ruling for khabar al-wahid in rights of Allah
Recognize that the text states khabar al-wahid is hujja (proof) in rights of Allah, both in worship and punishments.
The passage calls this an indulgence (musamaha) of the Salaf.
3
Distinguish the two positions on the condition of number
One view requires no specific number, citing the Companions' acceptance of Aisha's single hadith on ghusl. Another requires two narrators, citing the Prophet's initial rejection of Dhul-Yadayn's report.
The text presents both but leans toward the majority without condition.
4
Analyze al-Karkhi's exception for punishments
Al-Karkhi rejects khabar al-wahid in hudud because such reports raise doubts, and hudud are repelled by doubts. The Hanafi response is that hudud are established by the Quran, not by khabar; khabar only establishes causes.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical scenario
Consider whether a single reliable report about a new cause for a hadd penalty (e.g., a confession) would be accepted. Apply the Hanafi position: it establishes the cause, but the penalty itself is from the Quran.
Practical outcome: testimony of one witness may be accepted for establishing the cause, not the punishment itself.

وَالتَّقْسِيْمُ الثَّالِثُ فِي بَيَانِ مَعَلُ الْخَبَرِ الَّذِى جُعِلَ الخَبَر فِيهِ حُمَّةٌ وَهُوَ إِمَّا حَقُوق اللهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ عُقُوبَاتٌ وَغَيْرُهَا وَإِما حَقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ وَهُوَ ثَلَاثَةُ أَقْسَامٍ مَا فِيْهِ إِلزام مَحْضَ أَوْ لَا الزَامَ فِيهِ أصلاً أوْ فِيْهِ الْالزَامَ مِنْ وَجْهِ دُونَ وَجْةٍ فَهَذَا خَمْسَةُ أنْوَاعِ وَهذَا التَّقْسِيمُ لِمُطلَقِ الْخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ أَعَمُ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ خَبَرَ الرَّسُولِ أَوْ أَصْحَابِهِ أَوْ عَامَّةِ الْخَلْقِ مِنْ أَهْلِ السُّوقِ وَهِيَ مِنَ الْمُسَامحَاتِ المَشْهُورَةِ لِجَمْهُورِ السَّلَفِ اقْتِدَاءَ بِفَخْرِ الإسْلَامِ فَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ حُقوقِ الله تَعَالَى يَكُونُ خَبَرُ الْوَاحِدِ فِيهِ حُمَّةٌ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مِنَ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَالْعُقُوبَاتِ أَوْ دَائِرَا بَيْنَهُمَا أَوْ مَؤنَةٌ مَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا وَلَكِنْ قِيْلَ بِلا شَرْطِ عَدَدٍ لأن الصحابة قبلوا حَدِيث إِذَا الْتَقَى الْخِتَانَانِ مِنْ عَائِشَةَ وَحْدَهَا وَقِيلَ بِشَرط عَدَدٍ لأن النبي عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَمْ يَقْبَلُ خَبَرَ ذِي الْيَدَيْنِ فِي عَدَم تَمَام صَلوَتِهِ مَالَمْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهِ خَبَرَ غَيْرِهِ خِلافًا لِلْكَرْخِي فِي الْعُقُوبَاتِ فَإِنَّهُ لا يَقْبَلُ فِيْهَا خَبَرَ الْوَاحِدِ وَلَا يَثْبِتُ الْحُدُودَ مِنْه لأن فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ عَلَى الرَّسُوْلِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ شُبْهَةٌ وَالْحُدُودُ تَفْدِرِى بِهَا وَأَمَّا إِثْبَاتُهَا بِالبَيِّنَاتِ عِنْدَ الْقَاضِي فَيَجُوزُ بِالنَّص عَلَى خِلَافِ الْقَيَاسِ وَهُوَ قَوْله تَعَالَى فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةٌ مِنْكُمْ وَأَمْثَالُة ولأن الحدود لم تثبت بالبَيِّنَاتِ وَإِنَّمَا تَثْبُتُ أَسْبَابُهَا وَالْحُدُودُ ثَابِتَةٌ بِالْكِتَابِ.
And the third division is about the explanation of the locus of the report that is made a proof. It is either rights of Allah the Exalted, and they are of two types: punishments and others; or rights of the servants, and they are of three types: that which has pure imposition, or that which has no imposition at all, or that which has imposition from one aspect but not another; thus these are five types. And this division is for the absolute khabar al-wahid, general whether it is the report of the Messenger or of his Companions or of the general people from the marketplace. And it is among the famous indulgences of the majority of the Salaf, following the pride of Islam. So if it is from the rights of Allah the Exalted, then the khabar al-wahid therein is a proof, whether it is from acts of worship and punishments, or encompasses both, or with responsibility accompanying one of them. But it is said without the condition of number because the Companions accepted the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet' from Aisha alone. And it is said with the condition of number because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not accept the report of Dhul-Yadayn regarding the incompletion of his prayer until he joined to it the report of another. Contrary to al-Karkhi regarding punishments, for he does not accept therein khabar al-wahid and does not establish the hudud from it, because in establishing it upon the Messenger, peace be upon him, there is doubt, and hudud are repelled by doubts. As for establishing them by evidence before the judge, it is permitted by text contrary to analogy, and it is His statement: 'Then bring four witnesses from among you' and similar examples. And because hudud are not established by evidence, rather their causes are established, and hudud are established by the Book.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage explains the third classification regarding the subject matter (mahall) of a khabar based on which it is considered hujja (proof). There are five categories: rights of Allah (two: punishments and others) and rights of servants (three: pure imposition, no imposition, and partial imposition). The author states that this classification applies to all khabar al-wahid, whether from the Prophet, Companions, or common people. Following the majority of the Salaf, khabar al-wahid is accepted in rights of Allah without needing a specific number of narrators, though there is disagreement. The text presents two positions: one holds that no number is required, citing the acceptance of Aisha's hadith about ghusl from the meeting of circumcised parts. The other requires two narrators, citing the Prophet's initial rejection of Dhul-Yadayn's report about the prayer until another witness confirmed it. Imam al-Karkhi differs regarding punishments: he does not accept khabar al-wahid for hudud because such reports are uncertain and hudud are repelled by doubts. However, establishing hudud through testimony (bayyinah) before a judge is allowed by nass (Quranic text) contrary to qiyas, as the Quran requires four witnesses for zina. The author clarifies that hudud themselves are proven by the Book, not by testimony; testimony only proves their causes.

Key Terms
حقوق الله تعالى (huquq Allah ta'ala): Matters pertaining to obligations owed to Allah, including worship (ibadat) and punishments (uqubat).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on accepting khabar al-wahid in rights of Allah (huquq Allah)?
A) It is always rejected.
B) It is accepted without condition of number.
C) It is accepted only if two narrators report.
D) It is accepted only in worship, not punishments.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, khabar al-wahid is accepted as proof in all rights of Allah, including punishments, but the dispute over number and al-Karkhi's exception for hudud highlights the role of doubt in penal matters.

Rights of Servants: Conditions for Acceptance of Khabar
Details conditions for accepting khabar in pure imposition cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid in cases of pure imposition (ilzam mahd) and apply them to distinguish between ilzam and non-ilzam reports.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid requires full testimony conditions only when it imposes liability; without imposition, fewer conditions apply.

This passage from the Hanafi usul text details the heightened evidentiary requirements when a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) is used to establish a right that imposes a burden on someone. The author expands on the general conditions of khabar by adding specific requirements drawn from the rules of testimony (shahada). Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the correct standard of proof in different legal claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of rights of servants
The passage distinguishes between cases with pure imposition (ilzam mahd) and those without. Ilzam mahd includes debts, sales, pledges, and usurpation.
2
List the general conditions of khabar
The 'preceding four' conditions are intelligence, uprightness, precision, and Islam. These are always required for khabar al-wahid.
These are the baseline conditions from earlier in the text.
3
Understand the added conditions for ilzam mahd
For imposition cases, additional conditions are required: the narrators must be two, they must use the wording of shahada ('Ashhadu'), and they must have wilayah (legal capacity, including freedom).
These conditions mirror those of testimony in court.
4
See how the added conditions transform khabar
When all conditions are met, the khabar becomes equivalent to testimony and is accepted as a binding proof before the judge in transactions involving imposition.
5
Contrast with cases of no imposition
For reports like agency, mudarabah, or gifts, the added conditions are not required; the general conditions suffice. This distinction is crucial for ijtihad.
The passage cuts off but the contrast is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ حُقوق الْعِبَادِ مِمَّا فِيْهِ الْزَامُ مَحْضَ كَخَبَرَ إِثْبَاتِ الْحَقِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ فِي الدُّيُونِ وَالأَعْيَانِ الْمَبِيْعَةِ وَالْمُرْتَبِنَةِ وَالْمَغْصَوْبَةِ تُشْتَرَطُ فِيهِ سَائِرُ شَرَائِطِ الأَخْبَارِ مِنَ الْعَقْلِ وَالْعَدَالَةِ وَالضَّبْطِ وَالإِسْلَامِ مَعَ الْعَدَدِ وَلَفْطِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالْوِلايَةِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ اثْنَيْنِ وَيَتَلَفَّظُ بِقَوْلِهِ أَشْهَدُ وَتَكُونُ لَهُ الْوِلايَةُ بِالْحُرِّيَةِ فَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَتْ هَذِهِ الشَّرَائِط مَعَ الأَرْبَعَةِ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يُقْبَلُ خَبَرُ الْوَاحِدِ عِنْدَ الْقَاضِي فِي الْمَعَامَلاَتِ الَّتِي فِيهَا الْالزَام عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا الْزَامَ فِيْهِ أَصْلاً كَخَبَرِ الْوِكَالَةِ وَالْمُضَارَبَةِ وَالرِّسَالَةِ فِي الْهَدَايَا
And if it is from the rights of servants, from that which has pure imposition, like the report of establishing a right against someone in debts, sold goods, pledged goods, and usurped goods, then all conditions of reports are required in it: intelligence, uprightness, precision, and Islam, together with number and the wording of testimony and authority, such that they be two and utter with his statement 'I testify' and he has authority by freedom. So when these conditions are combined with the preceding four, then the khabar al-wahid is accepted before the judge in transactions that have imposition upon the defendant. And if there is no imposition at all, like the report of agency, mudarabah, and sending gifts...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid in matters involving pure imposition (ilzam mahd) on a defendant, such as claims for debts, goods sold, pledged (mortgaged), or usurped. Here, the report must meet all the conditions of testimony (shahada): the reporter must be sane, upright (`adil), precise (dabit), and Muslim. Additionally, there must be a number of two narrators, they must use the wording 'Ashhadu' ('I testify'), and they must have legal authority (wilayah), which includes freedom (hurriyah). These conditions are added to the four general conditions of acceptance (intelligence, uprightness, precision, Islam). When all are met, the khabar al-wahid is accepted before the judge in transactions that impose liability. The passage then introduces another type: cases with no imposition (la ilzam), such as reports about agency (wakalah), mudarabah, or sending gifts; these will be discussed further.

Key Terms
الزام محض (ilzam mahd): Pure imposition of liability on someone, e.g., debt, sale, pledge, usurpation.
ولاية (wilayah): Legal capacity to testify, which includes freedom (hurriyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a report about a debt (right of a servant), what additional condition is required beyond the four general conditions?
A) The reporter must be a male.
B) The reporter must be two and use the word 'Ashhadu'.
C) The reporter must be a scholar.
D) The report must be from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
For khabar al-wahid to establish a binding right with liability, it must meet all testimony conditions: two narrators, wording of shahada, and freedom.

Accepting Reports in Non-Compulsory Matters
Ruling on accepting reports without compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that only tamyiz is required for accepting reports in non-compulsory matters and apply this rule to agency, partnership, and gifts.

Core Idea
Reports with no compulsion require only a discerning reporter, not an upright one.

When a report imposes no obligation on the recipient, such as being informed of a gift or agency, the Hanafi school sets minimal conditions for its acceptance. This lesson explains the requirement of tamyiz (discernment) as the sole condition, supported by Prophetic practice and practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize reports about agency, partnership, and gifts as having no ilzam (compulsion) on the recipient. The recipient can accept or reject without consequence.
2
State the condition
The reporter must be mumayyiz (discerning), regardless of age, gender, religion, or moral character. Tamyiz is the basic ability to understand and convey the message.
3
Justify with dalil
The Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted gift reports from both righteous and sinful, showing uprightness is not required. This is a Sunnah ahad dalil.
Refer to the Arabic passage: وَالنَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السلام كَانَ يَقْبَلُ خَيْرَ الْهَدَيَةِ مَنِ البَرِ وَالْفَاجِرِ
4
Apply to examples
If a child informs you of a partnership, accept it. If a known sinner brings a gift, accept it. The condition is tamyiz; any discerning person qualifies.

ونحوها بأنْ يَقُولَ وَكُلكَ فُلانٌ أَوْ صَارَبَكَ فِي هَذَا أَوْ أَهْدَ إِلَيْكَ هذا الشيء هدية فَإِنَّهُ لَا الْرَّامَ فِيْهِ عَلَى أَحَدٍ تِلْ يَخْتَارُ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَقْبَلَ الوِكَالَةَ وَالْمُصَارَبَةَ وَالْهَدْيَةَ وَبَيْنَ أَن لا يَقْبَلَ يَثْبُتُ بِأَخْبَارِ الأَحَادِ بِشَرْطِ المِيْنِ دُونَ الْعَدَالَةِ يَعْنِي بِشَرْطِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُكْبِرُ مُميّرًا صَبيًا كَانَ أَوْ بَالِفًا حُرًّا كَانَ أَوْ عَبْدًا مُسْلِمًا كَانَ أَوْ كَافِرًا عادِلاً كَانَ أوْ فَاسِقًا فَيَجودُ لِمَنْ أَخْبَرَهُ بِالْوِكَالَةِ وَالْمُصَارَبَةِ أَنْ يَتَصرِف فِيهِ وَيُبَاشِرُهُ لأَن الإِنْسانَ قَلْمًا يَجِدُ رَجُلاً مُسْتَجْمعًا للشرَائِطِ يَبْعَثُهُ عَلَى وَكَيْلِهِ. لَوْ غُلامِهِ  ِبالْخَبَرِ فَلَوْ شَرِطَت فيه الشروط لتَعَلتْ الْمَصَالِحُ فِي الْعَالَمِ وَلَان الْخَيْرَ غَيْرُ مُلْزِمٌ فِي الْوَاقِعِ فَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ فِيْهِ شَرَائِط الإلزام وَالنَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السلام كَانَ يَقْبَلُ خَيْرَ الْهَدَيَةِ مَنِ البَرِ وَالْفَاجِرِ وَأَنْ كَانَ فِيهِ الْوَامِ مَنْ وَجْهِ دُونَ وَجْهِ كَخَيْرٍ عَزْلِ الْوَكِيلِ وَحِجْرِ الْمَادُونِ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّ الْمُوَكَّلَ وَالْمَوْلَىٰ يَتَصَرْفُ فِي حَى نَفْسِهِ بِالْعَزْلِ وَالْحِجْرِ كَمَا يَتَصَرْفُ بِالتَّوْكِيلِ وَالاِذْنِ فَلَا الْرَامَ فِيْهِ أَصْلاً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّ التَّصَرُّفَ يَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الْوَكِيلِ وَالْعَبْدِ بَعْدَ الْعَدْلِ وَالْحَجْرِ وَتَلْرَمِة الْعَهْدَةُ فِي ذلِكَ فَفِيْهِ الْرَام ضَرَرْ عَلَى الْوَكِيْلِ وَالْعَبْدِ فَلِهَذَا يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ أَحَدٌ شطْرَى الشَّهَادَةِ عِنْدَ أبَى حَنِيفَةَ يَعْنِي الْعَدَدَ وَالْعَدَالَة أى لابد أن يَكُونَ الْمُكْبَرُ اثْنَيْنِ أَوْ وَاحِدًا عَدْلاً رِعَايَةً لِشِبْهِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ الْرَامًا مَحْضًا فِيهِ كِلاَهُمَا وَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ الْزَامًا أصلاً ما شرِطَ فِيهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْهُمَا فَوَفْرْنَا حَظًّا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ فِيهِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لا يَشْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ شَيْءٌ بَلْ يَثْبُ الْحِجَرُ وَالْعَزْلِ يَخَيْرِ كُلِّ مُمَيْرٍ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الْمُكْبِرُ فَضَوْلِيًا فَإِنْ كَانَ وَكِيْلاً أَوْ رَسُولاً مِنَ الْمُؤكِّلِ وَالْمَوْلَى لَمْ تُشْتَرِطِ الْعَدَالَةُ وَالْعَدَدْ اِثْفَاقًا لَأَنْ عِبَارَةَ الْوَكِيلِ وَالرَّسُوْلِ كَعِبَارَةِ الْمُؤكُل وَالْمُرْسَلِ اوان كان لا الزام فيه اصلاً إذا محل حقوق العباد کی اس قسم میں سے ہے جس میں سرے سے کوئی الزام نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کسی کے وکیل ہونے کی خبر ۔ اور شریک مال ہونے کی خبر اور ہدیہ میں قاصد ہونے کی خبر اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے چیزوں کی خبریں۔ مثلاً کوئی کہے تم کو فلاں نے وکیل بنایا ہے۔ بالا نے تجھ کو اس چیز میں شریک بنالیا ہے۔ یا فلاں نے یہ چیز تمہیں ہدیہ میں دی ہے۔ ان مثالوں میں کسی پر الزام نہیں ہے بلکہ جسے خبر دی گئی ہے وہ چاہے اس ہدیہ، وکالت، شرکت کو قبول کرنے یا قبول نہ کرے اس کو دونوں باتوں کا اختیار ہے۔ ويُثبت بأخبار الآحاد : تو یہ اخبار آحاد سے ثابت ہو گا، بشرطیکہ خبر دینے والا صاحب تمیز ہو۔ نہ اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ مخیر صاحب عدالت ہو۔ یعنی شرط یہ ہے کہ مخیر امتیاز پیدا کرانے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو، جو کہ دہ میں (بچہ) ہو یا بالغ یا آزادی غلام اور مسلمان ہویا کافر عادل ہو یا ناسق ہو۔ پس جس کو خبر دی گئی ہے اس کے لئے وکالت کرنا، مال میں شرکت کرنا اور اس میں تصرف کرنا اور اس کے مطابق عمل درآمد کر ناصریح ہے، کیونکہ انسان بہت ہی کم ایسا آدمی پائے گا جو تمام صفات کا جامع ہو جسے دور کیل کے پاس بھیجے لہذا اگر مذکورہ شرطیں یہاں بھی ضروری قرار دی جائیں گی تو عالم سے مصالح معطل ہو کر رہ جائیں گی۔ نیز دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ نفس خبر کسی چیز کو واقع میں لازم نہیں کرتی۔ لہذا الزام کی شرائط کا اس میں کیسے اعتبار کیا جائے گا نیز نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہدیہ کی خبر صالح وفاجر ہر ایک کی قبول فرما لیتے تھے۔ وإن كان فيه انا الح اگر محل خیر ایسی ہو کہ جس میں من وجه الزام ہو اور من وجه الزام نہ ہو جیسے وکیل کے معزول کرنے کی خبر اور عمید مازون کو مجور قرار دیئے جانے کی خبر ۔ تو اس حیثیت سے کہ مؤکل اور مولی اپنے اپنے حقوق میں معد دل کرنے یا مجبور کرنے کا تصرف کرتے ہیں جس طرح وہ وکیل بنانے اور غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دینے کا تصرف کرتے ہیں، اور اس میں کوئی الزام نہیں ہے اور دوسری حیثیت یہ ہے کہ تصرف کا تعلق وکیل سے اور اجازت کے ختم کرنے کا تعلق فلام سے ہے اور اس میں ایک قسم کی ذمہ داری ماکہ ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں وکیل اور عید پر الزام نقصان پایا جاتا ہے۔ فَلِهَذَا يُشْتَرَطَ فِيْهِ أَحَدٌ شطري الشهادة : تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک (نصاب) شہادت کا نصف شرط ہو گا۔ یعنی خواہ عد د پایا جائے۔ یا عدالت پائی جائے یعنی مخبر کا رو ہونا ضروری ہے یا ایک گواہ ہو عادل ہو، دونوں جانب کا لحاظ ر کھتے ہوئے یہ حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ محل خبر اگر الزام محض ہو تو اس میں دونوں چیزیں شرط ہیں۔ عدد بھی اور عدالت بھی اور اگر بالکل الزام نہ ہو تو ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے کسی شرط کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فَوَفِّرْنَا حَظًّا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنَ لہذا اس میں ہم نے دونوں جانب کی پوری رعایت رکھی ہے۔ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يَسْتَرِطُ فيه شي :- اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس میں کوئی شرط ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ مجور نے معزول کرنے کی خبر ہر تمیز رکھنے والے آدمی کی مقبول ہوگی۔ یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جب مخبر فضولی ہو۔ لیکن اگر خبر دینے والا وکیل ہو یا موکل اور مولی کا بھیجا ہوا قاصد ہو ۔ تو بالاتفاق عدد اور عدالت کی کوئی شرط نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل اور قاصد کا بیان ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ مؤکل اور مولی یا بھیجنے والے کا بیان ہوتا ہے۔
And similar to them, such as someone saying, 'So-and-so appointed you as agent,' or 'He made you a partner in this,' or 'He gave this thing to you as a gift.' There is no compulsion in it upon anyone; rather, he chooses between accepting the agency, partnership, and gift, and not accepting. It is established by solitary reports on condition of discernment without uprightness, meaning on condition that the informer is discerning, whether he is a child or adult, free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, upright or sinful. So the one informed about agency or partnership is permitted to act and undertake it, because a person rarely finds a man who combines all the conditions to send as his agent. If conditions were required in it, then interests in the world would be nullified, and because the report does not impose an obligation in reality, so the conditions of obligation are not considered in it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to accept the report of a gift from the righteous and the sinful. And if there is in it compulsion from one aspect and not from another, like news of the dismissal of an agent and the interdiction of a permitted slave—from the aspect that the principal and master dispose of their own right by dismissal and interdiction just as they dispose by appointment and permission, so there is no compulsion in it at all; and from the aspect that the disposal is restricted to the agent and slave after dismissal and interdiction, and liability attaches in that, so in it there is compulsion and harm upon the agent and slave. Therefore, one of the two halves of testimony is required in it according to Abu Hanifa, meaning number and uprightness; i.e., the informer must be two or one upright, observing both aspects. Because if it were pure compulsion, both would be required; if there were no compulsion at all, nothing would be required. So we have given a share from both aspects in it. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is required in it; rather, interdiction and dismissal are established by the report of every discerning person. This is when the informer is a third party. But if the informer is an agent or messenger from the principal and master, then uprightness and number are not required by consensus, because the expression of the agent and messenger is like the expression of the principal and sender. [Urdu commentary: If there is no compulsion at all... then the report is established by solitary reports provided the informer is discerning, not necessarily upright, due to necessity and the Prophet's practice... In cases of partial compulsion, Abu Hanifa requires one of the two halves of testimony, while the two companions require no condition. But if the informer is an agent or messenger, no condition at all by consensus.]
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for accepting reports (khabar) in matters that involve no compulsion, partial compulsion, or full compulsion, specifically in the context of agency (wakala), partnership (sharika), gifts (hadiya), and similar transactions. The author explains that when a report carries no obligation (la ilzam), such as informing someone that they have been appointed an agent or given a gift, the report is accepted from any discerning person (mumayyiz), regardless of age, status, religion, or moral character. This is based on practical necessity because finding a fully qualified person is difficult, and also on the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepting gifts from both righteous and sinful people. When the report carries partial compulsion (fih ilzam min wajh), such as news of an agent's dismissal or a slave's interdiction, Imam Abu Hanifa requires that the reporter fulfill one of the two halves of testimony (shahada): either two reporters, or one reporter who is upright ('adl). This balances the presence and absence of compulsion. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no condition is needed; any discerning person suffices. However, all agree that if the reporter is the agent or messenger himself, no conditions apply, as his statement is equivalent to the principal's.

Key Terms
الْخَبَر (al-khabar): A report or piece of news transmitted by one or more persons.
الإِلْزَام (al-ilzam): The quality of a report that imposes an obligation or harm upon the recipient.
التَّمْيِيز (al-tamyiz): The capacity to discern and understand the meaning of what is being reported; a basic condition for the reporter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for accepting a report about a gift?
A) The reporter must be two upright witnesses.
B) The reporter must be a single upright person.
C) The reporter must be a discerning person, regardless of uprightness.
D) The reporter must be a free adult Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In non-compulsory matters, only tamyiz is required; uprightness is not a condition.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Reports with Partial Compulsion: The Hanafi Dispute on Dismissal and Interdiction
Ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on accepting reports of dismissal/interdiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on accepting reports of dismissal and interdiction, and identify the consensus exception for agents and messengers.

Core Idea
Reports with partial compulsion require one of the two halves of testimony according to Abu Hanifa, but nothing according to Sahibayn; all agree no conditions when the reporter is the agent.

When a report carries compulsion from one angle but not another—such as news of an agent's dismissal—the Hanafi masters differ on the required reporter qualifications. Imam Abu Hanifa balances the two aspects by requiring one half of testimony, while his disciples hold that no extra conditions are needed. This lesson also covers the universal exception for reports given by the agent or messenger himself.

Guided Path
1
Define partial compulsion
Consider the report of an agent's dismissal: from the principal's side, it is his own right (no compulsion on him); from the agent's side, it imposes harm (compulsion).
The passage describes this as 'min wajh wa min wajh' (from one aspect and another).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa requires one of the two halves of testimony (shahada): either two male reporters, or one reporter who is 'adl (upright).
This balances the two extremes: full compulsion (both halves) and no compulsion (nothing).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require no additional conditions; any discerning person's report is accepted.
They consider the element of compulsion insignificant because the principal is acting in his own right.
4
Identify the consensus exception
All agree that if the reporter is the agent or messenger himself, no condition of number or uprightness is needed.
Because the agent's statement is equivalent to the principal's.
5
Derive practical outcome
In practice, according to Abu Hanifa, a single upright informer suffices for dismissal/interdiction; according to Sahibayn, any discerning person (even a child) suffices.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school often follows Abu Hanifa's precaution.

فَلِهَذَا يُشْتَرَطَ فِيْهِ أَحَدٌ شطري الشهادة : تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک (نصاب) شہادت کا نصف شرط ہو گا۔ یعنی خواہ عد د پایا جائے۔ یا عدالت پائی جائے یعنی مخبر کا رو ہونا ضروری ہے یا ایک گواہ ہو عادل ہو، دونوں جانب کا لحاظ ر کھتے ہوئے یہ حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ محل خبر اگر الزام محض ہو تو اس میں دونوں چیزیں شرط ہیں۔ عدد بھی اور عدالت بھی اور اگر بالکل الزام نہ ہو تو ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے کسی شرط کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فَوَفِّرْنَا حَظًّا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنَ لہذا اس میں ہم نے دونوں جانب کی پوری رعایت رکھی ہے۔ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يَسْتَرِطُ فيه شي :- اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس میں کوئی شرط ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ مجور نے معزول کرنے کی خبر ہر تمیز رکھنے والے آدمی کی مقبول ہوگی۔ یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جب مخبر فضولی ہو۔ لیکن اگر خبر دینے والا وکیل ہو یا موکل اور مولی کا بھیجا ہوا قاصد ہو ۔ تو بالاتفاق عدد اور عدالت کی کوئی شرط نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل اور قاصد کا بیان ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ مؤکل اور مولی یا بھیجنے والے کا بیان ہوتا ہے۔
And similar to them, such as someone saying, 'So-and-so appointed you as agent,' or 'He made you a partner in this,' or 'He gave this thing to you as a gift.' There is no compulsion in it upon anyone; rather, he chooses between accepting the agency, partnership, and gift, and not accepting. It is established by solitary reports on condition of discernment without uprightness, meaning on condition that the informer is discerning, whether he is a child or adult, free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, upright or sinful. So the one informed about agency or partnership is permitted to act and undertake it, because a person rarely finds a man who combines all the conditions to send as his agent. If conditions were required in it, then interests in the world would be nullified, and because the report does not impose an obligation in reality, so the conditions of obligation are not considered in it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to accept the report of a gift from the righteous and the sinful. And if there is in it compulsion from one aspect and not from another, like news of the dismissal of an agent and the interdiction of a permitted slave—from the aspect that the principal and master dispose of their own right by dismissal and interdiction just as they dispose by appointment and permission, so there is no compulsion in it at all; and from the aspect that the disposal is restricted to the agent and slave after dismissal and interdiction, and liability attaches in that, so in it there is compulsion and harm upon the agent and slave. Therefore, one of the two halves of testimony is required in it according to Abu Hanifa, meaning number and uprightness; i.e., the informer must be two or one upright, observing both aspects. Because if it were pure compulsion, both would be required; if there were no compulsion at all, nothing would be required. So we have given a share from both aspects in it. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is required in it; rather, interdiction and dismissal are established by the report of every discerning person. This is when the informer is a third party. But if the informer is an agent or messenger from the principal and master, then uprightness and number are not required by consensus, because the expression of the agent and messenger is like the expression of the principal and sender. [Urdu commentary: If there is no compulsion at all... then the report is established by solitary reports provided the informer is discerning, not necessarily upright, due to necessity and the Prophet's practice... In cases of partial compulsion, Abu Hanifa requires one of the two halves of testimony, while the two companions require no condition. But if the informer is an agent or messenger, no condition at all by consensus.]
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for accepting reports (khabar) in matters that involve no compulsion, partial compulsion, or full compulsion, specifically in the context of agency (wakala), partnership (sharika), gifts (hadiya), and similar transactions. The author explains that when a report carries no obligation (la ilzam), such as informing someone that they have been appointed an agent or given a gift, the report is accepted from any discerning person (mumayyiz), regardless of age, status, religion, or moral character. This is based on practical necessity because finding a fully qualified person is difficult, and also on the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepting gifts from both righteous and sinful people. When the report carries partial compulsion (fih ilzam min wajh), such as news of an agent's dismissal or a slave's interdiction, Imam Abu Hanifa requires that the reporter fulfill one of the two halves of testimony (shahada): either two reporters, or one reporter who is upright ('adl). This balances the presence and absence of compulsion. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no condition is needed; any discerning person suffices. However, all agree that if the reporter is the agent or messenger himself, no conditions apply, as his statement is equivalent to the principal's.

Key Terms
الْخَبَر (al-khabar): A report transmitted by one or more persons.
الإِلْزَام (al-ilzam): The compulsion or obligation imposed by a report.
شُطْرَا الشَّهَادَةِ (shutra al-shahada): The two halves of testimony: number ('adad) and uprightness ('adala).
التَّمْيِيز (al-tamyiz): Discernment, the basic capacity to understand and convey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required for accepting a report about the dismissal of an agent when the reporter is a third party?
A) The reporter must be two upright men.
B) The reporter must be either two persons or one upright person.
C) The reporter must be at least one discerning person regardless of uprightness.
D) The reporter must be a free adult Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In reports with partial compulsion, Abu Hanifa requires one half of testimony, while the Sahibayn require only tamyiz; all agree no conditions when the informer is the agent.

Condition of Ability: Belief vs Action
Stating the Hanafi condition of ability to believe, not ability to act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of ability (tamakkun) for taklif and distinguish it from the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
For Hanafi taklif, only ability to believe is required; ability to act is not a condition.

This passage clarifies a fundamental usul principle: what minimal capacity must a person have before being held accountable for a divine command? The Hanafi school distinguishes sharply between belief and action, requiring only the former for obligation. The Mu'tazila counter that ability to act is necessary, but Hanafis respond with a prophetic example and a logical argument that belief is the origin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What condition is being discussed? The passage states that sharṭ al-tamakkun (condition of ability) is required for taklif.
2
Locate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi view is that only ability to believe (i'tiqad) is required, not ability to act.
The text says: 'اور اعتقاد قلبی کی قدرت ہمارے نزدیک نفع کی شرط ہے عمل پر قدرت حاصل ہونا شرط نہیں ہے'
3
Contrast with Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila require ability to act because they consider action the origin of taklif.
The passage says: 'خلافا للمعتزلة معتزلہ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کیوں کہ ان کے نزدیک فعل پر قدرت رکھنا ضروری ہے'
4
Analyze the proof
The Hanafi proof is from the Prophet (saw) and the ummah: the ummah was given respite only for belief, not action, and the Prophet's belief represented the ummah.
Key evidence: 'صرف نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اس کے اعتقاد پر قدرت کی مہلت پاسکے تھے'
5
Understand the logical argument
Belief is the origin (asl), action is subsidiary (tab'). When the origin is found, the subsidiary is not needed.
The text states: 'لِمَا أَنَّ حُكْمَة بَيَانُ الْمُدَّةِ لِعَمَلِ القَلْبِ عِنْدَنَا أصلاً وَلِعَمَلِ الْبَدَنِ تَبْعًا فَإِذَا وُجِدَ الأصلُ لأَيَحْتَاجُ إلى وُجُوْدِ التَّبْعِ'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرطُ التَّعَكُن مِنْ عَقْدِ المقلب [؟] اور اعتقاد قلبی کی قدرت ہمارے نزدیک نفع کی شرط ہے عمل پر قدرت حاصل ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکلف بندوں کے پاس حکم پہونچنے کے بعد اتنا قلیل زمانہ ضرور ملنا چاہیئے کہ وہ اس حکم کے اعتقاد رکھنے کی قدرت رکھ سکتا ہو تا کہ اس کے بعد نفع کو قبول کرے اپنے طویل فاصلہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس حکم پر عمل کرنے کی قدرت رکھتا ہو خلافا للمعتزلة معتزلہ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کیوں کہ ان کے نزدیک فعل پر قدرت رکھنا ضروری ہے تا کہ وہ صبح کو قبول کر سکے ۔ ہماری دلیل جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور امت کوئی بھی فعل پر قدرت کی مہلت نہیں پاسکی۔ اور صرف نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اس کے اعتقاد پر قدرت کی مہلت پاسکے تھے اور چوں کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سب کے مقتداء اور امام ہیں اسلئے آپ کا اعتقاد پوری امت کا اعتقاد تصور کر لیا گیا گویا سب نے اس کے حق ہونے کا اعتقاد کر لیا اس کے بعد اس حکم کو منسوخ کر دیا گیا۔
لِمَا أَنَّ حُكْمَة بَيَانُ الْمُدَّةِ لِعَمَلِ القَلْبِ عِنْدَنَا أصلاً وَلِعَمَلِ الْبَدَنِ تَبْعًا فَإِذَا وُجِدَ الأصلُ لأَيَحْتَاجُ إلى وُجُوْدِ التَّبْعِ البَتْه وَعِنْدَهُمْ هُوَ بَيَانَ مُدَّةِ الْعَمَلِ بِالْبَدَنِ فَلاَ بُدَّ أنْ يَتَمَكَّنَ مِنَ الْفِعْلِ الْبَتَّةَ
کیوں کہ ہمارے نزدیک اعتقاد قلبی ترجمه تشریح کی بات کا بیان در اصل شیخ ہے اور عمل بدنی کی عدت کا بیان اس سے جھا ہوا کرتا ہے لہذا جب مدت دراصل کس سے بچا ہو اصل پا لیا گیا تو تبع کے پائے جانے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں باقی رہی۔
وعندهم بيان مدة العمل بالبدن : اور معتزلہ کے نزدیک چوں کہ بدن سے عمل کی مدت کے بیان کے لئے شیخ ہے لہذا اس حکم کے مطابق عمل کرنے کی مہلت پر قدرت کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
The condition of ability from the belief of the heart. And the ability of belief is in our view a condition for profit; the acquisition of ability to act is not a condition. Meaning that after the command reaches the obligated persons, there must be such a short time that they are able to hold belief in that command, so that after that they may accept it; there is no need for a long interval that they are able to act on that command, contrary to the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazila have disagreement in this, because in their view ability to act is necessary so that they can accept it in the morning. Our proof: the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the ummah could not obtain a respite for ability to act. Only the Prophet (peace be upon him) could obtain a respite for ability to believe. And since the Prophet (peace be upon him) is the leader and imam of all, his belief was considered the belief of the whole ummah, as if all believed in its truth. After that, this ruling was abrogated. Because the wisdom of stating the period for the action of the heart is in our view the origin, and for the action of the body is subsidiary. So when the origin is found, there is no need at all for the existence of the subsidiary. In their view, it is a statement of the period for action by the body, so it is absolutely necessary to be able to perform the action. Because in our view, the statement of the period for belief is the origin, and the statement of the period for bodily action is subsidiary to it. Therefore, when the origin is found, there remains no need for the existence of the subsidiary. According to them: the statement of the period for action by the body. And according to the Mu'tazila, since the period for action by the body is the origin for them, it is necessary to have the ability to act in accordance with this ruling.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on the matn regarding the condition of ability (tamakkun) required for taklif. The Hanafi position is that only the ability to believe (i'tiqad) is required, not the ability to act. The author presents the proof from the Prophet (saw) and the ummah, where the ummah was not given time to act but only to believe, and the Prophet's belief represented the ummah's belief. The Mu'tazila require ability to act, which the Hanafis reject by pointing to the original nature of belief over action. The passage then contrasts the Hanafi view that the period for belief is primary and bodily action subsidiary, so when the origin is present, the subsidiary is not needed. The Mu'tazila make bodily action the origin, hence requiring action ability.

Key Terms
شرط التمكن (sharṭ al-tamakkun): The condition of ability: the minimal capacity required for the obligated person to comply with a divine command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, what is the condition (sharṭ) for the obligation (taklif) to apply to a person upon receiving a command?
A) Ability to act on the command in the immediate future
B) Ability to believe in the command
C) Ability to both believe and act
D) Ability to perform the action at any time

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the minimal condition for taklif is the capacity to believe, not the capacity to act.
