Classification of the Prophet's Actions and the Ruling on Following Them
Classifying the Prophet's actions and rulings on following them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of the Prophet's actions, define a slip (zallah), and apply the Hanafi rule for following actions of unknown basis.

Core Idea
The Prophet's actions are followed according to their rank; unknown actions are considered permissible because he never did haram.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text addresses a fundamental question: how are we to follow the actions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)? The author first categorizes his actions, excluding slips, into four ranks. Then he presents different scholarly views on what to do when the basis of an action is unknown, and finally adopts the Hanafi position that unknown actions are considered permissible (mubah). Understanding this classification is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Prophet's example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of the Prophet's actions
The passage states there are four: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard. Note that slips are excluded.
2
Define 'zallah' (slip) and understand its exception
A slip is an unintentional prohibited act not persisted in. It is not meant for emulation.
3
Understand the technical meaning of 'wajib' in usul
The passage explains that for the Prophet, actions are proven by definitive evidence, so the term 'wajib' (which requires zanni evidence) does not apply to him in the technical sense.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf regarding actions of unknown basis
Three views: tawaqquf, obligation of following, and Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Apply the correct (sahih) view: if basis unknown, assume mubah
The author states al-sahih: follow if basis known; if unknown, assume permissibility because the Prophet never did haram or makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث افعال النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم
فصل افعال النبى سوائے الگزشوں کے - فصل في كريم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال کے سوائے لغزشوں کے چار قسمیں ہیں۔ مباح، مستحب ، واجب اور فرض لغزشوں کا استثنا اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ یہ باب ان افعال کے بیان کا ہے جو امت کی اقتداء کی غرض سے صادر ہوئے اور لغزشیں وہ افعال نہیں کہ ان کی اقتداء کی جائے اور لغزش سے مراد اس جگہ یہ ہے کہ کوئی ممنوع شرعی صادر ہو جائے فعل مباح کے ارادہ ہے (یعنی ارتکاب سے پہلے اس فعل ممنوع کے کرنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو اور صادر ہونے کے بعد اس پر قائم نہ رہے جیسے کہ کوئی شخص راستہ میں چلتے ہوئے جھکا اور جھکتے ہی بے ارادہ میں گر پڑا اور گرتے ہی فورا کھڑا ہو گیا تو اس شخص کا ارادہ کرنے کا نہ تھا اور کرنے کے بعد وہ قرار نہیں رہا بلکہ فورا کھڑا ہو گیا جس طرح حضرت سیدنا حضرت موسی علیہ الاسلام کا قصد قبطی کو مارنے سے تادیب تھا اس کے ہلاک کرنے کا نہ تھا اور موسی علیہ السلام اس پر قائم نہ رہے بلکہ فورا نادم ہوئے اور فرمایا " هذا من عمل الشيطان یہ شیطان کا کا ر توت ہے۔ پر نہ رہے وَلَكِنْ هَذَا التَّقْسيمُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا - لیکن مذکور تقسیم ہمارے لحاظ سے ہے ورنہ کوئی چیز جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لحاظ سے کوئی عمل اصطلاحی واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اصطلاح میں واجب اس حکم کو کہتے ہیں جو ایسی حدیث سے ثابت ہو جس کے ثبوت میں شبہ ہو۔ اور آپ کے حق میں تمام دلیل قطعی ہیں پھر علماء نے ان افعال کی اقتداء کے بارے میں باہم اختلاف کیا ہے جو افعال آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے نہ سہوا صادر ہوئے نہ وہ افعال طبیعی تھے اور نہ آپ کے ساتھ مخصوص تھے تو بعض نے کہا کہ ایسے افعال میں توقف واجب ہے یہاں تک یہ ظاہر ہو جائے کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کس وجہ سے یہ افعال کئے ہیں اباحت کی وجہ سے یا ندب کی وجہ سے یا وجوب کی وجہ سے۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ آپ کی اتباع واجب ہے جب تک منع پر کوئی دلیل نہ قائم ہو جائے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس فعل میں اباحت کا عقیدہ رکھے کیونکہ یہ یقینی ہے لیکن جب وجوب یا استحباب کی دلیل مل جائے تو ان مذکوروں کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ وَالْمُصَنِّفُ تَرَكَ هَذَا كُلَّهُ وَبَيَّنَ مَا هُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَهُ فَقَالَ وَالصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا إِنَّ مَا عَلِمْنَاهُ مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَاقِعاً عَلَى جِهَةٍ مِنَ الْوُجُوبِ وَالنُّدْبِ أَوِ الْإِبَاحَةِ نَقْتَدِي بِهِ فِي إِيْقَاعِهِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْجِهَةِ حَتَّى يَقُومَ دَلِيلُ الْخُصُوصِ فَمَا كَانَ وَاجِبًا عَلَيْهِ يَكُونُ وَاجِبًا عَلَيْنَا وَمَا كَانَ مَنْدُوبًا عَلَيْهِ يَكُونُ مَنْدُوبًا عَلَيْنَا وَمَا كَانَ مُبَاحًا لَهُ يَكُونُ مُبَاحًا لَنَا وَمَا لَمْ نَعْلَمْ عَلَى أَيَّةِ جِهَةٍ فَعَلَهُ قُلْنَا فَعَلَهُ عَلَى أَدْنَى مَنَازِلِ أَفْعَالِهِ وَهُوَ الْإِبَاحَةُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ حَرَامًا أَوْ مَكْرُوهًا الْبَتَّةَ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُبَاحًا وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ تَقْسِيمِ السُّنَّةِ فِي حَقِّنَا شَرَعَ فِي تَقْسِيمِهَا فِي حَقِّهِ
Topic: Actions of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Section: The Prophet's actions except slips are of four types: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard. The exception of slips is because this chapter is about actions that occurred for the sake of the ummah's following, and slips are not actions to be followed. By 'slip' here is meant that a prohibited act occurs with the intent of a permissible act (i.e., before the commission, there was no intention to do the prohibited act, and after it occurs, he does not persist in it, like a person walking who stumbles and unintentionally falls, then immediately gets up; he had no intention to fall and did not persist. Similarly, Prophet Musa's intent in striking the Coptic was to discipline, not to kill, and he did not persist but immediately regretted and said 'This is from the work of Satan'). But this classification is relative to us; otherwise, nothing from the Prophet's perspective is technically wajib, because technically wajib is a ruling proven by a hadith of doubtful proof, whereas all evidences for him are definitive. Then scholars differed about following these actions that occurred from him not by forgetfulness, were not natural actions, and were not specific to him. Some said that in such actions, stopping (tawaqquf) is obligatory until it becomes clear why he did them – for permissibility, recommendation, or obligation. Others said that following him is obligatory until evidence of prohibition is established. Imam Abu Hanifa's view is to hold the belief of permissibility in that action because it is certain, but when evidence of obligation or recommendation appears, those (other) considerations will be accepted. The author left all this and stated what is preferred according to him, so he said: 'The correct view with us is that what we know from his actions, peace be upon him, occurring on a basis of obligation, recommendation, or permissibility, we follow him in performing it on that basis until evidence of specificity appears. So what was obligatory upon him is obligatory upon us, what was recommended upon him is recommended upon us, and what was permissible for him is permissible for us. And what we do not know on which basis he did it, we say he did it on the lowest of the ranks of his actions, which is permissibility, because he never did anything forbidden or disliked, so it must be permissible.' When he finished the classification of the Sunnah regarding us, he began its classification regarding him.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how to treat the Prophet's actions in terms of following. The author first outlines the four categories of his actions (mubah, mustahabb, wajib, fard), excluding slips (zallat) because they are not meant for emulation. A slip is defined as an unintentional prohibited act that is not persisted in. The classification (into these categories) is relative to the ummah; for the Prophet himself, the term 'wajib' technically does not apply because all his proofs are definitive, while 'wajib' in usul al-fiqh is defined as a ruling proven by a non-definitive (zanni) proof. The author then presents the ikhtilaf among scholars regarding following actions that are not forgetful, natural, or specific to him. Three positions: tawaqquf (wait until the intent becomes clear), obligation of following unless there is evidence of prohibition, and Imam Abu Hanifa's view (originally hold permissibility, but adjust if evidence of higher category arises). The author adopts the sahih view: if we know the category (wajib, mandub, mubah), we follow accordingly; if we do not know, we assume it is mubah because the Prophet never did haram or makruh. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الزلة (al-zallah): An unintentional prohibited act not persisted in, not meant for emulation
الواجب (al-wajib): In usul: a ruling proven by a non-definitive (zanni) proof; here noted that the Prophet's actions are proven by definitive proofs, so wajib in technical sense does not apply to him
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permissibility; the default rank of the Prophet's actions when the basis is unknown

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (al-sahih) in this passage, what is the ruling on a Prophet's action whose basis (wajib, mandub, mubah) is unknown?
A) It is obligatory to follow it as wajib.
B) It is considered mubah (permissible) because the Prophet never did haram.
C) One must stop (tawaqquf) until the basis is known.
D) It is recommended to follow it as mandub.

Key Takeaway
When the basis of a Prophet's action is unknown, the Hanafi school considers it permissible (mubah) to follow, as the Prophet never engaged in haram or makruh.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of Ijma' and Its Two Types
Defines ijma' and its two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ijma' as a Hanafi usul source, distinguish between azima (explicit) and rukhsa (silent consensus), and evaluate the Hanafi acceptance of ijma' suktuti by responding to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Ijma' is binding; its validity includes silent consent after adequate reflection time.

This lesson introduces one of the four primary sources of Islamic law: ijma' (consensus). The Hanafi school classifies ijma' into two types based on how the agreement is expressed. The passage defines ijma' linguistically and technically, then distinguishes azima (explicit agreement) from rukhsa (silent consensus). It also addresses a key intra-Usuli dispute: whether silence implies consent or may be due to fear. Understanding this classification and the reasoning behind it is essential for you to evaluate which consensus is binding in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the technical definition of ijma'
Identify the three essential elements: (1) agreement of the righteous mujtahids of the Ummah, (2) at a single time period, (3) on a religious matter (verbal or practical).
The definition excludes non-mujtahids and sinful persons.
2
Distinguish azima from rukhsa
The passage divides the 'essential element' of ijma' into two types: azima (determination) where all mujtahids explicitly agree, and rukhsa (concession) where some explicitly agree and others remain silent after a period for reflection.
Azima is further subdivided into verbal agreement (ijma' qawli) and practical agreement (ijma' fi'li).
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection to rukhsa
Imam al-Shafi'i rejects silent consensus (ijma' suktuti) because silence may stem from fear or intimidation, not consent. He cites the example of Ibn Abbas not objecting to Umar out of awe.
The period of reflection is given as three days or the duration of a scholarly gathering.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The passage refutes the Shafi'i argument by asserting the trustworthiness of the Companions, Umar's well-known openness to truth, and a hadith condemning silence in the face of truth. The Hanafi position is that after sufficient opportunity for objection, silence indicates approval.
This shows how Hanafi usul relies on customary practice and circumstantial evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو اجتماع کا بیان نور الانوار جلد سوم اجماع کے معنی لغت میں اتفاق کے ہیں اور اصطلاح شریعت میں آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی امت کے صلحاء و مجتہدین وقت کا ایک زمانہ میں کسی تولی یا فعلی امر میں اتفاق کر لینے کا نام اجماع ہے۔ وَرُكُنُ الإِجْمَاعِ نَوْعَانِ اجماع کی تحقیق کی دونو میں ہیں۔ (۱) عزیمت اور وہ یہ ہے کہ تمام مجتہدین یا تو ایسے الفاظ استعمال کریں جن سے ان کا اتفاق ثابت ہو تا ہو یعنی حمام کا کسی حکم پر اتفاق کر لینا۔ مثلا یوں کہیں اجمعنا على هذا ہم نے اس پر اتفاق کیا۔ اگر یہ مسئلہ الرسم تول اور بات ہے (جس میں زبان سے کہنا ضروری ہو ) شروعهم فِي الْفِعْلِ أَنْ كَانَ مِنْ بَابِهِ - اسی کام کو خود کرنے لگیں جب کہ امر فعلی ہو یعنی اس کام کا تعلق فعل سے ہو۔ جیسے تمام امام اجتہاد ( مجتہدین) مضاربت، مزارعت یا شرکت کے کام شروع کر دیں تو یہ ان حضرات کی طرف سے باختبار فعل اجتماع سمجھا جائے گا۔ (۳) ورخصته وهو أن يتكلم دوسری نوع رخصت ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ بعض اجتہاد کے قول یا فعل سے اتفاق محقق ہو اور بعض سے نہ ہو یعنی بعض مجتہدین قول فعل سے اتفاق کریں اور دوسرے بعض ان میں سے سکوت اختیار فرمائیں۔ اور غور و فکر کی مدت کے گذر جانے کے باوجود یہ حضرات کوئی تردید نہ فرمائیں اور غور دلگر) کی مدت تین دن ہے۔ یا مجلس علم ہے اسکو اجتماع مسکونی کہتے ہیں اور یہ اجتماع ہمارے یہاں مقبول ہے۔ وفيه خلات الشافعی اور اس میں امام شافعی خلاف کرتے ہیں۔ اس وجہ ہے کہ سکوت جس طرح موافقت کے لئے ہوا کرتا ہے اور ایسے ہی اہمیت اور خون کی بناء پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے صرف رضامندی پر دلالت نہیں کرتا ۔ جیسا کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ عول کے مسئلہ میں انہوں نے حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ سے اختلاف فرمایا تو ان سے پوچھا گیا کہ آپ نے حضرت عمر کے سامنے حجت (دلیل) کیوں نہ بیان فرمائی۔ تو فرمایا وہ بڑے بارعب تھے ان کا خوف مجھ پر طاری تھا اور ان کے کوڑے نے اظہار رائے سے مجھے باز رکھا۔ والجواب:۔ یہ بات کچھ سمجھ میں آنے والی نہیں ہے یہ جواب درست نہیں معلوم ہوتا ۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر فاروق رضی اللہ عنہ امر حق کو قبول کرلینے میں بہت زیادہ تابعدار تھے۔ دوسرے صحابہ کے مقابلہ ہیں حتی کہ زبان سے فرماتے رہتے کہ تمہارے اندر کوئی بھلائی نہیں ہے جب تک میں حق بات نہ سنوں (پھر سب سے بڑی بات یہ ہے) کہ امور دین میں حضرات صحابہ کو تاہی یا تقصیر کا نظن و گمان کیسے قائم کیا جا سکتا ہے اسی طرح حق بات کہتے پر خاموشی کا اختیار کرنا جب کہ وقت اور ضرورت اظہار و بیان کی ہو ۔ ( خاموشی سمجھ میں نہیں آتی ) حالانکہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے کہ حق بات کہتے سے خاموشی اختیار کرانے والا گونگا شیطان ہے۔
Ashraf al-Anwar Sharh Urdu: Section on Ijma'. Light of Lights Volume 3. The meaning of ijma' linguistically is agreement, and in the terminology of Shari'ah, it is the agreement of the righteous and mujtahids of the Ummah of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in a single time period on a matter verbal or practical. And the essential element of ijma' is of two types: (1) Azima: that all mujtahids either use words that prove their agreement, i.e., agreement on a ruling, e.g., they say 'We have agreed on this.' If the matter is verbal, speech is necessary. (2) They themselves begin the action if the matter is of an action type, i.e., if the matter relates to an action, like all the mujtahids begin the practices of mudaraba, muzara'a, or sharika, then this is considered ijma' by action from them. (3) Rukhsa: it is that some mujtahids agree by word or action and some others among them adopt silence, and after the period of reflection passes, they do not object, and the period of reflection is three days or the duration of the scholarly gathering. This is called suktuti ijma', and this type is accepted by us. And there is disagreement with Imam Shafi'i in this; he argues that silence could be due to agreement or also due to fear and intimidation, not necessarily indicating consent. As narrated from Hazrat Abdullah ibn Abbas (RA) regarding the issue of 'awl (inheritance increase), he differed with Hazrat Umar (RA), and he was asked why he did not present his proof before Umar. He said he was awe-inspiring and I feared him, and his whip prevented me from expressing my opinion. The response: This understanding is not correct because Hazrat Umar Farooq (RA) was very compliant in accepting the truth, more than other Companions. He used to say, 'There is no good in you unless I hear the truth.' Moreover, how can one suspect the Companions of negligence in religious matters? Likewise, remaining silent when there is need to speak is incomprehensible, especially since the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'One who remains silent from speaking the truth is a mute devil.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage defines ijma' (consensus) as a source of Islamic law. The author first gives the linguistic meaning (agreement) and the technical meaning (agreement of the righteous mujtahids of the Ummah at a specific time on a shar'i matter). He then explains that the rukn (essential element) of ijma' is of two main types: azima (determination) and rukhsa (concession). Under azima, there are two subtypes: (1) verbal agreement, where mujtahids explicitly state their consensus, and (2) practical agreement, where they all perform an action that indicates their consensus, e.g., engaging in mudaraba, muzara'a, or sharika. Rukhsa refers to silent consensus (ijma' suktuti), where some mujtahids explicitly agree and others remain silent after a period for reflection (three days or the end of the scholarly gathering). The Hanafis accept this type as binding. The author then presents the Shafi'i objection, citing the incident of Ibn Abbas not objecting to Umar out of fear. The Hanafi response refutes this by emphasizing Umar's known acceptance of truth and the general trustworthiness of the Companions, and quotes the hadith: 'Silence in the face of truth is a mute devil.'

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma'): Agreement of the righteous mujtahids of the Ummah at one time on a religious matter
عزیمت (azima): Determination; ijma' where all mujtahids explicitly agree verbally or by action
رخصت (rukhsa): Concession; ijma' where only some mujtahids explicitly agree and others remain silent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, which type of ijma' is formed when some mujtahids express agreement and others remain silent after the period of reflection?
A) Ijma' qawli (verbal)
B) Ijma' suktuti (silent)
C) Ijma' fi'li (practical)
D) Ijma' azima (determination)

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a binding source; its validity extends to silent consensus (ijma' suktuti) when qualified scholars have had adequate opportunity to object.

Proving a Condition (Wasf) through Hadith: Sa'imah for Zakat
Usul example: proving a wasf via hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Hanafi school proves a condition (wasf) for zakat from hadith and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument from the general Quranic verse.

Core Idea
A condition for zakat cannot be derived by qiyas; it must be established by explicit hadith.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi madhhab proves that livestock must be sa'imah (free-grazing) for zakat to be obligatory. The source is a classic usul al-fiqh example showing that certain descriptions (awsaf) are textual, not rational. Imam Malik disagrees, relying on the absolute wording of the Quran. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in distinguishing between a cause (sabab) and a condition (wasf) and in handling conflicting dalils.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab and the wasf
The sabab (cause) for zakat on livestock is ownership. The wasf (description) in dispute is that the animals must be sa'imah (grazing). Recognize that the wasf is an additional condition beyond the sabab.
Ownership is the mujib; sa'imah is a wasf that restricts the obligation.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'In five grazing camels, zakat is one goat.' Note the word 'sa'imah' which limits the obligation to grazing animals.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is accepted as proof for a wasf.
3
Understand the Maliki dalil
The Maliki school cites Quran 9:103: 'Take from their wealth charity...' The word 'amwal' (wealth) is general and includes all livestock, so zakat is due on all, grazing or not.
They treat the verse as absolute (mutlaq) without restriction.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith specifies (takhsis) the general verse. The specification is valid because the hadith is explicit about the condition.
This illustrates the usul principle: al-khass yuqaddam 'ala al-amm (the specific takes precedence over the general).
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says zakat is not wajib on non-sa'imah livestock; Maliki says zakat is wajib on all livestock.
This affects the obligation of many animal owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نور الانوار جلد سوم اشرف الافوار شرح اردو موجب ثابت کرنے کی مثال ہے کیونکہ جانوروں کا مالک ہونا زکوۃ کا اصلی موجب ہے۔ اور سائمہ ہونا (یعنی پورے سال یا سال کے اکثر حصہ میں جنگل میں چر پھر کر پیٹ بھر لینا، مالک کو گھر سے چارہ دینا نہ پڑتا ہو) ان جانوروں کا وصف ہے جس کا اثبات محض رائے و قیاس سے درست نہیں ہے۔ اس وصف کو ہم آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حدیث "فِي خَمْسِ مِنَ الإِبِلِ السَّائِمَةِ زَكَاةٌ" سے ثابت کرتے ہیں (پانچ اونٹوں میں جو کہ سائمہ ہوں ایک بکری زکوۃ میں واجب ہے) اور امام مالک کے نزدیک جانوروں کی زکوۃ کے وجوب میں سائمہ ہونے کی شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور وہ دلیل دیتے ہیں کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول "خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِمْ بِهَا" میں اموال مطلق ہے، سائمہ کی قید سے مقید نہیں ہے۔
It is an example of proving a cause (sabab). Because owning animals is the original cause for zakat. And being sa'imah (i.e., grazing in the desert for the full year or most of the year without the owner having to feed them at home) is a description of these animals, whose proof is not valid by mere opinion and analogy. We prove this description from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'In five grazing camels, zakat is one goat.' Imam Malik holds that the condition of being sa'imah is not necessary for zakat on animals. He argues that Allah's saying 'Take from their wealth charity to purify them and cleanse them thereby' is absolute regarding wealth, not restricted by the condition of grazing.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an example from usul al-fiqh showing how a legal cause (sabab) can be proven. Here, the cause for zakat on livestock is ownership, but the additional condition of the animals being sa'imah (grazing freely) is a description that cannot be established by mere reason or analogy. Instead, it is proven by the Prophet's hadith. The Hanafi position requires the animals to be sa'imah for zakat to be wajib, based on the hadith. Imam Malik disagrees, arguing that the Quranic verse is absolute and does not impose this condition. The passage illustrates the principle that certain details must be derived from textual sources, not from human reasoning.

Key Terms
موجب (mujib): The cause (sabab) that triggers a legal obligation.
سائمہ (sa'imah): Livestock that graze freely in the desert for most of the year without being fed by the owner.
تخصيص (takhsis): The act of specifying a general text by a specific text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakat is wajib on all livestock regardless of grazing.
B) Zakat is not wajib on non-sa'imah livestock.
C) Zakat is wajib only if the animals are male.
D) Zakat is wajib only on non-sa'imah animals.

Key Takeaway
The condition of sa'imah for zakat on livestock is proven by hadith, not by qiyas, and it takes precedence over the general Quranic verse in the Hanafi school.

Proving a Prohibition: The Case of Butayra Prayer
Example of proving a ruling (hukm) through hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of dalil naqli to derive a ruling from a hadith and evaluate a counter-argument from another textual evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's forbiddance of butayra proves its prohibition; a general permission does not override a specific prohibition.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school uses an explicit hadith to establish a legal ruling. The issue is whether praying only one rak'ah (al-butayra) is permitted. The Hanafis rely on the Prophet's prohibition, while al-Shafi'i cites a permission for witr. Through this example, you will learn the process of istinbat and the priority of specific texts over general ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Determine what 'al-butayra' refers to: a prayer consisting of a single rak'ah. Understand the issue: is it legislated or not?
The term 'butayra' literally means 'maimed' or 'cut off', indicating a truncated prayer.
2
Locate the Hanafi evidence
Find the textual proof used by Hanafis: the hadith 'Nahi 'an al-butayra' (He forbade al-butayra). This is a direct prohibition from the Prophet.
This hadith is classified as ahad (single narration) but is accepted as a valid proof.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the prohibition indicates the ruling. In Hanafi usul, a direct nahy (prohibition) from the Prophet indicates that the act is haram (or makruh tahriman) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
The principle 'al-nahy yufidu al-tahrim' is applied here.
4
Identify the opposing evidence
Consider the Shafi'i proof: the hadith 'Idha khashiya ahadukum al-subha falyutir bi-rak'ah' (When one of you fears dawn, let him perform witr with one rak'ah). This seems to permit one-rak'ah prayer.
Note the context: the permission is for witr when in fear of missing the dawn.
5
Apply the Hanafi rule of tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school prefers the prohibition over the permission. The prohibition is specific to one-rak'ah prayers, while the permission is a conditional exception. The specific and explicit prohibition takes precedence over a general or conditional permission.
This is a key tarjih principle: specific (khass) overrides general (amm).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْبُتَيْرَاءُ تَصْغِيرُ بَتْرَاءَ الَّتِي تَأَنَّثَ أَلْبَتْرَ، الْمُرَادُ بِهَا الصَّلَاةُ بِرَكْعَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَهُوَ مِثَالٌ لِلْحُكْمِ أَيْ إِثْبَاتُ أَنَّ هَذِهِ الصَّلَاةَ مَشْرُوعَةٌ أَمْ لَا، وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُتَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ بِالرَّأْيِ وَالْعِلَّةِ. وَإِنَّمَا أَثْبَتْنَا عَدَمَ مَشْرُوعِيَّتِهَا بِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَهَى عَنِ الْبُتَيْرَاءِ. وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُجَوِّزُهَا عَمَلًا بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: "إِذَا خَشِيَ أَحَدُكُمُ الصُّبْحَ فَلْيُوتِرْ بِرَكْعَةٍ".
Al-butayra is the diminutive of batra, which is the feminine of al-batr (maimed). It is intended to mean the prayer of one rak'ah. This is an example of a ruling (hukm): proving whether this prayer is legislated or not. It is not proper to speak about it with opinion and reasoning. Rather, we prove its non-legislation by the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade al-butayra. And al-Shafi'i permits it based on his saying: 'When one of you fears the dawn, let him perform witr with one rak'ah.'
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage provides an example of proving a legal ruling (hukm) from a textual source. The Hanafi position is that praying only one rak'ah (al-batira') is prohibited because the Prophet explicitly forbade it. The term 'batira' literally means 'cut off' and refers to a prayer truncated to a single rak'ah. Imam Shafi'i permits it based on the hadith allowing witr as one rak'ah if one fears dawn. The Hanafi response is that the forbiddance is specific and takes precedence. This illustrates the usul principle that rulings must be derived from explicit texts, not from analogy or personal opinion.

Key Terms
بتيراء (butayra): A prayer consisting of one rak'ah only, deemed impermissible by Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis prohibit the 'batira' prayer?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the Prophet forbade it
C) Because it is performed after Fajr
D) Because it requires too many bowings

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on butayra demonstrates that an explicit prohibition (nahy) takes precedence over a permission (rukhsah) when the prohibition is specific.

Proving the Description of a Ruling: Witr Prayer
Example of proving the description of a ruling through hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul methodology to determine the description (sifah) of a ruling by analyzing and weighing textual evidences, specifically for witr prayer.

Core Idea
The description of a ruling is determined solely by textual evidence, not by reason.

In this lesson, we explore how the Hanafi school proves the legal description (sifah) of a ruling. Using the example of witr prayer, we see how two competing hadith lead to different conclusions: Hanafis hold witr as wajib, Shafi'is as sunnah. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in deriving rulings from texts and evaluating ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its description
First, note the ruling in question: witr prayer. Its description (sifah) — whether wajib or sunnah — is what we aim to prove. The text states that this cannot be determined by opinion (ra'y).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer, and it is witr.' Focus on the word 'zada' (increase). In Hanafi usul, an increase upon the obligatory indicates that the added act carries the same obligation.
This is a form of istidlal through linguistic implication.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof is the Prophet's reply to the Bedouin: 'None except that you may perform voluntary prayers.' This suggests no additional obligatory prayers beyond the five daily prayers.
The Shafi'is interpret this as clear negation of obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the Bedouin hadith refers only to the five daily prayers, not excluding witr. The explicit 'increase' hadith takes precedence because it is specific to witr.
This is a form of tarjih (preference) based on specificity.
5
Determine the operative description
Based on the Hanafi tarjih, the mufta bihi position is that witr is wajib. The practical consequence: missed witr must be made up.
The Shafi'i ruling means qada is not required but recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصِفَةُ الْوِتْرِ مِثَالٌ لِإِثْبَاتِ صِفَةِ الْحُكْمِ، فَإِنَّ الْوِتْرَ حُكْمٌ مَشْرُوعٌ وَصِفَتُهُ كَوْنُهُ وَاجِبًا أَوْ سُنَّةً، وَلَا يُتَكَلَّمُ فِيهِ بِالرَّأْيِ. فَأَثْبَتْنَا وُجُوبَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: "إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى زَادَكُمْ صَلَاةً وَهِيَ الْوِتْرُ"، وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يَقُولُ إِنَّهَا سُنَّةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: "لَا إِلَّا أَنْ تَطَوَّعَ" حِينَ سَأَلَ الْأَعْرَابِيُّ بِقَوْلِهِ: هَلْ عَلَيَّ غَيْرُهُنَّ؟
And the description of witr is an example of proving the description of a ruling. For witr is a legislated ruling, and its description is whether it is obligatory or sunnah. It is not to be spoken about with opinion. So we proved its obligation by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer, and it is witr.' And al-Shafi'i says it is sunnah based on his saying: 'None except that you may perform voluntary prayers' when the Bedouin asked: 'Are there any other prayers upon me?'
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage demonstrates how to prove the nature (description) of a ruling. The Hanafi position holds witr prayer as wajib (obligatory), based on the hadith 'Inna Allah zada-kum salatan wa hiya al-witr'. The word 'zada' (increased) indicates that witr is an addition to the five daily prayers, and since the prophet said it is an 'increase from Allah', it implies obligation. Imam Shafi'i argues it is sunnah, citing the Prophet's reply to the Bedouin who asked about additional prayers: 'La illa an tatawwa'a' meaning no other obligatory prayers except voluntary ones. This illustrates the usul principle that the description (sifah) of a ruling—whether it is wajib, sunnah, etc.—must be derived from explicit texts.

Key Terms
وصف الحكم (wasf al-hukm): The description or attribute of a ruling, such as whether it is wajib, sunnah, etc.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib by Hanafis and sunnah by Shafi'is.
زاد (zada): To increase. In the hadith, it indicates addition to the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for the obligation of witr prayer?
A) The Prophet's hadith: 'Prayer is the key to Paradise'
B) The Prophet's hadith: 'Allah has increased for you a prayer, and it is witr'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Quranic verse: 'And perform the witr from the night'

Key Takeaway
The description (sifah) of a ruling must be derived from textual evidence; for witr, Hanafis rely on the 'increase' hadith to establish wujub.

The Five Types of Preventers (Mawani') in Hanafi Usul
Classification and correction of mawani' in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the five types of preventers (mawani') that block the establishment, completion, or binding of a ruling, and distinguish them from specification of the cause (takhsis al-illa).

Core Idea
Preventers block the ruling at cause, inception, completion, or binding—not mere condition absence.

This lesson unpacks a key classification in Hanafi usul: the five types of preventers (mawani') that obstruct a legal ruling. The passage not only lists them with examples but also corrects a common mistake—confusing the first two types with specification of the cause (takhsis al-illa). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying legal causes and their effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main classification
The text presents five types of preventers. List them: those blocking (1) establishment of the cause, (2) completion of the cause, (3) inception of the ruling, (4) completion of the ruling, and (5) bindingness of the ruling.
Each type targets a different stage of the legal process.
2
Understand the correction about takhsis al-illa
The author refutes Imam Fakhr al-Islam's claim that the first two types are cases of specification of the cause. The correct view: the cause itself is absent legally, so they are preventers, not specifications.
Specification requires the cause to exist but the ruling to be absent; here the cause is missing.
3
Analyze each type with its example
For each type, note the example from Hanafi fiqh: (1) selling a free person, (2) selling another's property without permission, (3) khiyar al-shart, (4) khiyar al-ru'yah, (5) khiyar al-'ayb.
Relate each example to the specific stage it blocks.
4
Relate to the legal cause (illa)
Determine how each preventer affects the cause: types 1-2 block the cause itself, types 3-5 block the ruling after the cause is present.
The first two preventers are absent cause; the rest are obstructed ruling.
5
Synthesize the practical impact
Each type leads to a different legal outcome: invalid contract, incomplete contract, non‑binding ownership, etc. Recognize these outcomes in real cases.
A mufti must identify the exact type to give correct fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقسام موانع
(۱) وہ مانع جو علت کے انعقاد کے لئے مانع ہو۔ جیسے آزاد (حر) کی بیع کیونکہ جب کسی نے حر (آزاد آدمی) کو فروخت کیا تو شرعا بیع منعقد نہ ہو گی۔ اگرچہ صورت پائی جاتی ہے۔
(۲) وَمَانِعٌ يَمْنَعُ تَمَامَ العلة: ایسا مانع جو اتمام علت کو روک دے جیسے بلا اجازت دوسرے کے غلام کی بیع۔ کیونکہ یہ بیع شرعا منعقد ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ محل بیع موجود ہے البتہ بیع تام نہیں ہوئی جب تک کہ مالک کی طرف سے اجازت نہ مل جائے۔ اور ان دونوں قسموں کو تخصیص فی العلة کے قبیل سے شمار کرنا تسارع ہے جو غلطی سے امام فخر الاسلام سے صادر ہو گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ تخصیص فی العلة نام ہے کہ حکم نہ پایا جائے باوجودیکہ علت پائی جاتی ہو۔ اور یہاں علت ہی پائی نہیں جاتی۔ البتہ بطور تاویل کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ علت صورةً پائی جاتی ہے مگر شرعاً اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے مصنف توضیح نے اس تعبیر کو چھوڑ کر جو صاحب المنار نے کی ہے ان الفاظ کو اختیار فرمایا ہے: مَا يُوجِبُ عَدَمَ الْحُكْمِ خَمْسَةٌ جو موانع حکم کو مرتب نہ ہونے کے موجب ہیں خواہ علت موجود ہو اور حکم ثابت نہ ہو یا علت ہی نہ پائی جائے۔ یہ تقسیم سب ہی کو شامل ہے۔ اس تعبیر پر اشکال وارد نہیں ہوتا۔
(۳) وَمَا يَمْنَعُ ابْتِدَاءَ الحكم: ایسا مانع جو از سر نو ثبوت حکم کو روک دے۔ جیسے بیع میں خیار شرط کا ہونا۔ اس صورت میں علت بتمامہا پائی جاتی ہے مگر حکم شروع نہیں ہوا، اور وہ ملک ہے خیار شرط کی وجہ سے۔
(۴) وَمَا يَمْنَعُ تَمَامَ الحُكْم: ایسا مانع جو اتمام حکم کو روک دے جیسے بیع میں خیار رویت کا حاصل ہونا کیونکہ یہ خیار ثبوت ملک کو نہیں روکتا لیکن اس خیار کے موجود ہوتے ہوئے ملک کا تمام حاصل نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے من له الخيار (جسے خیار حاصل ہے) کو حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ بغیر قضاء قاضی یا بغیر رضامندی بائع بیع کو توڑ دے۔
(۵) وَمَا يَمْنَعُ لُزُومَ الحكم: ایسا مانع لزوم حکم کو روک دے۔ جیسے خیار عیب کیونکہ یہ خیار ثبوت ملک کو نہیں روکتا اور ملک کے تمام ہونے کو روکتا ہے حتی کہ مشتری کو حق حاصل ہے کہ مبیع میں تصرف کر ڈالے۔ اور مشتری بیع کو بغیر قضاء قاضی یا بغیر رضامندی بائع نہیں کر سکتا۔ البتہ یہ خیار لزوم بیع کو روکتا ہے کیونکہ مشتری کو رد کرنے اور فسخ کرنے کا حق حاصل ہے۔ ان دونوں حقوق کے حاصل ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع لازم نہیں ہوئی۔
Sections of preventers: (1) The preventer that prevents the establishment of the cause. For example, the sale of a free person, because when someone sells a free man, the sale does not contract legally, even though the form is present. (2) And a preventer that prevents the completion of the cause: such as selling another's slave without permission. Because this sale is contracted legally since the object of sale is present, but it is not complete until permission from the owner is obtained. Counting these two types as specification of the cause (takhsis fi al-illa) is hasty, which occurred by mistake from Imam Fakhr al-Islam. Because specification of the cause means that the ruling is not found despite the cause being present. Here, the cause is not present. However, by way of interpretation, it can be said that the cause is present formally but legally it is not considered. For this reason, the author of al-Tawdih abandoned the expression used by the author of al-Manar and chose these words: 'What necessitates the absence of the ruling is five.' This prevents the ruling from being established, whether the cause is present and the ruling is not established, or the cause itself is not present. This division includes all. No objection arises on this expression. (3) And what prevents the beginning of the ruling: such as the presence of an option (khiyar al-shart) in a sale. In this case, the cause is fully present, but the ruling does not begin, and that is ownership due to the option. (4) And what prevents the completion of the ruling: such as khiyar al-ru'yah in a sale, because this option does not prevent the establishment of ownership, but with this option present, the completion of ownership is not attained. So the one who has the option has the right to cancel the sale without a judge's ruling or the seller's consent. (5) And what prevents the bindingness of the ruling: such as khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), because this option does not prevent the establishment of ownership and prevents its completion, so that the buyer has the right to dispose of the sold item. And the buyer cannot cancel the sale without a judge's ruling or the seller's consent. However, this option prevents the bindingness of the sale, because the buyer has the right to return and rescind. Due to these two rights, the sale is not binding.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the five types of preventers (mawani') that hinder the establishment of a legal ruling in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator begins by listing two types that prevent the cause itself: (1) prevention of the inception of the cause, as in selling a free person, where the sale is invalid because the cause (contract) is not legally recognized; (2) prevention of the completion of the cause, as in selling another's property without permission — the contract is valid but incomplete until permission. The commentator notes that Imam Fakhr al-Islam mistakenly classified these under 'takhsis al-illa' (specification of the cause), but the correct view is that they are not specifications because the cause itself is absent. Instead, the author of al-Tawdih adopts the formulation 'what necessitates the absence of the ruling is five' which covers all cases. The remaining three types prevent the ruling after the cause is present: (3) prevention of the beginning of the ruling, exemplified by khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in a sale where ownership does not immediately transfer; (4) prevention of the completion of the ruling, e.g., khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) where ownership is established but not finalized; (5) prevention of the bindingness of the ruling, e.g., khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) where the sale is valid but not binding because the buyer retains the right to rescind. This classification is fundamental for understanding how legal causes interact with their effects in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): A factor that prevents the existence, completion, or bindingness of a ruling despite the presence of its cause
تخصيص العلة (takhsis al-illa): Specification of the cause: the cause is present but the ruling is excluded for a specific reason
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation: a contractual right to cancel within a specified period
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): Option of inspection: the right to cancel a sale after seeing the item if it was bought unseen
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect: the right to return a defective item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of preventer prevents the ruling from being binding (luzum) despite the ruling being established?
A) Mani' yamna' ibtida' al-hukm
B) Mani' yamna' tamam al-illa
C) Mani' yamna' tamam al-hukm
D) Mani' yamna' luzum al-hukm

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mawani' are five: those blocking the cause's establishment, its completion, the ruling's inception, its completion, and its bindingness.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Al-Tarjih: Preponderance of Evidences in Hanafi Usul
Defining tarjih and its rules with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarjih, identify its conditions, and apply the Hanafi rules for preponderance between conflicting evidences using intrinsic strength.

Core Idea
Tarjih is based on intrinsic strength, not mere multiplicity of evidences or claims.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text defines tarjih (preponderance) and lays out its fundamental rules. The author emphasizes that preference between conflicting evidences arises from inherent qualities, not from the number of evidences or the size of shares in property rights. Understanding this principle is key to resolving apparent contradictions in legal proofs.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of tarjih
Identify the precise meaning as 'preference of one of two similar things due to a specific quality' and note the nuance between tarjih (active preference) and rujhan (mere inclination). The author clarifies that the definition is 'bayān faḍl aḥad al-mithlayn' (expressing the superiority of one of the two issues).
The quality must be intrinsic, not an independent proof.
2
Identify the condition of the quality (waṣf)
The quality used for tarjih must be an attribute that is not self-subsisting; it enhances one evidence over another. For example, justice in a witness is the quality, but it is not an independent proof of truthfulness.
Multiplicity alone is not a valid quality.
3
Apply the rule against multiplicity
Understand that a single qiyas is not outweighed by two opposing qiyas, nor a hadith by another hadith, nor a Quranic verse by another verse, unless the evidence itself has greater intrinsic strength.
This refutes the notion that numbers determine preponderance.
4
Examine practical examples
Analyze the wound case: if one wound is fatal (e.g., decapitation) and another is non-fatal, the fatal wounder is the sole killer. In shuf'a: co-owners with unequal shares have equal pre-emption rights. Both illustrate that intrinsic quality, not quantity, drives tarjih.
The shuf'a example includes a madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i.
5
Study two methods of tarjih in qiyas
Identify (1) strength of effect (athar) – istihsan over qiyas because its effect is stronger; (2) strength of provenness (thubut) – an attribute more necessary for the ruling, as in intention in Ramadan fast vs. make-up fast.
These methods derive from the principle of intrinsic strength.

وكذا الشفيعان في استحقاق الشفعة ولا يترجح أحدهما على الآخر بكثرة نصيبه صورتها دار مشتركة بين ثلاثة لأحدهم سدسها ولآخر نصفها ولثالث ثلثها فباع صاحب النصف مثلا نصيبه وطلب الآخران الشفعة يكون المبيع بينهما نصفين بالشفعة وعند الشافعي يقضى بالشقص المبيع أثلاثا لأن الشفعة من مرافق الملك فيكون مقسوما على قدره وإنما وضع المسألة في الشقص وإن كان حكم الجوار عندنا كذلك لتأتي فيه خلاف الشافعي وما يقع به الترجيح أن ترجيح أحد القياسين على الآخر أربعة بقوة الأثر كالاستحسان في معارضة القياس والأثر في الاستحسان أقوى فيترجح عليه فإن قيل فعلى يلزم أن يكون الشاهد الأعدل راجحا على العادل لأن أثره أقوى أجيب بأنا لانسلم أن العدالة تختلف بالزيادة والنقصان فإنها عبارة عن الانزجار عن محظورات الدين بالاحتراز عن الكبائر وعدم الإصرار على الصغائر وهو أمر مضبوط لا يتعدد وإنما الاختلاف في التقوى وبقوة ثباته أي ثبات الوصف على الحكم المشهور به يكون وصفة الزم للحكم المتعلق به من وصف القياس الآخر كقولنا في صوم رمضان أنه متعين من جانب الله تعالى فلا يجب التعيين على العبد في النية أولى من قولهم صوم فرض فيجب تعيين النية فيه كصوم القضاء لأن هذا أي وصف الفرضية الذي أورده الشافعي مخصوص في الصوم بخلاف التعيين الذي أوردناه تقد تعدى إلى الودائع والمغصوب ورد المبيع في البيع الفاسد أي إذا رد الوديعة إلى المالك والمغصوب إليه أو رد المبيع الفاسد إلى البائع بأي جهة كانت يخرج من العهدة.
As for opposition in transmitted evidences, 'tarjih' is a term meaning preference of one of the two similar things, and giving preference to one of two evidences due to a specific quality, i.e., expressing the superiority of one of the two similar things. The author of the matn's phrase 'فضل احد المثلين' is originally 'بيان فضل احد المثلين' (expressing the superiority of one of the two issues). If the genitive construction is not considered deleted, then this definition would be of 'رجحان' (inclination) and not of 'ترجيح' (preference). The author's word 'وصفا' means that the reason for preference is not an independent proof in itself, but a quality of the evidence that is not self-subsisting. For example, the testimony of a just person is preferred over that of a sinful person because of the quality of justice. Similarly, the testimony of four people is not preferred over that of two just people. Thus, qiyas is not given preference over an opposing qiyas by a third qiyas that supports the first, because then one side has one qiyas and the other has two qiyas. Likewise, a hadith is not preferred over its opposing hadith by a third supporting hadith, nor is a Qur'anic verse preferred over its opposing verse by a third supporting verse. Rather, preference occurs between qiyas, hadith, and Qur'an due to the strength inherent in them. Therefore, istihsan whose effect is sound is given priority over qiyas that is weak in effect. A mashhur hadith is given priority over khabar wahid. A muhkam and definitive Qur'anic verse is given priority over a verse whose meaning is zanni. Similarly, the one who inflicts multiple wounds is not preferred over the one who inflicts a single wound. Thus, if a man inflicts one wound on a man and another man inflicts multiple wounds, and the wounded man dies, the one who inflicted multiple wounds is not preferred (so that his wounding caused death). Rather, the blood-money is divided equally between both wounders. This is unlike the case where one of them inflicted stronger and deeper wounds and the other inflicted minor wounds, because then death is attributed to the one who inflicted the serious wound. For example, one cut off the hand and the other severed the neck; then the one who severed the neck is considered the killer, because living without a neck is impossible, unlike without a hand. Likewise, two pre-emptors in pre-emption (shuf'a) are equal in their right to pre-empt, and one is not preferred over the other due to the larger size of his share. The example: a house owned jointly by three: one owns 1/6, another 1/2, and the third 1/3. The owner of half sells his share, and the other two claim pre-emption. The sold property is divided equally between them by pre-emption. According to Shafi'i, it is divided into thirds, because pre-emption is a right pertaining to ownership, so it is divided proportionally. The issue is placed here (though the rule of neighbors is the same according to us) to include the disagreement with Shafi'i. What actually causes preference (tarjih) between two qiyas are four things: (1) strength of effect, like istihsan in opposing qiyas; the effect of istihsan is stronger, so it takes precedence. If it is said, then the testimony of the more just would be preferred over the merely just, because his effect is stronger. The answer: we do not accept that justice varies in increase and decrease; it is a matter of refraining from religious prohibitions by avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins. That is a fixed matter, not varying. The difference is in piety (taqwa). (2) By strength of its provenness, i.e., the provenness of the attribute over the ruling that is well-known due to it; that attribute is more necessary for the ruling connected to it than the attribute of the other qiyas. For example, our saying about fasting in Ramadan: it is determined by Allah, so determination of intention is not obligatory on the servant, which is more preferable than their saying: it is an obligatory fast, so determination of intention is required, like the fast of make-up. Because this attribute of obligation, which al-Shafi'i used, is specific to fasting, unlike determination, which we used, which extends to deposits, usurped property, and return of sold goods in invalid sales. That is, if one returns a deposit to the owner or the usurped property to its owner, or returns the sold goods in an invalid sale to the seller by any means, he is discharged from liability.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition and rules of tarjih (preponderance). The author begins by clarifying that tarjih means giving preference to one of two similar things due to a specific quality. He notes that if the matn's phrase 'فضل احد المثلين' is interpreted literally without understanding the deletion, it would define 'رجحان' (inclination) rather than 'ترجيح' (active preference). The quality (wasf) used for tarjih must be an attribute that is not an independent proof but enhances one evidence over another, like justice in a witness. Crucially, tarjih is not achieved by the number of evidences: a single qiyas is not outweighed by two opposing qiyas, nor is a hadith by another hadith, nor a Quranic verse by another verse, unless the evidence itself has greater intrinsic strength (quwwa). This intrinsic strength can come from istihsan (stronger effect), from the fame of a hadith (mashhur over khabar wahid), or from clarity of text (muhkam over zanni). The author then applies this to wounds: in a homicide case where multiple wounds are inflicted, if one wound is clearly fatal (e.g., decapitation) compared to another (e.g., cutting a hand), the fatal wounder is the sole killer; otherwise, blood-money is shared equally. This illustrates the principle that intrinsic quality, not multiplicity, determines preponderance. Finally, the passage discusses shuf'a (pre-emption) among joint owners with unequal shares: despite differing shares, all co-owners have equal pre-emption rights, and the sold share is divided equally among them, not proportionally to their shares. The Hanafi position is contrasted with al-Shafi'i's, who divides proportionally. The author explains that the purpose of including this example is to highlight the disagreement and to demonstrate that tarjih does not occur merely due to larger share (quantity). The discussion then returns to the methods of tarjih in qiyas: (1) strength of effect (athar), e.g., istihsan over qiyas; (2) strength of thubut (provenness) – an attribute that is more necessary for the ruling – illustrated by the example of intention in Ramadan fast vs. make-up fast, where al-Shafi'i's attribute (obligation) is specific to fasting, whereas the Hanafi attribute (determination by Allah) extends to other areas and thus is stronger.

Key Terms
الترجیح (al-tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one of two similar evidences or claims due to a specific quality.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): A stronger effect (athar) that causes qiyas to be preferred over another qiyas; it is a source of tarjih.
الشفعة (al-shufʿa): The right of pre-emption for a co-owner to acquire a sold share from another co-owner, divided equally among all pre-emptors in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Proportionally to each co-owner's share.
B) Equally among all pre-emptors regardless of share size.
C) According to the seniority of ownership.
D) To the co-owner with the largest share.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in Hanafi usul is based on intrinsic strength of the evidence, not on the number of evidences or shares; multiplicity alone does not confer preference.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
10 min
What Is Established by the Proofs: Rulings and Their Adjuncts
Opening of rulings section: proofs establish taklifi and wadi'i rulings; qiyas excluded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between taklifi and wadi'i rulings and explain why qiyas is excluded from the proofs that establish rulings.

Core Idea
Qiyas does not establish a new ruling; it only extends an existing one from the primary proofs.

After discussing the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma), the author turns to what these proofs establish: the rulings of Shari'ah. He clarifies that qiyas is not a source of new rulings but merely a tool for extending existing ones. This distinction is fundamental in Hanafi usul: a ruling is either taklifi (a direct demand on the mukallaf) or wadi'i (a condition, cause, or impediment). Understanding this classification helps us see how the proofs function and sets the stage for the deeper analysis of the components of a ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of usul
The author states that the subject of usul al-fiqh, according to the chosen madhhab, is both the proofs (adilla) and the rulings (ahkam). After finishing the proofs, he now begins the rulings. This two-part structure is a hallmark of Hanafi usul works.
2
Understand why qiyas is excluded from 'thubut'
The author says: 'I excluded qiyas because it does not establish anything; it is only for extension (ta'diya).' The term 'thubut' here means establishment of a ruling. Qiyas does not create a new ruling; it transfers a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared illa. Therefore, it is not a 'proof that establishes' but a 'proof for extension'.
If 'thubut' is taken in a general sense including extension, then the four proofs would include qiyas, but the author narrows it to establishment only.
3
Differentiate taklifi and wadi'i rulings
The author states that the two things established by the proofs are: the rulings (al-ahkam) and what pertains to the rulings (ma yata'allaqu biha al-ahkam). In the commentary, these are identified as taklifi rulings and wadi'i rulings, respectively. Taklifi rulings are direct demands (wajib, haram, etc.), while wadi'i rulings are conditions, causes, or impediments that affect other rulings.
This distinction is key: a wadi'i ruling does not command an action directly but sets a precondition (e.g., purity for prayer) or a cause (e.g., nisab for zakat).
4
Recognize the three components of a ruling
The author then explains that every ruling depends on the Ruler (al-hakim – Allah), the subject of the ruling (al-mahkum 'alayh – the mukallaf), and the object of the ruling (al-mahkum bih – the action). This framework is the foundation for the upcoming discussions on capacity (ahliyyah) and obstacles.
This sets the stage for the detailed analysis of the mahkum bih (action) and mahkum 'alayh (subject) in subsequent sections.

ثُمَّ لَمَّا فَرَغَ الْمُصَلِّف عَنْ يَحْثِ الأدلّةِ الأَرْبَعَةِ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَبْحَثُ بَعْدَهَا عَمَا ثَبَتَ بالأدلة وقَدْ قُلْت فِيْمَا سَبَقَ إِنْ مَوْضُوعَ عِلْمَ الأصول عَلَى الْمَذْهَبِ الْمُخْتَارِ هوَ الأدلة والأحكامُ جَمِيعًا فَبَعْدَ الفَراغ عَنِ الأول شرَعَ فِي الثاني فَقَالَ فَصل ثُم جُمْلَةُ مَاثَبَتَ بِالْحَجَجَ الَّتِي سَبَقَ ذِكْرُهَا عَلَى بَابِ الْقَيَاسِ يَعْنِي الْكِتَابَ والسنَّةَ وَالإجْمَاعَ شَيْئَانِ الأَحْكَامُ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقَ بهِ الأَحْكَامُ وَإِثْمَا اسْتَثْتُيْتُ القياس لأنه لا يُثْبِتُ شَيئًا وَإِنْمَا هُوَ لِلتَّعْدِيَةِ وَلَوْ أَرِيْدَ بِالقُبُوتِ الْمَعْنى الأعم فَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُرَادَ بِالْحُجَج الأدلَّةُ الأَرْبَعَةُ وَالمُرَادُ بِالأحكام الأحكامُ التَّكْلِيفِيَّةُ وَبِمَا يَتعلق به الأَحْكَامُ الْوَصْعِيَةُ وَقَدْ ذَكَرُوا هَذِهِ الْقَوَاعِدَ مُنْتَشِرَةٌ وَالَّذِي يُعْلَمُ مِنَ التوضيح فِي صَبَطِهَا إِنَّ الْحُكْمَ مُفْتَقِرُ إِلَى الْحَاكِمِ وَالْمَحْكُوْم عَلَيْهِ والمحكوم به فالْحَاكِمُ هُوَ الله تَعَالَى وَالْمَحْكُومَ عَلَيْهِ هُوَ الْمُكَلِّفُ وَالْمَحْكُومُ بِهِ فَعْلُ الْمُكَلِّفِ بِهِ مِنَ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَالْعُقُوبَاتِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا وَالْأَحْكَامُ صِفَاتٌ فِعْلٍ الْمُكَلَّفِ مِنَ الْوُجُوْبِ وَالنُّدْبِ وَالْفَرْضِيَةِ وَ الْعَزِيْمَةِ وَالرُّخْضَةِ فَعَلَى هَذَا التحقيق الأحْكَامُ فِي صِفَاتُ الْفِعْلِ وَقَدْ مَضى ذَكَرَهَا بَعْدَ بَحْثِ الْكِتَابِ فِي الْعَزِيْمَةِ وَالرُّحْصَةِ وَهَذَا الْمَبْحَثُ مَبْحَثُ فِعْلِ الْمُكَلِّلْفِ يَعْنِى الْمَحْكُومَ بِهِ وَمَبْحَثُ الْمَحْكُومَ عَلَيْهِ بِاتِى بَعْدَهُ فِى بِيَانِ الأَهْلِيَةِ وَالأُمُورِ الْمُعْتَرِضَةِ عَلَيْهَا وَبِالْجُمْلَةِ لاَ يَحْلُوا تَقْسِيمُ الْقَدَمَاءِ عَنْ مُسَامَحَةٍ أَمَّا الأَحْكَامُ فَارْبَعَةٌ يَعْنِي الْمَحْكُومُ بِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ عِبارَةٌ عَنْ فِعْلِ الْمُكَلِّفِ اَرْبَعَةُ أَنْوَاعِ الأَوَّلُ حُقوق اللهِ تَعَالَى خَالِصَةٌ وَهُوَ مَا يَتَعَلُقُ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعَام كَحُرْمَةِ الْبَيْتِ فَإِنْ نَفْعُهُ عَامُ لِلنَّاسِ بِاتِّخَانِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ قَبْلَةً وَكَحَرْمَةِ الزَّنَا فَإِنَّ نَفَعُهُ عَامَ لِلنَّاسِ بِسَلامَةِ أَنْسَابِهِمْ وَإِنَّمَا نُسب إلى اللهِ تَعَالَى تَعْظِيمًا وَإِلا فَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَنْ يَنْتَفِعَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا يَجُودُ أَنْ يَكُونَ حَقًّا لَهُ بِهَذَا الْوَجْهِ وَلَا بِجَهَةِ التَّخْلِيْقِ إِنَّ الْكُلِّ سَوَاءٌ فِي ذالك . انم لما فرغ المصنف عَنْ بَحْث الأدلة الأربعة جب مصنف دلائل اربعہ کے بیان ترجمہ و تشریح ثُمَّ فَرَغَ سے فارغ ہوئے تو اب ما ثبت بالا دلۂ یعنی احکام کا ذکر فرمانا چاہتے ہیں وقد قلت فيما سنبق اور میں نے ما سبق میں کہہ دیا تھا کہ علم اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام دونوں ہیں لہذا اول سے فارغ ہو کو مصنف ثانی کو شروع فرمار ہے ہیں یہ بصل ثم جملة ما ثبت بالحجج (فصل احکام اور متعلقات احکام کے بیان میں ) دلائل مذکورہ سے جو کچھ ثابت ہوا باب قیاس سے پہلے جن دلائل کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے وہ مراد ہیں یعنی کتاب، سنت اور اجماع شینان الاحكام وما يتعلق بها الاحکام و حد و چیزیں ہیں اول احکام دوم وہ امور جین کے ساتھ احکام کا میں نے دلائل مذکورہ سے قیاس کا استثناء کر دیا ہے کیونکہ قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ قیاس محض تعد یہ حکم کے لئے ہوا کرتا ہے اور اگر بثبوت سے عام معنی مراد لئے جائیں (یعنی اثبات حکم اور تعد محکم تو پھر ممکن ہے کہ بیج سے ادلہ اربعہ مراد لئے جائیں اور احکام سے وہ احکام مراد ہیں جن کا بند سے کو مکلف بنایا گیا ہے
Then when the author finished the discussion of the four proofs, he wanted to discuss after them what is established by the proofs. And I have already said before that the subject of usul al-fiqh according to the chosen madhhab is both the proofs and the rulings. So after completing the first, he began the second. He said: 'Chapter: Then the totality of what is established by the proofs that were mentioned before the chapter on qiyas' meaning the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma, are two things: the rulings and what pertains to the rulings. And I excluded qiyas because it does not establish anything; it is only for extension. If by 'thubut' the general meaning is intended, then it is possible that the 'proofs' mean the four proofs, and the 'rulings' mean the taklifi rulings, and 'what pertains to the rulings' means the wadi' rulings. And they have mentioned these principles scattered. What is known from al-Tawdih in their arrangement is that the ruling is dependent on the ruler, the subject of the ruling, and the object of the ruling. The ruler is Allah, the subject is the mukallaf, and the object is the action of the mukallaf in acts of worship, punishments, and other things. And the rulings are attributes of the mukallaf's action from obligation, recommendation, mandatory, determination, and concession. According to this verification, the rulings are attributes of the action. And their mention has already passed after the discussion of the Book in the section on 'azima and rukhsah. And this discussion is the discussion of the action of the mukallaf, i.e., the object of the ruling, and the discussion of the subject of the ruling comes after it in the explanation of capacity and the obstacles to it. In summary, the division of the ancients is not free from approximation. As for the rulings, they are four: meaning the object of the ruling, which is the action of the mukallaf, has four types: first, the pure rights of Allah, which are those whose benefit is general, like the sanctity of the Kaaba, for its benefit is general for people by their taking it as a qibla, and like the prohibition of zina, for its benefit is general for people by the preservation of their lineages. It is attributed to Allah out of veneration; otherwise, Allah is far above benefiting from anything. So it cannot be a right for Him in this way or in the way of creation, for all are equal in that. Then when the author finished the discussion of the four proofs... (Urdu commentary follows).
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage begins the second major part of usul al-fiqh: the rulings established by the proofs. The author clarifies that the subject of usul al-fiqh includes both proofs and rulings. After discussing proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma), he now examines what they establish: rulings (ahkam taklifiyya) and their adjuncts (ahkam wadi'iyya). Qiyas is excluded because it does not create a new ruling but merely extends an existing one. The passage then explains the components of a ruling: the Ruler (Allah), the subject (mukallaf), and the object (action). Rulings are attributes of actions (e.g., wajib, mandub, etc.). It then classifies the object of rulings into four types, beginning with the pure rights of Allah—those that benefit the general public, such as the sanctity of the Kaaba and the prohibition of zina. These are attributed to Allah as an honorific, not because He benefits. The passage also references that the detailed discussion of 'azima and rukhsah has already passed.

Key Terms
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A ruling that directly requires the mukallaf to perform or refrain from an action, such as wajib, haram, etc.
حكم وضعي (hukm wadi'i): A ruling that is not a direct demand but establishes a condition, cause, or impediment for a taklifi ruling.
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment; in this context, the act of a proof establishing a ruling as authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is qiyas excluded from the proofs that establish rulings?
A) Because qiyas is a weak proof not accepted by all scholars.
B) Because qiyas does not establish anything; it is only for extension.
C) Because the Hanafi madhhab does not use qiyas at all.
D) Because qiyas was introduced after the early generations.

Key Takeaway
The primary proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) establish rulings (taklifi and wadi'i), while qiyas only extends rulings to new cases.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Object of the Ruling: Haqq Allah and the Classification of Actions
Classification of the object of ruling into four types; detailed analysis of haqq Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'haqq Allah' in the Hanafi usul framework and explain why it is attributed to Allah despite Allah not benefiting.

Core Idea
Haqq Allah rulings benefit the general public and are attributed to Allah as veneration, not because He benefits.

In the previous lesson, we learned that rulings are attributes of actions. Now we delve into the object of the ruling—the action itself—and how the early scholars classified it into four types. The first and most significant category is the pure rights of Allah (haqq Allah). These are rulings whose benefit is universal, such as the sanctity of the Kaaba or the prohibition of zina. Understanding why these are attributed to Allah clarifies the distinction between divine commands and individual entitlements, and underscores the public interest (maslaha) underlying Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Explain that rulings are attributes of actions
The author says: 'The rulings are attributes of the mukallaf's action from obligation, recommendation, etc.' This means that when we say an action is wajib or haram, we are describing a quality of that action as determined by Shari'ah. The action itself (the mahkum bih) is the locus of the ruling.
2
Classify the object into four types according to the ancients
The author notes that the ancients divided the object (the action) into four types. He only details the first in this passage: the pure rights of Allah. The other three types (rights of individuals, mixed rights, etc.) are implied or expected in later discussions.
The passage does not list all four explicitly but prepares the student for a more detailed taxonomy.
3
Analyze the first type: Haqq Allah (pure) with examples
The author gives two examples: the sanctity of the Kaaba and the prohibition of zina. He explains that the benefit of these rulings is general (naf' 'am). For the Kaaba, everyone benefits by having a qibla. For zina, society benefits by preserving lineages. These are not for the benefit of Allah but for the creation.
4
Understand the attribution to Allah as honorific
The author emphasizes that calling these 'rights of Allah' is out of veneration (ta'zim), not because Allah benefits. Allah is above needing anything. This distinction is crucial to avoid anthropomorphism and to highlight the public welfare aspect.
This principle underlies the Hanafi view that punishment for crimes like zina is a right of Allah that cannot be waived by an individual.

تَعَالَى خَالِصَةٌ وَهُوَ مَا يَتَعَلُقُ بِهِ نَفْعُ الْعَام كَحُرْمَةِ الْبَيْتِ فَإِنْ نَفْعُهُ عَامُ لِلنَّاسِ بِاتِّخَانِهِمْ إِيَّاهُ قَبْلَةً وَكَحَرْمَةِ الزَّنَا فَإِنَّ نَفَعُهُ عَامَ Then when the author finished the discussion of the four proofs, he wanted to discuss after them what is established by the proofs. And I have already said before that the subject of usul al-fiqh according to the chosen madhhab is both the proofs and the rulings. So after completing the first, he began the second. He said: 'Chapter: Then the totality of what is established by the proofs that were mentioned before the chapter on qiyas' meaning the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma, are two things: the rulings and what pertains to the rulings. And I excluded qiyas because it does not establish anything; it is only for extension. If by 'thubut' the general meaning is intended, then it is possible that the 'proofs' mean the four proofs, and the 'rulings' mean the taklifi rulings, and 'what pertains to the rulings' means the wadi' rulings. And they have mentioned these principles scattered. What is known from al-Tawdih in their arrangement is that the ruling is dependent on the ruler, the subject of the ruling, and the object of the ruling. The ruler is Allah, the subject is the mukallaf, and the object is the action of the mukallaf in acts of worship, punishments, and other things. And the rulings are attributes of the mukallaf's action from obligation, recommendation, mandatory, determination, and concession. According to this verification, the rulings are attributes of the action. And their mention has already passed after the discussion of the Book in the section on 'azima and rukhsah. And this discussion is the discussion of the action of the mukallaf, i.e., the object of the ruling, and the discussion of the subject of the ruling comes after it in the explanation of capacity and the obstacles to it. In summary, the division of the ancients is not free from approximation. As for the rulings, they are four: meaning the object of the ruling, which is the action of the mukallaf, has four types: first, the pure rights of Allah, which are those whose benefit is general, like the sanctity of the Kaaba, for its benefit is general for people by their taking it as a qibla, and like the prohibition of zina, for its benefit is general for people by the preservation of their lineages. It is attributed to Allah out of veneration; otherwise, Allah is far above benefiting from anything. So it cannot be a right for Him in this way or in the way of creation, for all are equal in that. Commentary
This passage begins the second major part of usul al-fiqh: the rulings established by the proofs. The author clarifies that the subject of usul al-fiqh includes both proofs and rulings. After discussing proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma), he now examines what they establish: rulings (ahkam taklifiyya) and their adjuncts (ahkam wadi'iyya). Qiyas is excluded because it does not create a new ruling but merely extends an existing one. The passage then explains the components of a ruling: the Ruler (Allah), the subject (mukallaf), and the object (action). Rulings are attributes of actions (e.g., wajib, mandub, etc.). It then classifies the object of rulings into four types, beginning with the pure rights of Allah—those that benefit the general public, such as the sanctity of the Kaaba and the prohibition of zina. These are attributed to Allah as an honorific, not because He benefits. The passage also references that the detailed discussion of 'azima and rukhsah has already passed.

Key Terms
حق الله (haqq Allah): A ruling whose benefit is general to the public; attributed to Allah as veneration, not because He benefits.
نفع عام (naf' 'am): General benefit that accrues to the public as a whole, such as social order, lineage preservation, or religious unity.
تعظيم (ta'zim): Veneration; the reason why rulings are attributed to Allah despite His self-sufficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the prohibition of zina considered a 'right of Allah'?
A) Because Allah directly benefits when people avoid zina.
B) Because its benefit is general (preserving lineage) and it is attributed to Allah out of veneration.
C) Because only Allah can forgive the sin of zina.
D) Because the punishment for zina is prescribed in the Quran and cannot be changed.

Key Takeaway
Pure rights of Allah are those rulings whose benefit is universal, attributed to Allah to emphasize their importance for public welfare.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Fourfold Classification of Rulings: Rights of Allah and Rights of Servants
Introduces the classification of ahkam after discussing the four proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi classification of rulings into four types based on whose right is dominant, and explain the practical legal consequences for each type.

Core Idea
Rulings are divided by whose interest they serve: public (Ḥaqq Allāh), private (Ḥaqq al-ʿAbd), or mixed with one dominant.

This passage transitions from studying the four proofs to studying what they establish: the rulings (ahkam). It clarifies that rulings are not random; they are categorized by whose right is primary. This classification is essential for determining legal effects like pardonability, inheritance, and compensation. We will follow the Hanafi framework and note where another school differs.

Guided Path
1
Frame the mahkum bih
Understand that the object of ruling (mahkum bih) is the act of the mukallaf, and rulings are attributes such as obligation, recommendation, etc. This section focuses on the object.
The lawgiver (Allah) and subject (mukallaf) are established; here we analyze the act itself.
2
Grasp the fourfold classification
The mahkum bih is divided into four types based on whose right is predominant: pure Allah's right (public benefit), pure servant's right (private benefit), mixed with Allah's right dominant, mixed with servant's right dominant.
Attribution to Allah is for glorification—He does not benefit. Examples: sanctity of Kaaba, prohibition of adultery.
3
Analyze the practical differences
Each type carries distinct legal consequences: pure servant's rights can be waived; mixed with Allah's right dominant (e.g., hadd qadhf) cannot be pardoned or inherited; mixed with servant's right dominant (e.g., qisas) can be pardoned or settled with compensation.
Compare with Shafi'i view on qadhf where servant's right is dominant.

نفع حاصل کرے لہذا ذاتی نفع اٹھانے کے اعتبار سے ان کو حق اللہ کہنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ تخلیق کے اعتبار سے ان کو حق اللہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ ان معنی کے اعتبار سے تو خالق سارے ہی افعال کا اللہ تعالی ہی
