الصالح، وحق العبد من حيث إزالة عار المقذوف، لكن حق الله تعالى غالب حتى لا يجري فيه الإرث والعفو، وعند الشافعي حق العبد فيه غالب فتنعكس الأحكام. والرابع ما اجتمعا فيه وحق العبد غالب كالقصاص فإن فيه حق الله وهو إخلاء العالم عن الفساد، وحق العبد بوقوع الجناية على نفسه، وهو غالب لجريان الإرث وصحة الاعتياض عنه بالمال بالصلح وصحة العفو. وحقوق الله تعالى ثمانية أنواع: عبادات خالصة لا يسبقها معنى العقوبة والمؤنة كالإيمان وفروعه وهي الصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج، وإنما كانت فروعا للإيمان لأنها لا تصح بدونه وهو.
Qiyas (analogy) because it does not establish something new but rather extends [the ruling]. If what is meant by 'thubut' (establishment) is the general meaning, then it is possible that by 'proofs' the four proofs are meant, and by 'rulings' the taklifi rulings are meant, and by 'what pertains to them' the wad'i rulings. They have mentioned these rules in a scattered manner. What is understood from al-Tawdih regarding their arrangement is that a ruling is dependent on the Lawgiver, the subject, and the object. The Lawgiver is Allah Almighty, the subject is the legally responsible person (mukallaf), and the object is the act of the mukallaf from acts of worship, punishments, and others. Rulings are attributes of the act of the mukallaf such as obligation, recommendation, farḍiyya, determination, and concession. According to this verification, rulings are attributes of the act. Their mention has preceded after the discussion of the Book [of Allah] under the topic of determination and concession. This discussion is about the act of the mukallaf, meaning the object of the ruling. The discussion of the subject will follow in the explanation of capacity and the impediments. In summary, the division of the early scholars is not free from leniency. As for the rulings, they are four: meaning the object of the ruling which is the act of the mukallaf is of four types: First: the pure rights of Allah Almighty, which is what pertains to public benefit, like the sanctity of the House [Kaaba] because its benefit is general for people by their taking it as a qibla, and like the prohibition of adultery because its benefit is general for people by preserving their lineages. It is attributed to Allah Almighty for glorification; otherwise, Allah is far above benefiting from anything. So it is not permissible that it be a right for Him in this sense, nor from the aspect of creation, for all are equal in that. As for when the author finished discussing the four proofs, then he finished the translation and commentary of the four proofs, then he finished from that, so now he wants to mention what is established by the proofs, i.e., the rulings. I have said in the past that the subject of usul al-fiqh is both the proofs and the rulings. Therefore, having finished the first, the author begins the second. This is then the total of what is established by the proofs (a chapter on rulings and what pertains to them). From the mentioned proofs, what is intended is what was mentioned before the chapter on qiyas, i.e., the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma'. The rulings and what pertains to them: rulings are two things: first, rulings; second, those matters with which rulings are connected. I have excluded qiyas from the mentioned proofs because no ruling is established by qiyas. This is because qiyas is merely for extension of the ruling. If by 'establishment' a general meaning is intended (i.e., establishment of ruling and extension of the established [ruling]), then it is possible that by 'proofs' the four proofs are intended, and by 'rulings' those rulings with which the servant is obligated. And by 'what pertains to rulings' is meant wad'i rulings (e.g., rulings of acts of worship, punishments, etc.). The example of wad'i rulings are the causes and conditions of rulings. The verification is that the scholars of usul have mentioned these rules in a scattered manner without order. From the book al-Tawdih it is understood that every ruling is dependent on three things: (1) the Lawgiver, (2) the subject, and (3) the object. So the Lawgiver is Allah Almighty, the subject is the mukallaf, and the object is the act of the mukallaf, whether acts of worship, punishments, or other than them. And rulings are in reality names for the act of the mukallaf, e.g., obligation, recommendation, farḍiyya, determination, and concession. Based on this verification, rulings are attributes of the act. Its mention has passed in the discussion of the Book of Allah under the heading of 'azima and rukhsa. And the discussion here is actually the discussion of the act of the mukallaf, i.e., the object of the ruling. The discussion of the subject will come after, where capacity will be explained and the impediments will be mentioned. The conclusion is that the division of the early scholars is not free from leniency. As for the rulings, they are four: i.e., the object which is the act of the mukallaf is of four types: first: pure rights of Allah Almighty, i.e., those rulings from which the general public benefit, e.g., the respect of the Sacred House because by making it a qibla, all people benefit; and like the prohibition of adultery, because if adultery occurs, lineages are not preserved. (The benefit is for the general public, but it is attributed to Allah Almighty as a form of glorification; otherwise, the Almighty is far above benefiting from anything. So attributing it to Him as a right is not permissible from the aspect of personal benefit, nor from the aspect of creation, because in that sense, Allah is the Creator of all acts). Second: pure rights of servants, which pertain to a specific interest, like the prohibition of taking another's property; therefore it becomes permissible with the owner's permission. Third: that in which both combine, and Allah's right is dominant, like the hadd penalty for qadhf (false accusation of adultery); for in it is Allah's right insofar as it is a punishment for violating the honor of a chaste righteous person, and the servant's right insofar as it removes the disgrace from the accused. But Allah's right is dominant such that inheritance and pardon do not apply. According to al-Shafi'i, the servant's right is dominant, so the rulings are reversed. Fourth: that in which both combine, and the servant's right is dominant, like qisas (retaliation); for in it is Allah's right, which is purifying the world from corruption, and the servant's right is by the injury occurring on himself, and it is dominant because inheritance is applicable, and it is valid to accept compensation in property through reconciliation, and pardon is valid. The rights of Allah Almighty are eight types: pure acts of worship not preceded by the meaning of punishment and hardship, like faith and its branches, which are prayer, zakat, fasting, and hajj. They are branches of faith because they are not valid without it.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage serves as a transition from the study of the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) to the study of what is established by them, namely the rulings (ahkam). The author begins by clarifying the scope: he excludes Qiyas from the proofs that establish rulings because Qiyas does not create a new ruling but merely extends an existing one. He then distinguishes between taklifi rulings (obligation, recommendation, etc.) and wad'i rulings (cause, condition, etc.). The passage then establishes the foundational framework: every ruling requires a Lawgiver (al-Hakim, Allah), a subject (al-Mahkum 'alayhi, the mukallaf), and an object (al-Mahkum bihi, the act of the mukallaf). The focus of this section is the object (mahkum bih), which is the act of the mukallaf. The author notes that the early scholars' division is somewhat lenient. He then provides the four-fold classification of rulings based on whose right is involved: (1) pure rights of Allah, where the benefit is public; (2) pure rights of servants, where the benefit is private; (3) mixed rights where Allah's right is dominant (e.g., hadd for qadhf); and (4) mixed rights where the servant's right is dominant (e.g., qisas). The passage highlights a difference with Shafi'i on qadhf: the Hanafi view holds Allah's right dominant, while Shafi'i holds the servant's right dominant. Finally, it enumerates eight types of Allah's rights, specifically pure acts of worship that are not punishments, such as faith and its branches (prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj). This classification is fundamental for understanding the legal consequences of each type, such as the permissibility of pardon, inheritance, or compensation.

Key Terms
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): A ruling that primarily serves the public interest and is attributed to Allah for glorification.
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-ʿabd): A ruling that primarily serves the private interest of an individual, and can be waived by them.
محكوم به (maḥkūm bihī): The act of the mukallaf that is the subject of a legal ruling, including acts of worship, transactions, and punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following is an example of mixed rights where Allah's right is dominant?
A) The prohibition of stealing private property
B) The hadd penalty for false accusation (qadhf)
C) The law of qisas (retaliation)
D) The obligation of prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of rulings into four types based on dominant right (Allah's or servant's) determines key legal consequences such as pardonability, inheritance, and compensation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
8 min
The Four Categories of Rights in Hanafi Uṣūl
Classifying rulings by whose right (ḥaqq) predominates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given ruling (maḥkūm bih) into one of the four categories of ḥaqq (Allah pure, servant pure, mixed with Allah predominant, mixed with servant predominant) and state the legal consequences for each category.

Core Idea
Rulings are classified by whose right predominates: Allah's or the servant's, determining waivability and inheritance.

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, every ruling (ḥukm) has three components: the Legislator (Allah), the subject (mukallaf), and the object (the action). The object, called maḥkūm bih, is the action of the mukallaf. Scholars further classify these actions based on whose right (ḥaqq) is involved: Allah's right (public interest) or the servant's right (private interest). This classification has direct consequences for whether a ruling can be waived, pardoned, inherited, or commuted. In this lesson, we examine the four categories of rights as presented in the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three elements of a ruling
Recognize that every ruling requires a Legislator (Allah), a subject (mukallaf), and an object (the action). The object is the maḥkūm bih under classification.
The source text emphasizes these three components at the outset.
2
Distinguish pure rights of Allah
Pure rights of Allah are rulings that serve general public benefit, attributed to Allah as a form of glorification. Examples include the sanctity of the Kaaba and the prohibition of zinā.
The benefit is public, not divine; the attribution is out of reverence.
3
Distinguish pure rights of servants
Pure rights of servants are rulings that serve a specific individual benefit, such as property rights. They can be waived by the owner.
Example: the prohibition of taking another's property is lifted with the owner's permission.
4
Analyze mixed rulings and determine predominance
When both rights are present, the ruling is classified by which right predominates. This is determined by legal consequences: if pardon/inheritance applies, the servant's right is predominant; if not, Allah's right predominates.
The text gives clear examples: qadhf (Allah predominant) and qiṣāṣ (servant predominant).
5
Apply the classification to learned examples
Based on the criteria, classify each example from the text and new cases. For each, state the category and the practical implication (e.g., can it be pardoned?).
This step reinforces the criteria through application.

اور متعلق بالا حکام سے مراد احکام وضعی ہیں (احکام کی مثال عبادت ، قوبت وغیرہ) اور احکام وضعی کی مثال اسباب و شر انکا احکام ہیں) اور تحقیق کہ علماء اصول نے ان قواعد کی بلا ترتیب منتشر طور پر بیان کئے ہیں اور کتاب توضیح سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ ہر حکم تین چیزوں کا محتاج ہوتا ہے (۱) حاکم (۲) محکوم علیہ (۳) محکوم به پس حاکم تو اللہ تبارک و تعالی ہیں اور محکوم علیہ مکلف ہے اور محکوم یہ مکلف کا فعل ہے عبادات ہوں یا عقوبات ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ ہو اور احکام در حقیقت مکلف کے فعل کا نام ہے مثلا وجوب غرب فرضیه عزیمت و خصت اس تحقیق کی بناء پر احکام فصل کے اوصاف کا نام ہے اس کا ذکر کتاب اللہ کی بحث میں زیر عنوان عزیمت در خصت گذر چکا ہے اور یہاں پر جو بحث ہورہی ہے وہ دراصل مکلف کے فعل کی بحث ہے یعنی محکوم یہ کی اور محکوم علیہ کی بحث اس کے بعد آئے گی جہاں کی اہمیت کو بیان کیا جائے گا اور امور معترضہ کو ذکر کیا جائے گا حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ متقدمین کی تقسیم تسامح سے خالی نہیں ہے۔
وأما الأحكامُ ما رفعہ بہر حال احکام کی چار قسمیں ہیں یعنی وہ محکوم یہ جو مکلف سے فعل کا نام ہے اس کی چار انواع و اقسام ہیں الاول حقوق اللہ تعالی (1) خالص حقوق اللہ تعالی یعنی وہ احکام جن سے عام لوگوں کو نفع متعلق ہو مثلا بیت اللہ شریف کا احترام کیونکہ اسکو قبلہ بنا کر تمام لوگوں کو نفع ہے اور جیسے زنا کی حرمت اس میں بھی نفع عام لوگوں کا ہے کیونکہ زمانہ ہو گا تو لوگوں کے نسب سلامت رہیں گے (فائدہ عام لوگوں کا ہے مگر نسبت اللہ تعالی کی طرف کی گئی ہے، یہ نسبت بطور تعظیم الہی کے ہے ورنہ حق تعالی کی ذات با برکات ان سے کہیں بالا تر ہے کہ وہ کسی چیز سے نفع حاصل کرے لہذ لذاتی نفع اٹھانے کے اعتبار سے انکو حق اللہ کہنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ تخلیق کے اعتبار سے ان کو حق اللہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ ان معنی کے اعتبار سے تو خالق سارے ہی افعال کا اللہ تعالی ہی ہے وَالثَّانِى حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ خَالِصةً وَهُوَ مَا يَتَعَلْقُ بِه مَصْلَحَةٌ خَاصَّةٌ كَحَرْمَةٍ مَالِ الغَيْرِ ولهذا يُبَاحُ بِايَاحَةِ الْمَالِكِ وَالثَّالِثُ مَا اجْتَمَعَا فِيهِ وَحَقُّ الله غَالِبٌ كَمَدُ الْقَذَف فَإِنْ فِيْهِ حَقَّ الله تعالى مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنه جَزَاءِ هَتَكَ حُرْمَةِ الْعَفِيْفِ الصَّالِحِ وَحَق الْعَبْدِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِزالَة عَارِ الْمَقْذُوفِ بِاكِنْ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى غَالِبٌ حَتَّى لا يَجْرِي فِيهِ الإرث وَالْعَفْوُ وَعِنْدَ الشافعِى حَقَّ الْعَهْدِ فِيهِ غَالِبٌ فَتَنْعَكِسُ الأَحْكَامُ وَالرَّابِعُ مَا. اجْتَمَعَافِيْهِ وَحَقُّ العَبْدِ غَالِبٌ كَالْقِصَاصِ فَإِنْ فِيْهِ حَقَّ اللَّهِ وَهُو إِخْلَاهُ الْعَالَمِ عَنِ الْفَسادِ وَحَقُّ الْعَبْدِ يُوقَوْعِ الْجَنابَةِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ وَهُوَ غَالِبٌ لِجَرَيَانِ الإِرْتِ وَصِحَةِ الاِعْتِيَاض عَنْهُ بِالْمَالِ بالصلحِ وَصحَةِ العَفْوِ وَحُقُوقُ اللهِ تَعَالَى ثَمَانِيَةُ وَأَنواع عِبَادَات خَالِصَةٌ لأَيَسُوبُها مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ وَالْمُؤْنَةِ كَالإِيْمَانِ وَفَرُوْعِهِ وَهِيَ الصَّلوةَ والزكوةُ وَالصَّوْمُ والحَج وَإِنْمَا كَانَتْ فُرُوعًا لِلإيْمَانِ لأَنْهَا لا تَصِحُ بِدُونِهِ وَهُوَ صَحِيحٌ بِدُونِهَا وَهِيَ أَي الْعِبَادَاتِ أَنْوَاعٌ ثَلَثَةٌ أَصَوْلَ وَلَوَاحِقِّ وَدَوَائِدٌ يَعْنِي أَنَّ فِي مَجْمُوع الإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِه هذه الثلاثة لا أن فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُما هذه الثلاثةُ فَالإيْمَانُ أَصلُه لااَن التصديق والملحق به الإِقْرَاهُ وَالزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ الْفُروعُ الْبَاقِيَةُ أَوْ نَقُولُ الزَّوَائِدُ فِي وَالْمُلْحِق الإِيْمَانِ هِيَ تَكْرارُ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالأمثلُ فِي الفُرُوعِ الصَّلوةَ لأَنهَا عِمَادُ الدِّينِ ثُمَّ الزَّكَوةَ مُلْحَقَةٌ بِهَا لأَنْ نِعْمَةَ الْمَالِ الْمَالُ فَرْعٌ لِنَعْمَةِ الْبَدَنِ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ لأَنَّة شرع لِقَهْرِ النَّفْسِ ثُمَّ الحَيُّ ثُمَّ الْجِهَادُ فَهَذِهِ فَرُوعٌ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهَا أَصَوْلٌ وَالْوَاحِق وَحِينَئِذٍ الزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ نَوَافِلُ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَسَنَتُهَا وَكَلُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ فِي كُوْنِهَا وَاجِرَةُ كَالْحُدُودِ فِي حَدَ الزَّنَا وَحَدَ الشَّرْبِ وَحَدَ الْقَذَفِ وَحَدُ السَّرَقَة.
And regarding the rulings mentioned above, they refer to prescriptive rulings. (An example of taklīfī rulings: worship, punishment, etc.) And an example of prescriptive rulings: causes and conditions and their rulings. And the verification is that the scholars of uṣūl have mentioned these rules in a scattered manner without order. And from the book al-Tawḍīḥ, it is understood that every ruling needs three things: (1) the Legislator, (2) the subject, (3) the object. So the Legislator is Allah, the subject is the legally responsible person, and the object is the action of that person, whether acts of worship, punishments, or otherwise. And rulings in reality are names for the actions of the legally responsible person, for example, obligation, prohibition, resolve, or concession. Based on this investigation, rulings are attributes of actions. This was mentioned in the discussion of the Book of Allah under the title of resolve and concession. And the discussion here is about the action of the legally responsible person, i.e., the object. The discussion of the subject will come later where its importance will be explained and the objections will be mentioned. The conclusion is that the division of the early scholars is not free from leniency. As for the rulings, in any case, there are four types of rulings, i.e., the object which is the action of the legally responsible person, its types and divisions are four: First: Rights of Allah. (1) Pure rights of Allah, i.e., rulings that involve benefit for the general public, for example, veneration of the Holy House of Allah because by making it the qiblah, all people benefit, and likewise the prohibition of fornication because in it too there is benefit for the public for if it spreads, lineages would not remain safe. (The benefit is for the general public, but it is attributed to Allah as a form of glorification of Allah; otherwise, the Blessed Essence of Allah is far above deriving benefit from anything. Therefore, it is not permissible to call them the right of Allah in the sense of Him deriving benefit, nor can they be called the right of Allah in the sense of creation, because in that sense Allah is the Creator of all actions.) Second: Pure rights of the servants which are related to a specific benefit, like the prohibition of another's property; therefore it becomes permissible with the owner's permission. Third: That in which both are combined but the right of Allah predominates, like the penalty for false accusation, for in it there is the right of Allah in that it is a punishment for violating the honor of a chaste person, and the right of the servant in that it removes the disgrace of the one accused. But the right of Allah predominates, so inheritance does not apply in it, nor is pardon valid. According to al-Shāfiʿī, the right of the servant is predominant, so the rulings are reversed. Fourth: That in which both are combined but the right of the servant predominates, like retaliation, for in it there is the right of Allah, which is to free the world from corruption, and the right of the servant, which is to take vengeance for the crime against himself. And the latter is predominant because inheritance applies, compensation with money is valid through settlement, and pardon is valid. And the rights of Allah are of eight types: pure acts of worship that are not mixed with the meaning of punishment or burden, like faith and its branches, which are prayer, zakāt, fasting, and pilgrimage. They are branches of faith because they are not valid without it, while it is valid without them. And these acts of worship are three types: root, appendix, and additions. That is, in the totality of faith and its branches there are these three, not that each of them has these three. So faith is its root because it is affirmation, and attached to it is declaration, and the additions are the remaining branches. Or we say the additions in faith are the repetition of the testimony. And the example in the branches is prayer because it is the pillar of religion. Then zakāt is attached to it because the blessing of wealth is a branch of the blessing of the body. Then fasting because it is legislated to subdue the self. Then pilgrimage, then jihād. So among these branches, some are root and some are appendix. And in that case, the additions are the supererogatory acts of worship and their sunan. And complete [acts] in being obligatory like the ḥudūd penalties: the ḥadd for fornication, the ḥadd for drinking, the ḥadd for false accusation, and the ḥadd for theft.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the subject of rulings (maḥkūm bih) in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh. It begins by establishing that every ruling has three elements: the Legislator (Allah), the subject (mukallaf), and the object (act of the mukallaf). The object is the action itself, categorized as worship, punishment, or other. The focus then shifts to the classification of rulings based on whose right (ḥaqq) is involved: rights of Allah, rights of servants, or mixed. The author enumerates four categories: (1) pure rights of Allah, like the sanctity of the Kaaba and prohibition of zinā, where benefit is general and attributed to Allah for glorification; (2) pure rights of servants, like property rights, which can be waived by the owner; (3) mixed with Allah's right predominant, like the ḥadd for qadhf (false accusation), where the punishment is fixed and cannot be pardoned or inherited—contrary to Imam al-Shāfiʿī's view that the servant's right is predominant; and (4) mixed with the servant's right predominant, like qiṣāṣ, where the victim or heirs can pardon or accept compensation. The passage then details the eight types of acts that are pure rights of Allah, starting with faith (īmān) as the root, with its branches (prayer, zakāt, etc.) categorized as root, appendix, and additions, including supererogatory acts. Finally, it mentions that ḥudūd penalties are also complete obligatory acts within the rights of Allah. Throughout, the commentary stresses the Hanafi distinction between the predominance of rights and its legal consequences.

Key Terms
حكم (ḥukm): The legal rule or injunction pertaining to an action of the mukallaf.
محكوم به (maḥkūm bih): The object of the ruling, i.e., the action of the mukallaf that is subject to the legal rule.
حق (ḥaqq): A legal claim or interest, either of Allah (public/honor) or of the servant (private).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which of the following is an example of a ruling where both the right of Allah and the right of the servant are present, but the right of Allah is predominant?
A) Hadd al-qadhf (penalty for false accusation)
B) Qiṣāṣ (retaliation for murder)
C) Prohibition of zinā (fornication)
D) Respect for the Kaaba

Key Takeaway
The classification of rulings by predominant right determines waivability and inheritance; this is a foundational tool for understanding Hanafi legal reasoning.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
7 min
The Rights of Allah: Acts of Worship and Penalties
Detailing the types and internal structure of rights of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the eight types of rights of Allah mentioned in the source text and explain the threefold division of worship (root, appendix, additions) with examples from the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The rights of Allah include pure acts of worship, their branches, and penal laws, structured hierarchically from faith as the root to supererogatory acts as additions.

Having established the four categories of rights, the source text then elaborates on the rights of Allah specifically. It lists eight types, beginning with faith (īmān) as the root, with its branches of prayer, zakāt, fasting, pilgrimage, and jihād. These are arranged in a threefold structure: root, appendix, and additions. This organization helps the student understand the hierarchical priority of obligations. Additionally, the ḥudūd penalties are included as complete obligatory acts within the rights of Allah, showing that penal laws also serve public interest.

Guided Path
1
List the eight types of pure rights of Allah
From the text, identify the eight: faith (īmān), prayer (ṣalāh), zakāt, fasting (ṣawm), pilgrimage (ḥajj), jihād, and the ḥudūd penalties for zinā, shurb, qadhf, and sariqa (four penalties listed, but eight total including the five pillars?). Actually the text says eight types: faith and its branches (prayer, zakāt, fasting, pilgrimage, jihād) plus the four ḥudūd? But jihād is included, making six, plus four ḥudūd = ten? The text likely has inconsistency; we follow the text's enumeration as eight.
The text explicitly states 'rights of Allah are of eight types' but the list seems to include more; this is a textual issue, but the lesson focuses on the classification.
2
Identify the three categories within worship: root, appendix, additions
The text divides the acts of worship into root (aṣl), appendix (lāḥiq), and additions (zawāʾid). Faith is the root, the declaration (shahāda) is attached, and supererogatory acts (nawāfil) are additions.
This structure applies to the totality of faith and its branches, not to each individual act.
3
Understand the hierarchy of branches
Within the branches, prayer is the example of a root, zakāt is attached, then fasting, then hajj, then jihād. This shows priority and relationship.
The text says 'among these branches, some are root and some are appendix'.
4
Recognize that ḥudūd penalties are rights of Allah
The text states that complete duties (kulliyāt) include the ḥudūd penalties. They are rights of Allah because they serve public order.
These are distinct from worship but share the characteristic of non-waivability.

الله تعالى مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنه جَزَاءِ هَتَكَ حُرْمَةِ الْعَفِيْفِ الصَّالِحِ وَحَق الْعَبْدِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِزالَة عَارِ الْمَقْذُوفِ بِاكِنْ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى غَالِبٌ حَتَّى لا يَجْرِي فِيهِ الإرث وَالْعَفْوُ وَعِنْدَ الشافعِى حَقَّ الْعَهْدِ فِيهِ غَالِبٌ فَتَنْعَكِسُ الأَحْكَامُ وَالرَّابِعُ مَا. اجْتَمَعَافِيْهِ وَحَقُّ العَبْدِ غَالِبٌ كَالْقِصَاصِ فَإِنْ فِيْهِ حَقَّ اللَّهِ وَهُو إِخْلَاهُ الْعَالَمِ عَنِ الْفَسادِ وَحَقُّ الْعَبْدِ يُوقَوْعِ الْجَنابَةِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ وَهُوَ غَالِبٌ لِجَرَيَانِ الإِرْتِ وَصِحَةِ الاِعْتِيَاض عَنْهُ بِالْمَالِ بالصلحِ وَصحَةِ العَفْوِ وَحُقُوقُ اللهِ تَعَالَى ثَمَانِيَةُ وَأَنواع عِبَادَات خَالِصَةٌ لأَيَسُوبُها مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ وَالْمُؤْنَةِ كَالإِيْمَانِ وَفَرُوْعِهِ وَهِيَ الصَّلوةَ والزكوةُ وَالصَّوْمُ والحَج وَإِنْمَا كَانَتْ فُرُوعًا لِلإيْمَانِ لأَنْهَا لا تَصِحُ بِدُونِهِ وَهُوَ صَحِيحٌ بِدُونِهَا وَهِيَ أَي الْعِبَادَاتِ أَنْوَاعٌ ثَلَثَةٌ أَصَوْلَ وَلَوَاحِقِّ وَدَوَائِدٌ يَعْنِي أَنَّ فِي مَجْمُوع الإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِه هذه الثلاثة لا أن فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُما هذه الثلاثةُ فَالإيْمَانُ أَصلُه لااَن التصديق والملحق به الإِقْرَاهُ وَالزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ الْفُروعُ الْبَاقِيَةُ أَوْ نَقُولُ الزَّوَائِدُ فِي وَالْمُلْحِق الإِيْمَانِ هِيَ تَكْرارُ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالأمثلُ فِي الفُرُوعِ الصَّلوةَ لأَنهَا عِمَادُ الدِّينِ ثُمَّ الزَّكَوةَ مُلْحَقَةٌ بِهَا لأَنْ نِعْمَةَ الْمَالِ الْمَالُ فَرْعٌ لِنَعْمَةِ الْبَدَنِ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ لأَنَّة شرع لِقَهْرِ النَّفْسِ ثُمَّ الحَيُّ ثُمَّ الْجِهَادُ فَهَذِهِ فَرُوعٌ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهَا أَصَوْلٌ وَالْوَاحِق وَحِينَئِذٍ الزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ نَوَافِلُ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَسَنَتُهَا وَكَلُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ فِي كُوْنِهَا وَاجِرَةُ كَالْحُدُودِ فِي حَدَ الزَّنَا وَحَدَ الشَّرْبِ وَحَدَ الْقَذَفِ وَحَدُ السَّرَقَة.
And regarding the rulings mentioned above, they refer to prescriptive rulings. (An example of taklīfī rulings: worship, punishment, etc.) And an example of prescriptive rulings: causes and conditions and their rulings. And the verification is that the scholars of uṣūl have mentioned these rules in a scattered manner without order. And from the book al-Tawḍīḥ, it is understood that every ruling needs three things: (1) the Legislator, (2) the subject, (3) the object. So the Legislator is Allah, the subject is the legally responsible person, and the object is the action of that person, whether acts of worship, punishments, or otherwise. And rulings in reality are names for the actions of the legally responsible person, for example, obligation, prohibition, resolve, or concession. Based on this investigation, rulings are attributes of actions. This was mentioned in the discussion of the Book of Allah under the title of resolve and concession. And the discussion here is about the action of the legally responsible person, i.e., the object. The discussion of the subject will come later where its importance will be explained and the objections will be mentioned. The conclusion is that the division of the early scholars is not free from leniency. As for the rulings, in any case, there are four types of rulings, i.e., the object which is the action of the legally responsible person, its types and divisions are four: First: Rights of Allah. (1) Pure rights of Allah, i.e., rulings that involve benefit for the general public, for example, veneration of the Holy House of Allah because by making it the qiblah, all people benefit, and likewise the prohibition of fornication because in it too there is benefit for the public for if it spreads, lineages would not remain safe. (The benefit is for the general public, but it is attributed to Allah as a form of glorification of Allah; otherwise, the Blessed Essence of Allah is far above deriving benefit from anything. Therefore, it is not permissible to call them the right of Allah in the sense of Him deriving benefit, nor can they be called the right of Allah in the sense of creation, because in that sense Allah is the Creator of all actions.) Second: Pure rights of the servants which are related to a specific benefit, like the prohibition of another's property; therefore it becomes permissible with the owner's permission. Third: That in which both are combined but the right of Allah predominates, like the penalty for false accusation, for in it there is the right of Allah in that it is a punishment for violating the honor of a chaste person, and the right of the servant in that it removes the disgrace of the one accused. But the right of Allah predominates, so inheritance does not apply in it, nor is pardon valid. According to al-Shāfiʿī, the right of the servant is predominant, so the rulings are reversed. Fourth: That in which both are combined but the right of the servant predominates, like retaliation, for in it there is the right of Allah, which is to free the world from corruption, and the right of the servant, which is to take vengeance for the crime against himself. And the latter is predominant because inheritance applies, compensation with money is valid through settlement, and pardon is valid. And the rights of Allah are of eight types: pure acts of worship that are not mixed with the meaning of punishment or burden, like faith and its branches, which are prayer, zakāt, fasting, and pilgrimage. They are branches of faith because they are not valid without it, while it is valid without them. And these acts of worship are three types: root, appendix, and additions. That is, in the totality of faith and its branches there are these three, not that each of them has these three. So faith is its root because it is affirmation, and attached to it is declaration, and the additions are the remaining branches. Or we say the additions in faith are the repetition of the testimony. And the example in the branches is prayer because it is the pillar of religion. Then zakāt is attached to it because the blessing of wealth is a branch of the blessing of the body. Then fasting because it is legislated to subdue the self. Then pilgrimage, then jihād. So among these branches, some are root and some are appendix. And in that case, the additions are the supererogatory acts of worship and their sunan. And complete [acts] in being obligatory like the ḥudūd penalties: the ḥadd for fornication, the ḥadd for drinking, the ḥadd for false accusation, and the ḥadd for theft.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the subject of rulings (maḥkūm bih) in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh. It begins by establishing that every ruling has three elements: the Legislator (Allah), the subject (mukallaf), and the object (act of the mukallaf). The object is the action itself, categorized as worship, punishment, or other. The focus then shifts to the classification of rulings based on whose right (ḥaqq) is involved: rights of Allah, rights of servants, or mixed. The author enumerates four categories: (1) pure rights of Allah, like the sanctity of the Kaaba and prohibition of zinā, where benefit is general and attributed to Allah for glorification; (2) pure rights of servants, like property rights, which can be waived by the owner; (3) mixed with Allah's right predominant, like the ḥadd for qadhf (false accusation), where the punishment is fixed and cannot be pardoned or inherited—contrary to Imam al-Shāfiʿī's view that the servant's right is predominant; and (4) mixed with the servant's right predominant, like qiṣāṣ, where the victim or heirs can pardon or accept compensation. The passage then details the eight types of acts that are pure rights of Allah, starting with faith (īmān) as the root, with its branches (prayer, zakāt, etc.) categorized as root, appendix, and additions, including supererogatory acts. Finally, it mentions that ḥudūd penalties are also complete obligatory acts within the rights of Allah. Throughout, the commentary stresses the Hanafi distinction between the predominance of rights and its legal consequences.

Key Terms
حكم (ḥukm): The legal rule or injunction pertaining to an action of the mukallaf.
محكوم به (maḥkūm bih): The object of the ruling, i.e., the action of the mukallaf that is subject to the legal rule.
حق (ḥaqq): A legal claim or interest, either of Allah (public/honor) or of the servant (private).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following is considered the 'root' (aṣl) of worship?
A) Prayer
B) Faith (īmān)
C) Fasting
D) Jihād

Key Takeaway
The rights of Allah encompass both acts of worship and penal laws, structured hierarchically from faith as the root to supererogatory acts as additions.

Three Types of Acts of Worship: Asl, Mulhaq, Za'id
Definition of three categories of worship: asl, mulhaq, za'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between asl, mulhaq, and za'id in acts of worship and apply this classification to faith and its branches.

Core Idea
Faith's conviction is the asl, confession is mulhaq, and repetition is za'id — a three-tier structure for all worship.

In Hanafi usul, acts of worship are not monolithic but exhibit a structured hierarchy. This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar introduces three categories: asl (fundamental), mulhaq (adjunct), and za'id (supererogatory). Understanding these layers helps you see how rulings differ in weight and necessity. We will explore this using faith (iman) and the pillars of Islam as examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The text states: أَصَوْلَ وَلَوَاحِقِّ وَدَوَائِدٌ (asl, mulhaq, za'id). Note the scope: these three exist in the totality of faith and its branches, not in every individual act.
The term 'za'id' here is a variant of 'zawa'id'.
2
Apply to iman (faith)
The asl of iman is conviction (tasdiq) in the heart. The mulhaq is verbal confession (iqrar). The za'id is repeating the shahada or performing additional acts.
This shows that confession is not the core but attached.
3
Apply to furu' (branches of faith)
Among furu', prayer (salat) is the asl because it is the pillar of religion. Zakat is mulhaq to prayer as wealth is a branch of bodily health. Fasting, hajj, and jihad are further branches.
The text says: ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ لأَنَّة شرع لِقَهْرِ النَّفْسِ (then fasting for subduing the self).
4
Define za'id in furu'
The supererogatory acts (nawafil) and sunan are the za'id in furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صَحِيحٌ بِدُونِهَا وَهِيَ أَي الْعِبَادَاتِ أَنْوَاعٌ ثَلَثَةٌ أَصَوْلَ وَلَوَاحِقِّ وَدَوَائِدٌ يَعْنِي أَنَّ فِي مَجْمُوع الإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِه هذه الثلاثة لا أن فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُما هذه الثلاثةُ فَالإيْمَانُ أَصلُه لااَن التصديق والملحق به الإِقْرَاهُ وَالزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ الْفُروعُ الْبَاقِيَةُ أَوْ نَقُولُ الزَّوَائِدُ فِي وَالْمُلْحِق الإِيْمَانِ هِيَ تَكْرارُ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالأمثلُ فِي الفُرُوعِ الصَّلوةَ لأَنهَا عِمَادُ الدِّينِ ثُمَّ الزَّكَوةَ مُلْحَقَةٌ بِهَا لأَنْ نِعْمَةَ الْمَالِ الْمَالُ فَرْعٌ لِنَعْمَةِ الْبَدَنِ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ لأَنَّة شرع لِقَهْرِ النَّفْسِ ثُمَّ الحَيُّ ثُمَّ الْجِهَادُ فَهَذِهِ فَرُوعٌ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهَا أَصَوْلٌ وَالْوَاحِق وَحِينَئِذٍ الزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ نَوَافِلُ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَسَنَتُهَا وَكَلُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ فِي كُوْنِهَا وَاجِرَةُ كَالْحُدُودِ فِي حَدَ الزَّنَا وَحَدَ الشَّرْبِ وَحَدَ الْقَذَفِ وَحَدُ السَّرَقَة. والثاني حقوق العِبَادِ خَالِصة وَالثَّالِثِ مَا اجْتَمَعَا فِيهِ وَحَقُّ اللهِ غَالِبٌ كَحَدِّ الْقَذْفِ وَالرابع مَا اجْتَمَعَا فِيْهِ وَحَقُّ الْعَبْدِ غَالِبٌ كَالْقَصَاصِ. وَحَقُوقُ اللهِ تَعَالَى ثَمَانِيَةُ انْوَاعِ: خَاصُّ عِبَادَةٍ لَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ فِيْهَا وَلَا مَعْنَى الْمَؤُنَةِ كَالْإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِهِ، وَعُقُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ كَالْحُدُودِ، وَعُقُوبَاتٌ قَاصِرَةٌ كَحِرْمَانِ الْمِيْرَاثِ بِسَبَبِ الْقَتْلِ، وَحُقُوقٌ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْكَفَّارَاتِ، وَعِبَادَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْمَؤُنَةِ كَصَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ، وَمَؤُنَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ كَالْعُشْرِ، وَمَؤُنَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْخَرَاجِ.
Valid without it, and they (the acts of worship) are three types: fundamentals, adjuncts, and supererogations. Meaning that in the totality of faith and its branches there are these three, not that each of them has these three. So the foundation of faith is conviction, and annexed to it is verbal confession, and the supererogations are the remaining branches. Or we say: the supererogations in faith are repetition of the testimony. The paradigm among the branches is prayer because it is the pillar of religion; then zakat is annexed to it because the blessing of wealth is a branch of the blessing of the body; then fasting because it is prescribed for subduing the self; then pilgrimage; then jihad. So among these branches, some are foundations and some are adjuncts. On this interpretation, the supererogations are the supererogatory acts of worship and their sunan. And complete punishments in their being deterrent are like the prescribed punishments: the punishment for fornication, for drinking, for slander, and for theft. The second (category) is purely the rights of people. The third is what combines both in which the right of Allah is predominant, like the hadd punishment for slander. The fourth is what combines both in which the right of the servant is predominant, like retribution. And the rights of Allah Almighty are eight types: specific worship with no meaning of punishment in it and no meaning of maintenance like faith and its branches; complete punishments like the hudud; incomplete punishments like deprivation of inheritance due to killing; rights that oscillate between worship and punishment like expiations; worship that contains the meaning of maintenance like sadaqat al-fitr; maintenance that contains the meaning of worship like the tithe; and maintenance that contains the meaning of punishment like the land tax.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar defines two important classifications in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the categories of acts of worship (ibadat) and the categories of rights (huquq).

The author explains that acts of worship related to faith are of three kinds: asl (fundamental), lahiq (adjunct), and za'id (supererogatory). For example, in iman (faith), the heart's conviction is the asl, verbal confession is the lahiq, and repeating the shahada is a za'id. Among the branches of iman (like prayer, zakat, etc.), prayer is the asl because it is the pillar of religion; zakat is lahiq because wealth is a branch of bodily health; fasting, hajj, and jihad follow in order. The supererogatory acts are the nawafil and sunan.

The passage then turns to huquq (rights). Rights are divided into four categories: (1) purely Allah's rights, (2) purely individual rights, (3) mixed with Allah's right predominant (e.g., hadd qadhf), and (4) mixed with the individual's right predominant (e.g., qisas). The Hanafi position on hadd qadhf is that Allah's right predominates, so the punishment cannot be waived by the victim, unlike the Shafi'i view where the victim may pardon.

Finally, the text enumerates eight types of Allah's rights, including worship without penalty (faith), complete penalties (hudud), incomplete penalties (disinheritance for killing), hybrid cases (kaffarat), and financial obligations with elements of maintenance or penalty (sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, kharaj). Each classification reflects the Hanafi method of analyzing the underlying meaning (ma'na) to derive rulings.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): The fundamental or core element, e.g., conviction (tasdiq) is the asl of iman; prayer is the asl among furu'
ملحق (mulhaq): That which is annexed or attached to the asl, such as verbal confession to conviction
زائد (za'id): Supererogatory or additional element beyond the essential

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the asl among the branches of faith (furu')?
A) Zakat
B) Fasting
C) Prayer
D) Jihad

Key Takeaway
Acts of worship are hierarchically structured: asl (core obligatory), mulhaq (attached obligatory), za'id (supererogatory), affecting their legal weight.

Categories of Rights: Haqq Allah, Haqq al-'Abd, and Mixed Types
Classification of rights into four categories and eight sub-types of Allah's rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize a given right as haqq Allah, haqq al-'abd, or mixed with predominance, and list the eight types of haqq Allah.

Core Idea
Rights are either Allah's, the servant's, or mixed — where Allah's right predominates in hudud and servant's in qisas.

This passage continues to classify rights (huquq) in Islamic law. Understanding whether a right belongs to Allah or to an individual affects enforceability, waivability, and inheritance. We will examine the four categories of rights and the eight sub-types of Allah's rights, focusing on the Hanafi view that in hadd al-qadhf Allah's right predominates, unlike the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of rights
The text lists: (1) purely haqq Allah (e.g., hudud without victim), (2) purely haqq al-'abd (e.g., financial claims), (3) mixed with haqq Allah predominant (e.g., hadd qadhf), (4) mixed with haqq al-'abd predominant (e.g., qisas).
The examples are dari (exemplary) not exhaustive.
2
Understand the Hanafi dispute on hadd al-qadhf
Hanafis say Allah's right predominates, so the punishment cannot be waived by the victim. Shafi'is say the servant's right predominates, allowing pardon.
The passage states 'وحق الله غالب كحد القذف'.
3
Analyze the eight types of haqq Allah
The text enumerates eight types: (1) pure worship (iman), (2) complete punishments (hudud), (3) incomplete punishments (disinheritance), (4) oscillating between worship and punishment (kaffarat), (5) worship with maintenance (sadaqat al-fitr), (6) maintenance with worship ('ushr), (7) maintenance with punishment (kharaj).
The eighth is not explicitly listed? The text says 'ثمانية انواع' and lists seven items; possibly a scribal issue. The Urdu commentary may fill.
4
Apply the classification to examples
For each type, consider: does it involve worship, punishment, or maintenance? This determines rulings like waivability and compensation.

Source Text

صَحِيحٌ بِدُونِهَا وَهِيَ أَي الْعِبَادَاتِ أَنْوَاعٌ ثَلَثَةٌ أَصَوْلَ وَلَوَاحِقِّ وَدَوَائِدٌ يَعْنِي أَنَّ فِي مَجْمُوع الإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِه هذه الثلاثة لا أن فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُما هذه الثلاثةُ فَالإيْمَانُ أَصلُه لااَن التصديق والملحق به الإِقْرَاهُ وَالزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ الْفُروعُ الْبَاقِيَةُ أَوْ نَقُولُ الزَّوَائِدُ فِي وَالْمُلْحِق الإِيْمَانِ هِيَ تَكْرارُ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالأمثلُ فِي الفُرُوعِ الصَّلوةَ لأَنهَا عِمَادُ الدِّينِ ثُمَّ الزَّكَوةَ مُلْحَقَةٌ بِهَا لأَنْ نِعْمَةَ الْمَالِ الْمَالُ فَرْعٌ لِنَعْمَةِ الْبَدَنِ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ لأَنَّة شرع لِقَهْرِ النَّفْسِ ثُمَّ الحَيُّ ثُمَّ الْجِهَادُ فَهَذِهِ فَرُوعٌ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهَا أَصَوْلٌ وَالْوَاحِق وَحِينَئِذٍ الزَّوَائِدُ هِيَ نَوَافِلُ الْعِبَادَاتِ وَسَنَتُهَا وَكَلُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ فِي كُوْنِهَا وَاجِرَةُ كَالْحُدُودِ فِي حَدَ الزَّنَا وَحَدَ الشَّرْبِ وَحَدَ الْقَذَفِ وَحَدُ السَّرَقَة. والثاني حقوق العِبَادِ خَالِصة وَالثَّالِثِ مَا اجْتَمَعَا فِيهِ وَحَقُّ اللهِ غَالِبٌ كَحَدِّ الْقَذْفِ وَالرابع مَا اجْتَمَعَا فِيْهِ وَحَقُّ الْعَبْدِ غَالِبٌ كَالْقَصَاصِ. وَحَقُوقُ اللهِ تَعَالَى ثَمَانِيَةُ انْوَاعِ: خَاصُّ عِبَادَةٍ لَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ فِيْهَا وَلَا مَعْنَى الْمَؤُنَةِ كَالْإِيْمَانِ وَفُرُوعِهِ، وَعُقُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ كَالْحُدُودِ، وَعُقُوبَاتٌ قَاصِرَةٌ كَحِرْمَانِ الْمِيْرَاثِ بِسَبَبِ الْقَتْلِ، وَحُقُوقٌ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْكَفَّارَاتِ، وَعِبَادَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْمَؤُنَةِ كَصَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ، وَمَؤُنَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ كَالْعُشْرِ، وَمَؤُنَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْخَرَاجِ.
Valid without it, and they (the acts of worship) are three types: fundamentals, adjuncts, and supererogations. Meaning that in the totality of faith and its branches there are these three, not that each of them has these three. So the foundation of faith is conviction, and annexed to it is verbal confession, and the supererogations are the remaining branches. Or we say: the supererogations in faith are repetition of the testimony. The paradigm among the branches is prayer because it is the pillar of religion; then zakat is annexed to it because the blessing of wealth is a branch of the blessing of the body; then fasting because it is prescribed for subduing the self; then pilgrimage; then jihad. So among these branches, some are foundations and some are adjuncts. On this interpretation, the supererogations are the supererogatory acts of worship and their sunan. And complete punishments in their being deterrent are like the prescribed punishments: the punishment for fornication, for drinking, for slander, and for theft. The second (category) is purely the rights of people. The third is what combines both in which the right of Allah is predominant, like the hadd punishment for slander. The fourth is what combines both in which the right of the servant is predominant, like retribution. And the rights of Allah Almighty are eight types: specific worship with no meaning of punishment in it and no meaning of maintenance like faith and its branches; complete punishments like the hudud; incomplete punishments like deprivation of inheritance due to killing; rights that oscillate between worship and punishment like expiations; worship that contains the meaning of maintenance like sadaqat al-fitr; maintenance that contains the meaning of worship like the tithe; and maintenance that contains the meaning of punishment like the land tax.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar defines two important classifications in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the categories of acts of worship (ibadat) and the categories of rights (huquq).

The author explains that acts of worship related to faith are of three kinds: asl (fundamental), lahiq (adjunct), and za'id (supererogatory). For example, in iman (faith), the heart's conviction is the asl, verbal confession is the lahiq, and repeating the shahada is a za'id. Among the branches of iman (like prayer, zakat, etc.), prayer is the asl because it is the pillar of religion; zakat is lahiq because wealth is a branch of bodily health; fasting, hajj, and jihad follow in order. The supererogatory acts are the nawafil and sunan.

The passage then turns to huquq (rights). Rights are divided into four categories: (1) purely Allah's rights, (2) purely individual rights, (3) mixed with Allah's right predominant (e.g., hadd qadhf), and (4) mixed with the individual's right predominant (e.g., qisas). The Hanafi position on hadd qadhf is that Allah's right predominates, so the punishment cannot be waived by the victim, unlike the Shafi'i view where the victim may pardon.

Finally, the text enumerates eight types of Allah's rights, including worship without penalty (faith), complete penalties (hudud), incomplete penalties (disinheritance for killing), hybrid cases (kaffarat), and financial obligations with elements of maintenance or penalty (sadaqat al-fitr, ushr, kharaj). Each classification reflects the Hanafi method of analyzing the underlying meaning (ma'na) to derive rulings.

Key Terms
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right that belongs solely to Allah, often involving public interest and not waivable by individuals
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right that belongs to an individual, such as claims for financial compensation or retaliation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which category includes hadd al-qadhf?
A) Purely haqq Allah
B) Purely haqq al-'abd
C) Mixed with haqq Allah predominant
D) Mixed with haqq al-'abd predominant

Key Takeaway
The classification of rights into four categories, with the predominance of haqq Allah or haqq al-'abd, determines whether a penalty can be waived or not, as seen in hadd al-qadhf.

Classification of Punishments and Mixed Rights
Taxonomy of punishments and mixed rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given legal obligation as a complete punishment, incomplete punishment, or mixed right according to the Hanafi taxonomy, and explain the reasoning behind each classification.

Core Idea
Hudud are complete punishments; deprivation of inheritance is incomplete; kaffarat mix worship and punishment.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar provides a taxonomy that goes beyond the simple ibada-uquba divide. It introduces a nuanced framework distinguishing complete punishments (uqubat kamilah), incomplete punishments (uqubat qasirah), and mixed categories where obligations participate in worship, punishment, and maintenance. Understanding this classification helps a faqih accurately apply the correct legal rules to each obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary categories
The passage divides obligations into complete punishments, incomplete punishments, mixed worship-punishment rights, and three types mixing maintenance (ma'una) with worship/punishment.
The mixed categories are: worship with maintenance meaning (sadaqat al-fitr), maintenance with worship meaning (ushr), and maintenance with punishment meaning (kharaj).
2
Understand the rationale for each classification
For each example, the author gives a reason: hudud are complete as fixed; deprivation of inheritance is incomplete as less than qisas and applies to minors; kaffarat are mixed because worship acts imposed as penalty; sadaqat al-fitr is worship with maintenance meaning; ushr is maintenance with worship; kharaj is maintenance with punishment.
Note the key phrases: 'fihi ma'na al-ibada' vs 'fihi ma'na al-uquba' vs 'fihi ma'na al-ma'una'.
3
Apply the taxonomy to unlisted cases
Using the same reasoning, classify, e.g., diyah as an incomplete punishment (like deprivation of inheritance) because it is less than qisas and applies to minors in some cases.
Be careful: diyah is not explicitly in the passage, but the reasoning can be extended.
4
Derive legal consequences
Note that incomplete punishments apply even to minors, while complete punishments require maturity; kaffarat require intention like worship but are triggered by sin.
This affects how the obligation is implemented (e.g., a minor can be deprived of inheritance but not stoned).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعُقُوبَاتٌ كَامِلَةٌ كَالْحُدُودِ وَهِيَ حَدُّ الزِّنَا وَحَدُّ الشُّرْبِ وَحَدُّ الْقَذْفِ وَحَدُّ السَّرِقَةِ. وَعُقُوبَاتٌ قَاصِرَةٌ مِثْلُ حِرْمَانِ الْمِيرَاثِ بِسَبَبِ قَتْلِ الْمُوْرِثِ فَإِنَّ الْعُقُوبَةَ الْكَامِلَةَ هِيَ الْقِصَاصُ فِي حَقِّهِ وَهَذَا قَاصِرٌ مِنْهُ وَلِهَذَا يُجْزَى بِهِ الصَّبِيُّ. وَحُقُوقٌ دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَهُمَا أَيْ بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْكَفَّارَاتِ فَإِنَّ فِيهَا الْعِبَادَةَ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهَا تُؤَدَّى بِالصَّوْمِ وَالْإِعْتَاقِ وَالْإِطْعَامِ وَالْكِسْوَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهَا لَمْ تَجِبِ ابْتِدَاءً بَلْ وَجَبَتْ جَزَاءً عَلَى أَفْعَالٍ مُحَرَّمَةٍ صَدَرَتْ عَنِ الْعِبَادِ. وَعِبَادَةٌ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْمَئُونَةِ كَصَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ فَإِنَّهَا فِي أَصْلِهَا عِبَادَةٌ مُلْحَقَةٌ بِالزَّكَاةِ وَلِهَذَا شُرِطَ لَهَا الْغِنَى وَلَكِنْ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْمَئُونَةِ وَلِهَذَا تَجِبُ عَمَّنْ يَمُونُهُ مِمَّنْ يُنْفِقُ عَلَيْهِ كَنَفْسِهِ وَأَوْلَادِهِ الصِّغَارِ وَعَبِيدِهِ الْمَمْلُوكِينَ فَإِنَّهُ لَمَّا مَانَهُمْ بِالنَّفَقَةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَمُونَهُمْ بِالصَّدَقَةِ أَيْضًا لِدَفْعِ الْبَلَاءِ. وَمَئُونَةٌ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ كَالْعُشْرِ فَإِنَّهُ فِي نَفْسِهِ مَئُونَةٌ لِلْأَرْضِ الَّتِي يَزْرَعُهَا وَلَوْ لَمْ يُعْطِ الْعُشْرَ لِلسُّلْطَانِ لَأَسْتَرَدَّ الْأَرْضِ مِنْهُ وَأَحَالَهَا بِيَدِ آخَرَ وَلَكِنْ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ يُصْرَفُ مَصَارِفَ الزَّكَاةِ وَلَا يَجِبُ إِلَّا عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ فَحُمِلَ فِعْلُهُمُ الْمُزَارَعَةَ عَلَى كَسْبِ الْحَلَالِ الطَّيِّبِ. وَمَئُونَةٌ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ كَالْخَرَاجِ فَإِنَّهُ فِي نَفْسِهِ مَئُونَةٌ لِلْأَرْضِ الَّتِي يَزْرَعُهَا وَإِلَّا اسْتَرَدَّهَا السُّلْطَانُ مِنْهُ وَأَحَالَهَا بِيَدِ آخَرَ وَلَكِنْ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ عَلَى الْفَلَّاحِينَ الَّذِينَ اسْتَغْلُّوا زِرَاعَةَ الدُّنْيَا وَنَبَذُوا الْآخِرَةَ وَرَاءَ ظُهُورِهِمْ.
And complete punishments like the hudud: the hadd for zina, hadd for drinking, hadd for qadhf, and hadd for theft. And incomplete punishments like deprivation of inheritance due to killing the testator; for the complete punishment for him is qisas, and this (deprivation) is less than that, hence it is applied to the minor. And rights that revolve between the two, i.e., between worship and punishment, like kaffarat; for in them is worship from the aspect that they are performed by fasting, freeing slaves, feeding, and clothing, and the meaning of punishment from the aspect that they are not obligatory initially but become obligatory as a recompense for prohibited actions committed by servants. And an act of worship that contains the meaning of maintenance/expense, like sadaqat al-fitr; for it is in origin an act of worship attached to zakat, and for this reason wealth is a condition for it, but it has the meaning of maintenance; hence it is obligatory for those whom one supports, such as himself, his young children, and his owned slaves; because when he maintains them with spending and guardianship, it is necessary that he maintain them with sadaqah as well to repel calamity. And a maintenance that contains the meaning of worship, like ushr; for it is in itself a maintenance for the land he cultivates; and if he does not pay the ushr to the ruler, the ruler would take the land from him and hand it over to another; but it also has the meaning of worship in that it is distributed to the recipients of zakat and is obligatory only on Muslims, so their act of cultivation is considered as earning lawful and good sustenance. And a maintenance that contains the meaning of punishment, like kharaj; for it is in itself a maintenance for the land he cultivates; otherwise the ruler would take the land from him and hand it over to another; but it has the meaning of punishment in that it is obligatory upon the farmers who have profited from worldly cultivation and have cast the Hereafter behind their backs.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on Nur al-Anwar classifies legal obligations beyond the basic categories. The author presents a taxonomy of punishments and a set of obligations that share characteristics of both worship (ibada) and punishment (uquba) or maintenance (ma'una). The text first distinguishes complete punishments (uqubat kamilah) like the fixed hadd penalties for zina, drinking, slander, and theft from incomplete punishments (uqubat qasirah) like the denial of inheritance to a killer. The incomplete punishment applies even to minors because it is less severe than qisas. Next, rights that are intermediate between worship and punishment are discussed, such as expiations (kaffarat). They have the form of worship (fasting, freeing slaves, feeding) but are imposed as a consequence of prohibited acts, giving them a penal character. The passage then examines three types of obligations that mix the concept of 'ma'una' (maintenance/expense) with worship or punishment. Sadaqat al-fitr is primarily worship similar to zakat (requiring wealth) but also carries the sense of maintenance because it is due on behalf of those whom one supports. Ushr (the tenth on land produce) is a maintenance charge on land but also an act of worship since its proceeds go to zakat recipients and it is only required from Muslims, implying the cultivation is lawful. Kharaj (land tax on non-Muslims) is also a maintenance charge but has a punitive aspect, being imposed on those who focus on worldly agriculture and neglect the afterlife.

Key Terms
عقوبة كاملة (uqubat kamilah): A complete punishment that is a fixed hadd penalty.
عقوبة قاصرة (uqubat qasirah): An incomplete punishment that is less severe than qisas, such as deprivation of inheritance.
حق دائرة بين العبادة والعقوبة (haqq da'irat bayna al-ibada wa al-uquba): A right that partakes of both worship and punishment, like kaffarat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of an incomplete punishment (uqubat qasirah)?
A) Hadd for theft
B) Deprivation of inheritance due to killing the testator
C) Paying kaffarah for breaking an oath
D) Paying ushr on agricultural land

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi taxonomy distinguishes complete punishments (hudud), incomplete punishments, and mixed categories where obligations combine worship, punishment, or maintenance meanings.

Pure Divine and Servant Rights in Hanafi Usul
Defining pure divine and pure servant rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between rights that are purely for Allah (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi) and rights purely for servants (huquq al-ibad), and state the Hanafi position on their enforcement.

Core Idea
Allah's rights are enforced by the ruler; servant's rights can be waived.

In Hanafi usul, rights are classified by their beneficiary. Some rights are purely Allah's, established without human liability. Others are purely between servants, subject to their discretion. This lesson unpacks the first and last categories from the Nur al-Anwar commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories: pure divine vs pure servant
Read the passage and note the two main divisions: 'right that stands by itself' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi) and 'rights of servants' (huquq al-ibad).
2
Analyze the definition of haqq qa'im bi nafsihi
This right is established by itself, not attached to a servant's dhimma, and Allah retains it through the sultan. Examples: khums of booty and minerals.
3
Examine uqubat qasira
Punishments confined to the Hereafter, like deprivation from inheritance for killing. Though not enforced in this world, they have worldly effects and are a divine right.
Note: Even a minor can be subject to this penalty.
4
Contrast with servant's rights
Servant's rights are personal claims like compensation for destroyed property, blood money, contractual rights. They can be waived by the individual.
5
Apply the classification
Given a new scenario (e.g., a will), determine whether the right is divine or servant's based on its characteristics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو
نور الانوار جلد سوم 33
茶
عَلَى لَلْقَاءِ الَّذِينَ اسْتَغْلُوْا يَزْرَاعَةِ الدُّنْيَا وَنَبَدَ الآخِرَةَ وَرَاء ظُهُورِهِمْ وَحَقٌّ قَائِمٌ
بِنَفْسِهِ أَيْ ثَابِتْ بِذَاتِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِذِمَّةِ الْعَبْدِ شَيْءٌ مِنْهُ حَتَّى يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ
أَدَانَهُ بَلْ اسْتِبْنَاهُ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَأَجَلِ نَفْسِهِ وَتَوَلَّى أَخَذَهُ وَقِسْمَتَهُ مَنْ كَانَ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَهُوَ السَّلْطَانُ وعقوبات قاصرة الخ اور عقوبات قاصرہ جیسے میراث سے محرومی (۳) سورت کے قتل ترجمہ و تشریح کرنے کے سب سے کیونکہ اس کے حق میں عقوبت کا ملہ تو قصاص ہے اور یہ ( محرومی) اس سے کمتر ہے اس وجہ سے نا بالغ بچے پر بھی یہ سزا نافذ کی جاتی ہے۔
وحقوق دَائِرَةٌ بَيْنَهُمَا (۳) ایسے حقوق جو دونوں کے درمیان دائر ہوں یعنی عبادت اور عقوبت کے در میان دائر ہوں کا کفارات جیسے کفارا تمہیں اس حیثیت سے کہ اس میں عبادت کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ روزہ رکھ کر غلام آزاد کر کے اور کھانا کھلا کر اور کپڑے دے کر ادا کئے جاتے ہیں اور عقوبت کے معنی اس حیثیت سے پائے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ ابتدہ اور واجب نہیں ہوتے بلکہ بطور جزاء کے واجب ہوتے ہیں بندون کے اسے افعال پر جو حرام ہوتے ہیں اور بندوں سے صادر ہوتے ہیں۔
وعِبَادَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنَى المَؤنَةِ (۳) ایسی عبادت جس میں مؤنت کے معنی شامل ہوتے ہیں یعنی محنت بھی اور بوجھ بھی ہوتا ہے كصدقة الفطر جیسے صدقہ فطر کیونکہ صدقہ فطر میں اصل تو عبادت ہے جو ز کوۃ کے ساتھ ملحق ہے اسی وجہ سے (زکوۃ کی شرط) غنی مالدار ہونا مشروط ہے لیکن اس میں مونت ( محنت و بوجھ) کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں اس وجہ سے صدقہ فطر ان لوگوں کی طرف سے بھی دینا پڑتا ہے جو لوگ اس کی کفالت و پرورش میں رہتے ہوں اور جن پر یہ خرچ کرتا ہے اسی طرح پر جیسے کہ اپنے نفس اور اپنی چھوٹی اولاد پر اپنے مملوک غلاموں پر کیونکہ جب ان نے مونت برداشت کی ان کے نفقہ اور ولایت میں تو واجب ہوا کہ ان کی کفالت صدقہ میں بھی کرے تاکہ مصائب ویلا دور ہوں۔
وَمَؤُنَةٌ فِيْهَا مَعْنى الْعِبَادَةِ (1) ایسی مونت (بار ذمہ داری) جس میں معنی عبادت بھی موجود ہوں جیسے مشرکیونکہ عشر فی فی نفسہ اس زمین کی بار زمہ داری ہے جس کی زراعت کرتا ہے کیونکہ اگر یہ شخص عشر کی ادائیگی نہ کرے گا تو بادشاہ وقت اس سے عشری زمین واپس لے لیگا اور دوسرے کے ہاتھ میں حوالہ کر دیگا لیکن اس میں عبارت کے معنی بھی موجود ہیں کیونکہ اس کے مصارف وہی ہیں جو ز کوۃ کے مصارف ہیں اور عشر صرف مسلمانوں پر واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا ان کا فعل زراعت حلال پاک طبیب روزی کمانے پر محمول کیا گیا ہے۔ وَمَؤنَةٌ فِيهَا مَعْنَى الْعُقُوبَةَ مَا الْجَرَاج (۷) ایسی مونت (بار ذمہ داری) جس میں معنی عقوبت پائے جاتے ہوں جیسے خراج یہ بھی در حقیت اس زمین کا ٹیکس ہے جس کی یہ زراعت کرتا ہے اور اگر زمین جوت ہو کر پیداوار نہ کرے گا تو بادشاہ اس سے زمین کو واپس لے لے گا ارودوسرے کے ہاتھ حوالہ کر دیگا لیکن

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو
نور الانوار جلد سوم
ساتھ ہی اس میں عقوبت کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ فقط کفار پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو لوگ صرف دنیا کی سمیتی میں مصروف ہیں اور آخرت کی کھیتی کو پس پشت ڈال رکھا ہے۔
وَحَق قَائِمٌ بِنَفْسِهِ (۸) اور ایسا حق جو بذات خود قائم ہو یعنی وہ حق خود ہی ثابت ہو بغیر اس کے کہ بندہ کے ذمہ کے ساتھ کوئی چیز متعلق ہو حتی کہ اس پر اس کی ادائے گی واجب ہے بلکہ خود حق تعالی نے اس کو اپنے لئے باقی رکھا ہے اور دنیا میں اس کو لینے وصول کرنے) اور تقسیم کرنے کے لئے اپنا خلیفہ اور نائب مقرر
فرما دیا ہے اور وہ بادشاہ ہے۔ كَخَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ وَالْمَعَادِنِ فَإِنَّ الْجِهَادَ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُصَابُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَنِيمَةُ كُلُّها لِله تَعَالَى لَكِنْ أَوْجَبَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَخْمَاسِهِ لِلْغَائِمِيْنَ مِنْةٌ مِنْهُ وَأَبْقَى الْحُمْسَ لِنَفْسِهِ وَكَذَ الْمَعَادِنُ فَإِنَّهَا اسْمٌ خَلَقَهُ اللَّهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ مِنْ الذَّهَبِ وَالفِصْةِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ كُلَّهُ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلَكِنَّ الله تَعَالَى أَحَلُ لِلْوَاجِدِ أَوْ لِلْمَالِكِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَخْمَاسه مِنْةُ مِنْه وَفَضْلاً وَحَقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ كَبَدَلَ الْمُتَلِفَاتِ وَالْمَعْصُوبَاتِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا مِنَ الدِّيَةِ وَمِلْكِ الْمَبِيعِ وَالثَّمَنِ وَمِلْكِ النِّكَاحِ وَنَحْوِ
Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary, Nur al-Anwar Volume 3, page 33. Upon those who engross themselves in cultivation of the world and cast the Hereafter behind their backs. And a right that stands by itself, i.e., it is established by its own essence without anything from it being attached to the servant's liability such that he must fulfill it; rather, Allah the Exalted has retained it for Himself and He Himself undertook its collection and distribution through whoever is on earth, and he is the sultan. 'And punishments that are confined [to the Hereafter]' such as deprivation from inheritance and [the punishment for] intentional homicide? Because in its case, the punishment is retaliation, and this (deprivation) is less than that, for this reason it is also implemented on a minor. 'And rights that revolve between the two' (i.e., between worship and punishment) such as expiations, because they have the meaning of worship since they are performed by fasting, freeing a slave, feeding, and clothing; and they have the meaning of punishment because they are not obligatory initially but become obligatory as a penalty for the forbidden acts that servants commit. 'And a worship that contains the meaning of burden' such as sadaqat al-fitr, because sadaqat al-fitr is essentially worship attached to zakat; thus the condition of wealth is required. But it also contains the meaning of burden, therefore it must be given on behalf of those whom one supports, such as one's self, young children, and slaves, because one bears the burden of their maintenance. 'And a burden that contains the meaning of worship' such as 'ushr, because it is a burden on the land one cultivates; if one does not pay it, the ruler will take the land and give it to another. But it also contains the meaning of worship because its expenditures are the same as zakat, and 'ushr is only obligatory on Muslims. 'And a burden that contains the meaning of punishment' such as kharaj, because it is a tax on the land; if the land does not produce, the ruler will take the land. Along with that, it contains the meaning of punishment because it is obligatory only on disbelievers who are engrossed in worldly gains. 'And a right that stands by itself' (eighth category): a right that is established by itself, without anything being attached to the servant's liability; rather, Allah has retained it for Himself and appointed His vicegerent on earth for its collection and distribution, and he is the sultan. Like khums of booty and minerals: jihad is a right of Allah, so the property acquired (booty) should all be for Allah, but He obligated four-fifths for the fighters as a favor from Him and kept the fifth for Himself. Similarly for minerals: they are whatever Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so they should all be for Allah, but Allah has made four-fifths permissible for the finder or owner as a favor. And rights of servants are like compensation for destroyed property, usurped goods, blood money, ownership of sold item and price, ownership of marriage, etc.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of rights in Hanafi usul. It begins by defining a 'right that stands by itself' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi) as a right that is not attached to anyone's liability but is directly established by Allah, such as spoils of war (ghanima) and minerals. The commentary then explains that the state (sultan) acts as Allah's deputy in collecting and distributing such rights. The Urdu section clarifies that punishments confined to the Hereafter (uqūbāt qāṣira) include deprivation from inheritance, and even a minor can be subject to some penalties. Next, the text discusses 'rights revolving between the two' (i.e., between worship and punishment), like kaffarat (expiation), which combine elements of worship (fasting, feeding) and punishment (they are triggered by sin). Then come categories of acts that mix worship and burden (ma'ūna), such as sadaqat al-fitr, which is worship but also a financial burden on the provider; and burden with worship meaning, like 'ushr (tithe on land), which is a duty but has worship-like benefits. Finally, burden with punishment meaning, like kharaj (land tax on non-Muslims), which is a financial imposition with punitive aspect. The passage concludes with examples of servants' rights (huqūq al-‘ibād), including compensation for damages and contractual rights. The structure follows the matn's classification of rights into four categories: purely divine, mixed, and purely human, with subcategories. The Hanafi school emphasizes that Allah's rights are often enforced by the ruler, while servants' rights are individually enforceable.

Key Terms
حَقٌّ قَائِمٌ بِنَفْسِهِ (haqqun qā'imun bi nafsihi): A right that is established by itself without being attached to any person's liability; it is directly retained by Allah and implemented through His deputy, the sultan.
عُقُوبَاتٌ قَاصِرَةٌ (uqūbātun qāṣirah): Punishments that are confined to the Hereafter and not imposed in this world, such as deprivation from inheritance for killing.
حُقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ (ḥuqūq al-‘ibād): Rights that belong to individual servants, such as compensation for damages, blood money, and contractual ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a 'right that stands by itself' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi) according to the commentary?
A) Compensation for destroyed property
B) Khums of booty
C) Sadaqat al-fitr
D) Blood money (diyah)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a 'right that stands by itself' is a divine right enforced by the ruler, while servant's rights are personal and waivable.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Mixed Rights: Worship, Burden, and Punishment
Defining mixed rights with worship, burden, and punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify mixed rights (rights revolving between worship and punishment, worship with burden, burden with worship, burden with punishment) and explain the dual aspects.

Core Idea
Mixed rights combine worship, punishment, or burden; expiation is both worship and punishment, sadaqat al-fitr is worship with burden, 'ushr is burden with worship, kharaj is burden with punishment.

Many obligations in Islamic law are not purely one type but combine elements of worship, punishment, and financial burden. This lesson unpacks the four mixed categories from the Nur al-Anwar commentary, showing how each blends two aspects.

Guided Path
1
List the four mixed categories from the text
Identify each: rights revolving between worship and punishment (kaffarat), worship with burden (sadaqat al-fitr), burden with worship ('ushr), burden with punishment (kharaj).
2
For each, determine the dominant aspect
The commentary explains the dual nature. For kaffarat: worship (fasting, feeding) and punishment (triggered by sin). For sadaqat al-fitr: worship (attached to zakat) and burden (must be paid for dependents). For 'ushr: burden (land tax) and worship (zakat-like expenditure, only on Muslims). For kharaj: burden (land tax) and punishment (only on non-Muslims).
3
Understand the practical implications
These classifications affect rulings: e.g., kaffarat is not initially obligatory but becomes so upon violation; sadaqat al-fitr must be paid for dependents; 'ushr is obligatory on Muslims; kharaj is imposed on non-Muslims.
4
Compare and contrast these categories
Note similarities: all have a financial component. Differences: the dominant aspect (worship vs burden vs punishment) affects who must pay and when.
5
Apply the classification to a new example
Given a case like 'zakat on livestock', classify it based on its characteristics using the framework.

ساتھ ہی اس میں عقوبت کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ فقط کفار پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو لوگ صرف دنیا کی سمیتی میں مصروف ہیں اور آخرت کی کھیتی کو پس پشت ڈال رکھا ہے۔
وَحَق قَائِمٌ بِنَفْسِهِ (۸) اور ایسا حق جو بذات خود قائم ہو یعنی وہ حق خود ہی ثابت ہو بغیر اس کے کہ بندہ کے ذمہ کے ساتھ کوئی چیز متعلق ہو حتی کہ اس پر اس کی ادائے گی واجب ہے بلکہ خود حق تعالی نے اس کو اپنے لئے باقی رکھا ہے اور دنیا میں اس کو لینے وصول کرنے) اور تقسیم کرنے کے لئے اپنا خلیفہ اور نائب مقرر
فرما دیا ہے اور وہ بادشاہ ہے۔ كَخَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ وَالْمَعَادِنِ فَإِنَّ الْجِهَادَ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُصَابُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَنِيمَةُ كُلُّها لِله تَعَالَى لَكِنْ أَوْجَبَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَخْمَاسِهِ لِلْغَائِمِيْنَ مِنْةٌ مِنْهُ وَأَبْقَى الْحُمْسَ لِنَفْسِهِ وَكَذَ الْمَعَادِنُ فَإِنَّهَا اسْمٌ خَلَقَهُ اللَّهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ مِنْ الذَّهَبِ وَالفِصْةِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ كُلَّهُ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلَكِنَّ الله تَعَالَى أَحَلُ لِلْوَاجِدِ أَوْ لِلْمَالِكِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَخْمَاسه مِنْةُ مِنْه وَفَضْلاً وَحَقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ كَبَدَلَ الْمُتَلِفَاتِ وَالْمَعْصُوبَاتِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا مِنَ الدِّيَةِ وَمِلْكِ الْمَبِيعِ وَالثَّمَنِ وَمِلْكِ النِّكَاحِ وَنَحْوِ
Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary, Nur al-Anwar Volume 3, page 33. Upon those who engross themselves in cultivation of the world and cast the Hereafter behind their backs. And a right that stands by itself, i.e., it is established by its own essence without anything from it being attached to the servant's liability such that he must fulfill it; rather, Allah the Exalted has retained it for Himself and He Himself undertook its collection and distribution through whoever is on earth, and he is the sultan. 'And punishments that are confined [to the Hereafter]' such as deprivation from inheritance and [the punishment for] intentional homicide? Because in its case, the punishment is retaliation, and this (deprivation) is less than that, for this reason it is also implemented on a minor. 'And rights that revolve between the two' (i.e., between worship and punishment) such as expiations, because they have the meaning of worship since they are performed by fasting, freeing a slave, feeding, and clothing; and they have the meaning of punishment because they are not obligatory initially but become obligatory as a penalty for the forbidden acts that servants commit. 'And a worship that contains the meaning of burden' such as sadaqat al-fitr, because sadaqat al-fitr is essentially worship attached to zakat; thus the condition of wealth is required. But it also contains the meaning of burden, therefore it must be given on behalf of those whom one supports, such as one's self, young children, and slaves, because one bears the burden of their maintenance. 'And a burden that contains the meaning of worship' such as 'ushr, because it is a burden on the land one cultivates; if one does not pay it, the ruler will take the land and give it to another. But it also contains the meaning of worship because its expenditures are the same as zakat, and 'ushr is only obligatory on Muslims. 'And a burden that contains the meaning of punishment' such as kharaj, because it is a tax on the land; if the land does not produce, the ruler will take the land. Along with that, it contains the meaning of punishment because it is obligatory only on disbelievers who are engrossed in worldly gains. 'And a right that stands by itself' (eighth category): a right that is established by itself, without anything being attached to the servant's liability; rather, Allah has retained it for Himself and appointed His vicegerent on earth for its collection and distribution, and he is the sultan. Like khums of booty and minerals: jihad is a right of Allah, so the property acquired (booty) should all be for Allah, but He obligated four-fifths for the fighters as a favor from Him and kept the fifth for Himself. Similarly for minerals: they are whatever Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so they should all be for Allah, but Allah has made four-fifths permissible for the finder or owner as a favor. And rights of servants are like compensation for destroyed property, usurped goods, blood money, ownership of sold item and price, ownership of marriage, etc.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of rights in Hanafi usul. It begins by defining a 'right that stands by itself' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi) as a right that is not attached to anyone's liability but is directly established by Allah, such as spoils of war (ghanima) and minerals. The commentary then explains that the state (sultan) acts as Allah's deputy in collecting and distributing such rights. The Urdu section clarifies that punishments confined to the Hereafter (uqūbāt qāṣira) include deprivation from inheritance, and even a minor can be subject to some penalties. Next, the text discusses 'rights revolving between the two' (i.e., between worship and punishment), like kaffarat (expiation), which combine elements of worship (fasting, feeding) and punishment (they are triggered by sin). Then come categories of acts that mix worship and burden (ma'ūna), such as sadaqat al-fitr, which is worship but also a financial burden on the provider; and burden with worship meaning, like 'ushr (tithe on land), which is a duty but has worship-like benefits. Finally, burden with punishment meaning, like kharaj (land tax on non-Muslims), which is a financial imposition with punitive aspect. The passage concludes with examples of servants' rights (huqūq al-‘ibād), including compensation for damages and contractual rights. The structure follows the matn's classification of rights into four categories: purely divine, mixed, and purely human, with subcategories. The Hanafi school emphasizes that Allah's rights are often enforced by the ruler, while servants' rights are individually enforceable.

Key Terms
كفَّارَات (kaffārāt): Expiation acts that serve both as worship (since they involve devotional acts) and as punishment (since they are triggered by violations).
مَؤنَة (ma'ūnah): A burden or financial obligation that may have elements of worship or punishment associated with it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, which of the following is an example of 'burden that contains the meaning of punishment'?
A) Kaffarat for breaking an oath
B) Sadaqat al-fitr
C) 'Ushr
D) Kharaj

Key Takeaway
Mixed rights in Hanafi usul blend worship, burden, and punishment; each combination has distinct rulings based on its dominant aspect.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
