اور اس سے قول لاوجود ا کی قید سے شرط خارج ہو گئی کالا حصان جیسا کہ احصان زنا کے سلسلے میں کیونکہ احصان زانی کے لئے رحیم کئے جانے کی علامت ہے اور احصان یہ ہے کہ زانی مسلمان، آزاده مکلف اور شادی شدہ ہو اور شادی میں نکاح صحیح ہوا ہو پس مکلف ہونے کی شرط تمام احکام کے لئے یکساں ہیں اور حریت (آزاد ہونے) کی قید اس لئے لگائی گئی ہے تاکہ اس پر سزا مکمل جاری ہو سکے ان شرطوں میں سے خاص شرطیں دو ہیں اول مسلمان ہونا دوم نکاح صحیح سے وطی کر چکا ہو ا ہو ناباقی آزاد ہونا مکلف ہو تا تو عام شرطیں ہیں۔ دوسرے احکام کے لئے بھی یہ شرطیں ضروری ہیں مگر حد زنا جاری ہونے کے لئے خاص شرطیں یہ دونوں ہیں یعنی مسلمان ہونا اور نکاح صحیح سے وطی کرنا اور صفت احسان کو علت نہیں قرار دیا ہے بلکہ علامت کہا ہے کیونکہ زنا ثابت ہو جانے پر اس زنا کی رحم کا علت ہونا ( شرط کی مانند ) ہے اس پر موقوف نہیں رہتا کہ بعد میں احصان متحقق ہو جائے بلکہ اگر زنا کے بعد احسان پایا گیا تو اس سے رحیم ثابت ہی نہیں ہوتا اور احسان کا علمیتی یا سبب نہ ہونا ظاہری ہی ہے اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ احسان سے مراد در حقیقت زنا کی
And the fourth is the sign (alamah), which is that by which existence is known without a requirement of obligation or existence being attached to it. His statement 'what makes existence known' is a precaution against the cause (sabab), because the cause necessitates (muqtadī), not just makes known. And his statement 'without a requirement of obligation being attached to it' is a precaution against the 'illah (effective cause), and 'nor existence' is a precaution against the condition (shart). Like ihsan in the chapter of zina, for it is a sign for stoning (rajm). And it (ihsan) is the description of the fornicator being free, Muslim, legally responsible, and having had intercourse in a valid marriage once. So legal responsibility (taklif) is a condition in all rulings, and freedom (hurriyyah) is for completing the punishment. And the essential part here is Islam and intercourse in a valid marriage. And we only made it a sign, not a condition, because when zina is established, its character as a cause for stoning does not depend on an ihsan that occurs after it. For if ihsan occurred after zina, stoning would not be proven by its existence. And it is clear that it is not an 'illah or sabab. So it is learned that it (ihsan) refers to a state in the fornicator by which zina in that state becomes obligating of stoning. This is the meaning of its being a sign. And this is according to some later scholars. But the choice of the majority is that it is a condition for the obligation of stoning, because the condition is that on which the existence of the ruling depends, and ihsan is of this level, since zina does not necessitate stoning without it, like theft does not necessitate amputation without the nisab. Consequently, its witnesses do not guarantee (the blood money) if they retract in any case. A branch based on considering ihsan as a sign: meaning if the witnesses of ihsan retract after stoning, they do not guarantee the blood-money of the stoned person in any case, i.e., whether they retract alone or with the witnesses of zina as well, because it is a sign; no obligation or existence is attached to it, and it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it. And the condition (with its particle) combines both aspects... (repetition of earlier rule). And the fourth division is the sign... (Urdu commentary follows summarizing the same).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth type of connection in usul: the 'alamah (sign/marker). Unlike a cause (sabab) that necessitates the ruling, an 'illah that is the effective cause, or a shart upon which the ruling depends, a sign merely indicates that the ruling exists without any causal link. The example given is ihsan (being muhsan) in the law of zina. Ihsan is defined as the fornicator being free, Muslim, mature (mukallaf), and having had lawful intercourse. Some later Hanafi scholars consider ihsan a sign (alamah) for stoning because if someone becomes muhsan after zina, stoning is not applied; thus it does not cause but only indicates the state in which zina warrants stoning. However, the majority of Hanafis consider ihsan a condition (shart) because without it, stoning is not obligatory, just as theft requires nisab for amputation. The passage then explains a furu' (branch): if the witnesses of ihsan retract after stoning, they are not liable for blood money, because a sign does not carry obligation. This contrasts with witnesses of the zina act itself, who would be liable if they retract. The text emphasizes the distinction: the condition (with its particle) is effective, but the sign is merely indicative.

Key Terms
علامة (alamah): A sign by which the existence of a ruling is known, but without any obligation or existence being attached to it; it neither causes nor is a condition.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of a fornicator being free, Muslim, legally responsible (mukallaf), and having had valid marital intercourse.
شرط (shart): A condition on which the existence of the ruling depends; without it the ruling does not apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if witnesses of ihsan retract after the stoning, do they have to pay blood-money?
A) Yes, because they falsely accused the person of being muhsan.
B) No, because ihsan is a sign and no obligation attaches to it.
C) Yes, because ihsan is a condition and without it stoning is invalid.
D) No, because the witnesses of zina are the ones who pay.

Key Takeaway
The 'alamah is a minimal indicator that reveals a ruling's existence without being a cause or condition, as seen in the Hanafi analysis of ihsan.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
15 min
The Role of Intellect in Legal Capacity: Hanafi Position
Explaining the role of intellect in taklif and the inter-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the role of intellect in legal capacity (ahliyyah) and evaluate the arguments of the Ash'ari and Mu'tazila schools.

Core Idea
Intellect is a precondition, not a cause, for obligation; revelation remains the source of obligation.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational usul al-fiqh issue: what role does human intellect play in establishing legal responsibility (taklif)? The Hanafi school, as represented by Abu Hanifa and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, navigates between the Ash'ari reliance solely on revelation and the Mu'tazila view of intellect as an independent cause. Understanding this dispute clarifies the basis of accountability for those who never received the Islamic da'wa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The issue is whether intellect ('aql) alone can impose legal obligation (taklif) without the arrival of revelation (sam').
This is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the source of obligation.
2
State the Ash'ari position and their proof
The Ash'aris hold that intellect is useless without revelation; they cite Qur'an 17:15: 'And We were not to punish until We sent a messenger.'
They interpret the verse as indicating that no accountability exists before revelation.
3
State the Mu'tazila position and their proof
The Mu'tazila hold that intellect is a necessitating cause (illa mujiba) for obligation; they cite the story of Ibrahim (AS) who said to his father, 'Indeed I see you and your people in clear error' (Qur'an 6:74), before receiving revelation.
They argue that intellect by itself determines good and evil and imposes legal obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis distinguish between intellect as an identifier (mu'arraf) and as a cause (mujib). Intellect is a precondition for understanding the divine address but does not itself create obligation. The verse 17:15 refers to punishment in this world; afterlife accountability can arise from intellect when combined with opportunity to reflect.
The Hanafi position is that intellect makes one receptive to obligation, but the actual source is revelation. However, if one has the capacity and opportunity to reflect on God's signs, that opportunity serves like a call.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a person who grew up on a mountain peak and never received any revelation. According to the Hanafi view, if he did not have the opportunity to contemplate the existence of God, he is excused. If he had the opportunity and capacity but remained disbelieving, he is accountable.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

ترجمه و تشريح وقالت المعتزلة انه علية موجبة : - ور معتزلہ کہتے کہ عقل ہی قلعی طور پر علت موجہ ہے :- ان امور کے لئے جو اس کے نزدیک تحسن ہیں۔ اور علت مجرمہ ہے ان امور کے لئے جو اس کے نظر میں قبیح ہیں (بلکہ ) عقل کی تاثیر شرعی علتوں سے بھی بڑھ کر ہے اس وجہ سے کہ علل شرعیہ علامات ہیں
فی نفسہ علت موجہ نہیں ہیں اور علل عقلیہ فی نفسہا علت موجود ہیں اور شیخ اور تبدیل کو قبول نہیں کرتیں۔ فَلَمْ يَثْبُتُوا بِدَلِيْل الشرع مَالاً يُدْرِكَة العقل أي بناء پر یہ لوگ دلیل شرعی وارد ہونے کے با وجود ان باتوں کو ثابت نہیں مانتے جن کو عقل ادار کے نہ کر سکے مثال کے طور پر رویت باری تعالی، عذاب قبر، میزان، صراط اور آخرت کے عام احوال اور اس پر انھوں نے حضرت ابراہیم علیہ السلام کے قصے سے استدلال کیا ہے کہ انھوں نے اپنے والد سے کہا تھا إِنَّى أَرتُكَ وَقَوْمَكَ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِین میں تم کو اور تمہاری قوم " کو کھلی ہوئی گمراہی میں دیکھتا ہوں حضرت ابراہیم علیہ السلام کا یہ فرمان عقل کی مدد سے تھا جو کہ وحی کے نزول سے پہلے فرمایا تھا اور اگر وحی کے نازل ہونے کے بعد فرماتے تو یوں فرماتے أو جبن إلى (میرے پاس
He said: When the author finished discussing the rulings, he now begins the exposition of the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of the subject (mahkum 'alayh). The subject is called the mukallaf (legally responsible person). Since it is clear that capability (ahammiyyah) cannot be found without intellect, therefore: Section on the exposition of legal capacity. To establish taklif, according to us (Hanafis) the first consideration is intellect, because without intellect the address of taklif cannot be understood, and a person who does not accept the address – it is reprehensible to address him, as was explained in the discussion of Sunnah. (The author mentioned the conditions of the narrator, where he also explained intellect.) And that it (intellect) is created with variation; and intellect possesses innate variation. Thus among human groups, the most intelligent are the prophets, then the saints, then the scholars, then the wise, then the common people and the rulers, then after them the villagers and women; then within each type there is variation in degrees. So sometimes the variation is so great that on one side is a single person and on the other side a thousand people at once, and sometimes a child understands something with his intellect but an adult remains incapable. However, the Shari'ah has made puberty the level of moderate intellect for taklif. There is disagreement among scholars about whether intellect is considered or not. The Ash'aris said: Without a proof (texts of Quran and Hadith) intellect is useless. When a text is found for a matter, then instead of reason (the text) will be adopted. Therefore, something being good or bad and its being obligatory or prohibited cannot be understood by intellect (i.e., cannot be known by intellect). Thus the faith of an intelligent person (without revelation) would not be valid because the Shari'ah has not reached him (i.e., the Shari'ah has not made him obligated). This is also the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. They used this verse as proof: 'And We were not to punish until We sent a messenger' – from which it is understood that without the arrival of the legal address, a person is not considered obligated by his own intellect. The Mu'tazila said: Indeed it (intellect) is a cause that necessitates what it deems good and prohibits what it deems evil, and that its effect is over and above the legal causes, because legal causes are indicators, not necessitating in themselves, while intellectual causes necessitate by themselves and are not subject to abrogation or change. So they do not affirm by legal proof that which the intellect cannot grasp, such as seeing Allah, punishment of the grave, the scale, the path, and generally the states of the Hereafter. They used as proof the story of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) where he said to his father: 'Indeed I see you and your people in clear error.' This saying was by intellect before revelation because he said 'I see you' and did not say 'it was revealed to me.' And they said: There is no excuse for the one who has intellect regarding prevention from seeking and abandoning faith, and the intelligent child is obligated to faith because of his intellect even if the revealed message has not reached him. And the one whom the call has not reached, such as one who grew up on a mountain peak, if he does not believe in faith nor disbelief, he is among the people of the Fire due to the obligation of faith by mere intellect. But regarding the laws, he is excused until the proof is established against him. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa and also from Shaykh Abu Mansur. In that case, there is no difference between us and the Mu'tazila except in the technical classification: for them intellect is a cause (mujib), for us it is an identifier (mu'arraf). But the correct from the saying of Shaykh Abu Mansur and the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is what the author mentioned by his saying: 'And we say regarding the one whom the call has not reached: he is not obligated by mere intellect. So if he does not believe in faith nor disbelief, he is excused because he was not granted a period in which he could contemplate and deduce. But if Allah helps him with experience and provides him opportunity to realize consequences, then he is not excused even if the call has not reached him, because the opportunity and the realization of the period of contemplation are like the call in awakening the heart from the sleep of heedlessness through reflection on the evident signs. There is no reliable evidence regarding the number of the opportunity because it varies with individuals; perhaps one intelligent person may be guided in a short time to what another is not guided to, so its determination is left to Allah. And it was said that it is a fixed period of three days by analogy with the opportunity of the apostate, but this is weak. Translation and explanation: 'And the Mu'tazila said it is a necessitating cause': The Mu'tazila said that intellect is definitively a necessitating cause for matters that it deems good, and a prohibiting cause for matters that it deems evil; rather, the effect of intellect is greater than legal causes because legal causes are mere indicators, not necessitating in themselves, while intellectual causes necessitate by themselves and do not accept abrogation or change. Therefore, they do not affirm by legal proof that which the intellect cannot grasp, such as seeing Allah, punishment of the grave, the scale, the path, and the general states of the Hereafter. They used as proof the story of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) where he said to his father: 'Indeed I see you and your people in clear error.' This saying of Ibrahim was by intellect which he said before the revelation; if he had said it after revelation, he would have said: 'It has been revealed to me' (or 'to me').
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar discusses the usul al-fiqh principle of ahliyyah (legal capacity) and the role of intellect ('aql) in establishing taklif (obligation). The author begins by stating that after discussing the rulings (ahkam), he now turns to the subject of legal capacity. The subject (mahkum 'alayh) is the mukallaf, the one addressed by divine commands. Intellect is the first requisite for taklif in the Hanafi view because without it, the address cannot be understood. The text then notes that intellect varies innately among people, with prophets being the most intelligent, then saints, scholars, wise, common people, rulers, villagers, and women. Despite this variation, the Shari'ah considers puberty as the level of moderate intellect for taklif. The core of the lesson is the inter-school dispute on whether intellect alone imposes obligation. The Ash'aris (and Imam al-Shafi'i) hold that intellect is useless without revelation, citing the Quranic verse 'And We were not to punish until We sent a messenger' (17:15). The Mu'tazila hold that intellect is a necessitating cause (illa mujiba), and that its effect is stronger than legal causes; they cite the story of Ibrahim (AS) who recognized his father's error by intellect before revelation. The Hanafi position, as narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, is that intellect is a precondition but not the cause. For someone who has never received the call of Islam, he is excused if he lacks the opportunity to reflect. If he is given opportunity and intellect, he becomes obligated. The difference between Hanafis and Mu'tazila is terminological: for Mu'tazila, intellect is the direct cause (mujib); for Hanafis, it is an identifier (mu'arraf) that leads to obligation via revelation. The text clarifies that the sahih (correct) Hanafi position is that the person who never received the call is not obligated by mere intellect unless he had the capacity and opportunity to contemplate the signs of God. The period of opportunity is not fixed by a textual proof; it varies by individual. The opinion that it is three days by analogy with the apostate's period is weak.

Key Terms
الأهلية (al-ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the attribute by virtue of which a person becomes subject to divine commands (taklif).
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect; the rational faculty that enables understanding of the divine address and discernment of good and evil.
التكليف (al-taklif): The imposition of obligations by the Lawgiver upon a legally responsible person (mukallaf).
العلة الموجبة (al-illa al-mujiba): A necessitating cause; something that directly and necessarily produces a legal effect.
المعرف (al-mu'arraf): An identifier; something that makes a person capable of receiving obligation but does not itself create obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as presented in this passage, what is the ruling regarding a person who grew up on a mountain peak and never received the Islamic da'wa, and does not believe in faith or disbelief?
A) He is excused and not punished for disbelief because intellect alone does not obligate without opportunity to reflect.
B) He is punished because intellect is sufficient for obligation.
C) He is not accountable at all; he is like an animal.
D) He is considered a Muslim because of his innate nature.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that intellect is a necessary precondition for taklif, but the actual source of obligation is revelation; however, if one has the capacity and opportunity to reflect on the divine signs, that opportunity itself serves as a proxy for the call, making one accountable.

Ahliyya al-Wujub: Legal Capacity and Its Foundation
Defining the first type of legal capacity and its source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahliyya al-wujub and explain its foundation in the primordial covenant, distinguishing between the capacity for rights and obligations before and after birth.

Core Idea
Ahliyya al-wujub is rooted in the primordial covenant, not in physical maturity.

This passage introduces the first type of legal capacity in Hanafi usul: the capacity for obligation (ahliyya al-wujub). Understanding this concept is crucial because it establishes that even a newborn has a legal personality (dhimma) derived from the covenant with Allah, which allows them to hold rights and incur obligations. The passage also clarifies the transitional status of the fetus and the role of the guardian.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ahliyya
The passage states that ahliyya is of two types. Locate the first type and its definition.
The second type (ahliyya al-ada') is not discussed here.
2
Locate the definition of ahliyya al-wujub
Find the sentence that explains what ahliyya al-wujub is and what it depends on.
It is built upon the existence of a dhimma.
3
Determine the basis of dhimma
Identify the origin of the dhimma. The passage links it to a specific event from the Quran.
The day of covenant (yawm al-mithaq) is mentioned.
4
Distinguish the status before and after birth
The passage differentiates between the fetal stage and after birth regarding the suitability of dhimma.
Before birth, dhimma is suitable for rights but not for obligations against it.
5
Understand the role of the guardian
When a child is born, obligations become binding on the dhimma, but performance is carried out by the guardian.
The guardian's payment counts as the child's own payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ الْعَقْلِ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ الأهْلِيَةِ الْمَوْقُوفَةِ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ وَالأهْلِيَةُ نَوْعَانِ النَّوْعُ الأَوَّلُ أَهْلِيَةُ وُجُوبٍ وَهِيَ بِنَاءً عَلَى قِيَامِ الذِّمَّةِ أَيْ أَهْلِيَةُ نَفْسِ الْوُجُوبِ لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بَعْدَ وُجُودِ ذِمَّةٍ صَالِحَةٍ لِلْوُجُوبِ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ وَهِيَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ الْمِيثَاقِ الَّذِي عَاهَدْنَا رَبَّنَا يَوْمَ الْمِيثَاقِ بِقَوْلِهِ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى شَهِدْنَا فَلَمَّا أَقْرَرْنَا بِرُبُوبِيَّتِهِ يَوْمَ الْمِيثَاقِ فَقَدْ أَقْرَرْنَا بِجَمِيعِ شَرَائِعِهِ الصَّالِحَةِ لَنَا وَعَلَيْنَا وَالْآدَمِيُّ يُولَدُ وَلَهُ ذِمَّةٌ صَالِحَةٌ لِلْوُجُوبِ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ بِنَاءً عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْعَهْدِ الْمَاضِي وَمَا دَامَ لَمْ يُولَدْ كَانَ جُزْءًا مِنَ الْأُمِّ يَعْتِقُ بِعِتْقِهَا وَيَدْخُلُ فِي الْبَيْعِ تَبَعًا لَهَا وَلَمْ تَكُنْ ذِمَّتُهُ صَالِحَةً لِأَنْ يَجِبَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَقُّ مِنْ نَفَقَةِ الْأَقَارِبِ وَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ الَّذِي اسْتَرَاهُ الْوَلِيُّ لَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ صَالِحَةً لِمَا يَجِبُ لَهُ مِنَ الْعِتْقِ وَالْإِرْثِ وَالْوَصِيَّةِ وَالنَّسَبِ وَإِذَا وُلِدَ كَانَتْ صَالِحَةً لِمَا يَجِبُ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْوُجُودَ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ بِنَفْسِهِ وَإِنَّمَا الْمَقْصُودُ آدَاتُهُ فَلَمَّا لَمْ يَتَصَوَّرْ ذَلِكَ فِي حَقِّ الصَّبِيِّ فَجَازَ أَنْ يَبْطُلَ الْوُجُوبُ لِعَدَمِ حُكْمِهِ فَمَا كَانَ مِنْ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ مِنَ الْغَرَمِ كَضَمَانِ الْمُتْلَفَاتِ وَالْعَرَضِ كَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ وَنَفَقَةِ الزَّوْجَاتِ وَالْأَقَارِبِ لَزِمَهُ وَيَكُونَ أَدَاءُ وَلِيِّهِ كَأَدَائِهِ وَكَانَ الْوُجُوبُ غَيْرَ حَالٍ عَنْ حُكْمِهِ
When he finished explaining reason, he began explaining capacity (ahliyya) which depends on it. He said: Ahliyya is of two types. The first type is capacity for obligation (ahliyya al-wujub), which is based on the existence of a dhimma (legal personality) that is suitable for obligation in its favor and against it. It is the covenant that our Lord made with us on the day of covenant by His saying: 'Am I not your Lord?' They said: 'Yes, we bear witness.' When we acknowledged His Lordship on that day, we acknowledged all His laws that are suitable for us and against us. A human is born with a dhimma suitable for obligation in its favor and against it, based on that past covenant. As long as he is not born, he is part of the mother; he is freed with her freedom and enters the sale as a follower. His dhimma is not suitable for obligations against him such as maintenance of relatives or the price of goods his guardian buys for him, although it is suitable for rights in his favor like emancipation, inheritance, bequest, and lineage. When he is born, his dhimma becomes suitable for obligations in his favor and against him, except that the aim is not the existence of dhimma itself but rather its execution. Since that is not conceivable in the case of a child, it is possible that the obligation lapses due to the lack of its effect. What concerns rights of people involving damages like compensation for destroyed property or pecuniary matters like the price of goods and maintenance of wives and relatives, it becomes binding on him, and his guardian's payment is like his own payment, and the obligation does not cease to have effect.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of ahliyya (legal capacity) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, after finishing the discussion on reason, turns to capacity. He states that ahliyya is of two types: the first is ahliyya al-wujub (capacity for obligation), which is the inherent suitability to have rights and duties. This capacity depends on the existence of a dhimma (legal personality), which originates from the primordial covenant (mithaq) mentioned in the Quran (7:172) where humans acknowledged God's Lordship. From that moment, every human has a dhimma that is capable of receiving obligations and rights. Before birth, the fetus is part of the mother and does not have an independent dhimma for obligations against it (e.g., debts), but it does have rights (e.g., inheritance, bequest, lineage). After birth, the child's dhimma is fully suitable for both rights and obligations. However, the purpose of obligation is its actual performance, which is not possible for a child. Therefore, obligations that are purely for the benefit of others (like paying for damages, purchase price, maintenance of family) remain binding on the child's dhimma to be fulfilled by the guardian. The obligation does not become void; rather, the guardian's fulfillment counts as the child's own fulfillment. This establishes that children can have debts and obligations even if they cannot perform them themselves.

Key Terms
الأهلية (al-ahliyya): Legal capacity; the suitability of a person to have rights and obligations.
الذمة (al-dhimma): Legal personality or entity that can hold rights and obligations; it originates from the day of covenant.
الميثاق (al-mithaq): The primordial covenant between Allah and humanity (Quran 7:172).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis of ahliyya al-wujub according to this passage?
A) Reaching the age of puberty.
B) Being born alive.
C) The primordial covenant (mithaq) with Allah.
D) Being capable of understanding religious commands.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of ahliyya al-wujub is grounded in the primordial covenant, giving every human a dhimma from birth that can hold rights and obligations, even if performance is deferred.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Defining Legal Capacity (Ahliyah) and the Two Types
Defines ahliyah, dhimma, and the two types of capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahliyah, distinguish between ahliyat al-wujub and ahliyat al-ada, and explain the evidence for dhimma from the Quranic covenant.

Core Idea
Dhimma is the foundation of legal capacity; it arises from the primordial covenant and makes humans fit for rights and duties.

Legal capacity (ahliyah) is a core concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It determines who can bear rights and obligations. This lesson clarifies its definition, its two types, and the underlying legal construct of dhimma, which originates from the Quranic covenant of Alast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and its two branches
The text begins by stating that ahliyah is of two types. Identify the term (ahliyah) and its two divisions: ahliyat al-wujub and ahliyat al-ada. Note that only the first type is fully explained here.
The second type (ahliyat al-ada) is not detailed in this passage.
2
Understand the basis of ahliyat al-wujub: dhimma
Ahliyat al-wujub depends on the existence of dhimma. Dhimma is not a physical entity but a legal personality — the capacity to have rights and duties. The text defines dhimma as the covenant made with Allah on the Day of the Covenant.
Dhimma is a technical term unique to Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof for dhimma
The author cites Quran 7:172 (A lastu birabbikum) as the basis for dhimma. The universal acknowledgment of Allah's lordship implies acceptance of all His laws, establishing the inherent capacity for obligation in every human.
This is an example of using a Quranic narrative as a legal proof.
4
Distinguish between prenatal and postnatal capacity
Before birth, the fetus lacks an independent dhimma for obligations (e.g., maintenance for relatives), but it has rights (e.g., inheritance, bequest). After birth, the dhimma becomes fully capable of both rights and duties.
This shows that ahliyat al-wujub is present at birth but limited before that.
5
Apply the concept to a minor's obligations
The text explains that for a minor, obligations (e.g., compensation for damages) are binding but the guardian performs on his behalf. The obligation itself does not become null; rather, its performance is delegated.
This illustrates the interaction between wujub and ada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ الْعَقْلِ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ الأهْلِيَةِ المَوْقُوفَة عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ وَالأهْلِيَةُ نَوْعَانِ النُّوْعَ الأَوَّلُ أَهْلِيَةُ وُجُوبٍ وَهِيَ بِنَاءً عَلَى قِيَامِ الذِّمَّةِ أَى أَهْلِيَةُ نَفْسِ الْوُجُوبِ لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلا بَعْدَ وُجُودِ ذِمَّةٍ صَالِحَةٍ لِلْوُجُوبِ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ وَهِيَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ الْمِعْهَدِ الَّذِى عَاهَدْنَا رَبَّنَا يَوْمَ الْمِيثَاقِ بِقَوْلِهِ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى شَهِدْنَا فَلَمَّا أَقْرَرْنَا بِرُبُوبِيَتِهِ يَوْمَ الْمِيثَاقِ فَقَدْ أَقْرَرْنَا بِجَمِيعِ شَرَائِعِهِ الصَّالِحَةِ لَنَا وَعَلَيْنَا وَالآدَمِىُّ يُولَدُ وَلَهُ ذِمَّةٌ صَالِحَةٌ لِلْوُجُوبِ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ بِنَاءً عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْعَهْدِ الْمَاضِى وَمَا دَامَ لَمْ يُولَدْ كَانَ جُزْءًا مِنَ الأُمِّ يَعْتِقُ بِعِتْقِهَا وَيَدْخُلُ فِى الْبَيْعِ تَبَعًا لَهَا وَلَمْ تَكُنْ ذِمَّتُهُ صَالِحَةً لأَنْ يَجِبَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَقُّ مِنْ نَفَقَةِ الأَقَارِبِ وَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ الَّذِى اسْتَرَاهُ الْوَلِىُّ لَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ صَالِحَةً لِمَا يَجِبُ لَهُ مِنَ الْعِتْقِ وَالْإِرْثِ وَالْوَصِيَّةِ وَالنَّسَبِ وَإِذَا وُلِدَ كَانَتْ صَالِحَةً لِمَا يَجِبُ لَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ بِنَفْسِهِ وَإِنَّمَا الْمَقْصُودُ أَدَاؤُهُ فَلَمَّا لَمْ يَتَصَوَّرْ ذَلِكَ فِى حَقِّ الصَّبِىِّ فَجَازَ أَنْ يَبْطُلَ الْوُجُوبُ لِعَدَمِ حُكْمِهِ فَمَا كَانَ مِنْ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ مِنَ الْغُرَمِ كَضِمَانِ الْمُتْلَفَاتِ وَالْعِوَضِ كَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ وَنَفَقَةِ الزَّوْجَاتِ وَالأَقَارِبِ لَزِمَهُ وَيَكُونَ أَدَاءُ وَلِيِّهِ كَأَدَائِهِ وَكَانَ الْوُجُوبُ غَيْرَ حَالٍ عَنْ حُكْمِهِ
And when he finished from the explanation of reason, he began in the explanation of capacity which depends on it, and he said: Capacity is of two types. The first type is capacity of obligation (ahliyat al-wujub), and it is built upon the existence of the dhimma, i.e., the capacity of obligation itself is not established except after the existence of a dhimma fit for obligation for him and upon him. And it (the dhimma) is an expression of the covenant by which we covenanted with our Lord on the Day of the Covenant by His saying 'Am I not your Lord?' They said 'Yes, we testify.' So when we affirmed His lordship on the Day of the Covenant, we have affirmed all of His laws beneficial for us and binding upon us. And the human is born and he has a dhimma fit for obligation for him and upon him, based on that past covenant. And as long as he has not been born, he was a part of the mother, he is freed by her freeing, and he enters into the sale as a follow-up to her, and his dhimma is not fit for obligation upon him of rights like maintenance of relatives and the price of the item which the guardian purchased for him, although it was fit for what is due to him like freedom, inheritance, bequest, and lineage. And when he is born, it becomes fit for what is due to him and upon him, except that the obligation is not intended by itself; rather, what is intended is its performance. So when that is not conceivable in the case of the minor, then it is permissible that the obligation become nullified due to the lack of its legal effect. Whatever from the rights of people of financial liability like guarantee of destroyed property and compensation like price of the sale and maintenance of wives and relatives is binding upon him, and the performance of his guardian is like his performance, and the obligation does not divest from its legal effect.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage defines legal capacity (ahliyah) as a foundational concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first states that capacity is of two types: capacity of obligation (ahliyat al-wujub) and capacity of performance (ahliyat al-ada). The first type is based on the existence of dhimma, which is the legal personality or fiduciary capacity that every human possesses. The dhimma is not a physical entity but a metaphor for the potential to bear rights and obligations. It originates from the primordial covenant (mithaq) mentioned in the Quran (7:172), where all souls testified to Allah's lordship, thereby acknowledging all of His laws. Thus, every human is born with a dhimma that is fit for obligation (i.e., able to have rights and duties). Before birth, the fetus is considered a part of the mother and thus not an independent legal person; it does not bear obligations (like maintenance for relatives or debt from purchases made by the guardian on its behalf), but it does have rights (like freedom, inheritance, bequest, and lineage). After birth, the dhimma becomes fully capable of bearing obligations and rights. However, the text notes that obligation (wujub) itself is not the ultimate goal; rather, performance (ada) is. For a minor (sabi), since performance is not conceivable from him directly, the obligation may become nullified in the sense that he is not personally required to perform, but the obligation still attaches to him and his guardian performs on his behalf. For financial obligations (like compensation for damages, price of goods, maintenance of wives and relatives), the obligation becomes binding on the minor and the guardian's performance counts as the minor's own.

Key Terms
الأهلية (al-ahliyah): Legal capacity: the fitness of a person to bear rights and duties (ahliyat al-wujub) and to perform legal acts (ahliyat al-ada).
الذمة (al-dhimma): The legal personality or fiduciary receptacle that enables a person to have rights and be subject to duties; it originates from the primordial covenant.
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyat al-wujub): Capacity for obligation: the fitness to have rights (lihi) and duties (alayhi). It is passive capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the basis for the dhimma (legal personality) that makes a person capable of bearing obligations?
A) Reaching puberty
B) Accepting Islam
C) The primordial covenant (mithaq) in which all souls testified to Allah's lordship
D) Birth into a Muslim family

Key Takeaway
Legal capacity (ahliyah) in Hanafi usul is grounded in the dhimma, which originates from the Quranic covenant; it is divided into capacity for obligation (ahliyat al-wujub) and capacity for performance (ahliyat al-ada).

Types of Legal Capacity: Ahlīyat al-Wujūb and Ahlīyat al-Adā'
Defining two types of legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ahlīyat al-wujūb and ahlīyat al-adā', identify their foundations (dhimma and qudra), and apply the distinction to determine when a minor's action is valid or obligatory.

Core Idea
Capacity for obligation (ahlīyat al-wujūb) is present from birth; capacity for performance (ahlīyat al-adā') depends on intellect and body.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar introduces the foundational concepts of legal capacity in Hanafi usul. It begins with a dispute about whether a sane child's faith is valid, then defines the two types of capacity that determine when a person can hold rights, bear duties, and perform valid legal acts. Understanding these concepts is essential for grasping how the Lawgiver imposes obligations and accepts actions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the dispute on the minor's faith
Note that Abu Hanifa holds a child's faith valid even if not obligatory, while his disciples say it is invalid. Identify the hadith cited and how it is interpreted differently.
This dispute sets up the need to separate validity (ṣiḥḥah) from obligation (wujūb).
2
Define ahlīyat al-wujūb and its basis
The passage states that ahlīyat al-wujūb is based on al-dhimma (legal personality), present from birth. Identify which rights and duties apply to a minor and which are excluded (punishments, pure worship).
Financial rights of people (e.g., indemnity) apply; punitive ones (qiṣāṣ) do not.
3
Define ahlīyat al-adā' and its two levels
Ahlīyat al-adā' depends on two powers: understanding (intellect) and action (body). Note the deficient level (child or insane) and the complete level (sane adult).
Deficient capacity makes acts valid but not obligatory; complete capacity makes them obligatory.
4
Understand the role of puberty (bulūgh)
The Lawgiver uses puberty as a practical indicator of complete capacity. Explain why this is a concession (taysīr).
Puberty is a presumptive sign; the reality of complete intellect is difficult to ascertain.
5
Apply the concepts to new cases
Use the definitions to classify the legal effect of actions by a child, an insane adult, or a sane adult in different scenarios (financial obligations, acts of worship, punitive measures).
Practice ensures you can move from definition to application.

Source Text

وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ، وَعَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ حَتَّى يُفِيقَ». وَلِلْأَهْلِيَةِ نَوْعَانِ: الْأَوَّلُ: أَهْلِيَةُ الْوُجُوبِ، وَهِيَ تَبْتَنِي عَلَى الذِّمَّةِ. وَالْآدَمِيُّ يُولَدُ وَلَهُ ذِمَّةٌ صَالِحَةٌ لِلْوُجُوبِ لَهُ أَوْ عَلَيْهِ. غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ بِنَفْسِهِ، فَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَبْطُلَ الْوُجُوبُ لِعَدَمِ حُكْمِهِ. فَمَا كَانَ مِنْ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ مَالِيًّا كَالضَّمَانِ وَالنَّفَقَةِ يَجِبُ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ وَيَتَوَلَّاهُ وَلِيُّهُ. وَمَا كَانَ عُقُوبَةً أَوْ جَزَاءً لَمْ يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ. يُرَادُ بِالْعُقُوبَةِ الْقِصَاصُ، وَبِالْجَزَاءِ جَزَاءُ الْفِعْلِ الصَّادِرِ مِنْهُ بِالضَّرْبِ وَالْإِيلَامِ دُونَ الْحُدُودِ وَحِرْمَانِ الْمِيرَاثِ. وَأَمَّا ضَرْبُهُ عِنْدَ إِسَاءَةِ الْأَدَبِ فَمِنْ بَابِ التَّأْدِيبِ لَا مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ الْجَزَاءِ. وَحُقُوقُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى تَجِبُ مَتَى صَحَّ الْقَوْلُ بِحُكْمِهَا كَالْعُشْرِ وَالْخَرَاجِ فَإِنَّهُمَا فِي الْأَصْلِ مِنَ الْمَئُونَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ تَابِعٌ فِيهِمَا. وَمَتَى بَطَلَ الْقَوْلُ بِحُكْمِهَا لَا تَجِبُ كَالْعِبَادَاتِ الْخَالِصَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَاتِ. وَالنَّوْعُ الثَّانِي: أَهْلِيَةُ الْأَدَاءِ، وَهِيَ نَوْعَانِ: قَاصِرَةٌ تَبْتَنِي عَلَى الْقُدْرَةِ الْقَاصِرَةِ مِنَ الْعَقْلِ الْقَاصِرِ وَالْبَدَنِ الْقَاصِرِ. فَإِنَّ الْأَدَاءَ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِقُدْرَتَيْنِ: قُدْرَةُ فَهْمِ الْخِطَابِ وَهِيَ بِالْعَقْلِ، وَقُدْرَةُ الْعَمَلِ بِهِ وَهِيَ بِالْبَدَنِ. فَإِذَا كَانَ تَحَقَّقَ الْقُدْرَةِ بِهِمَا يَكُونُ كَمَالَهَا كَمَا لَهُمَا، وَقُصُورُهَا بِقُصُورِهِمَا. فَالْإِنْسَانُ فِي أَوَّلِ أَحْوَالِهِ عَدِيمُ الْقُدْرَتَيْنِ وَلَكِنْ لَهُ اسْتِعْدَادُهُمَا فَتَحْصُلَانِ لَهُ مَنْثِيَّيْنِ شَيْئًا فَشَيْئًا إِلَى أَنْ يَبْلُغَ كَالصَّبِيِّ الْعَاقِلِ فَإِنَّ بَدَنَهُ قَاصِرٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَقْلُهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْكَمَالَ، وَالْمُعْتَزِلَةُ الْبَالَهُ فَإِنَّ عَقْلَهُ قَاصِرٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ بَدَنُهُ كَامِلًا. وَتَبْتَنِي عَلَى الْأَهْلِيَةِ الْقَاصِرَةِ صِحَّةُ الْأَدَاءِ عَلَى مَعْنَى أَنَّهُ لَوْ أَتَى يَكُونُ صَحِيحًا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ. وَالْكَامِلَةُ تَبْتَنِي عَلَى الْقُدْرَةِ الْكَامِلَةِ مِنَ الْعَقْلِ الْكَامِلِ وَالْبَدَنِ الْكَامِلِ، وَتَبْتَنِي عَلَيْهَا وُجُوبُ الْأَدَاءِ وَتَوَجُّهُ الْخِطَابِ. وَلَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنْ إِدْرَاكُ كَمَالِهِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ تَجْرِبَةٍ عَظِيمَةٍ أَقَامَ الشَّارِعُ الْبُلُوغَ الَّذِي يَعْتَدِلُ عِنْدَهُ الْعَقْلُ فِي الْأَغْلَبِ مَقَامَ اعْتِدَالِ الْعَقْلِ تَيْسِيرًا.
And the faith of a sane child is not valid according to them, but according to us it is valid, even if he is not obligated. And the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers.' And legal capacity is of two types: The first: capacity for obligation, which is based on the dhimma. And the human is born with a dhimma suitable for obligation for him or against him. However, the obligation is not intended for itself, so it is permissible that the obligation becomes void due to the absence of its ruling. So what is from the rights of people that are financial, like indemnity and maintenance, becomes obligatory upon the child and his guardian undertakes it. And what is a punishment or retribution is not obligatory upon him. By punishment is meant qisas, and by retribution is meant compensation for an act committed by him through beating and inflicting pain, not the hadd punishments or deprivation of inheritance. As for his beating when he misbehaves, it is from the category of discipline, not from the types of retribution. And the rights of Allah the Most High become obligatory when the ruling regarding them is valid, like the tithe and the land tax, for they are originally from maintenance, and the meaning of worship and punishment is subsidiary in them. And when the ruling regarding them is invalid, they are not obligatory, like pure acts of worship and punishments. The second type: capacity for performance, and it is of two types: deficient, which is based on deficient power from deficient intellect and deficient body. For performance depends on two powers: the power to understand the address, which is by intellect, and the power to act according to it, which is by the body. So when power is fully realized by both, it is their perfection, and its deficiency is due to their deficiency. So the human in his initial state lacks both powers, but he has the potential for them, so they are acquired for him gradually until he reaches [maturity], like the sane child, for his body is deficient even if his intellect can potentially attain perfection, and the adult insane, for his intellect is deficient even if his body is complete. Upon deficient capacity depends the validity of performance, meaning that if he performs it, it is valid even if it is not obligatory upon him. Complete capacity is based on complete power from complete intellect and complete body, and upon it depends the obligation of performance and the address of command. And since the awareness of its perfection is not achieved except after great experience, the Lawgiver has established puberty, at which the intellect usually becomes balanced, in place of the balance of the intellect for ease.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar is an exposition on legal capacity (ahlīyah) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by addressing a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the faith (īmān) of a sane minor is valid, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it invalid. The proof quoted is the famous hadith that the pen (of accountability) is lifted from three categories: the sleeper, the child, and the insane. However, Abu Hanifa argues that validity of faith (saḥḥah) is separate from obligation (wujūb); a child's faith can be valid without being obligatory. This leads to the main discussion: the two types of ahlīyah. First: Ahlīyat al-wujūb (capacity for obligation) is based on the dhimma, a legal personality inherent in every human from birth due to the primordial covenant (mithāq). This capacity makes a person eligible for rights and duties. However, not all obligations are enforced on a minor. Obligations that are purely financial rights of people (e.g., compensation for damage, maintenance) become binding on the minor, and his guardian discharges them. Obligations that are punitive (uqūbah) or retaliatory (jazā') are not binding on a minor. 'Uqūbah here refers to qisas (retaliatory punishment), and jazā' refers to compensation for harm caused by the minor's deliberate act (like beating causing injury), not to fixed punishments (hudūd) or deprivation of inheritance. Disciplinary hitting is not considered jazā'. For rights of Allah, obligations like 'ushr (tithe) and kharāj (land tax) are binding because they are essentially maintenance (ma'ūnah) with a subsidiary aspect of worship and punishment. Pure acts of worship and pure punishments are not binding on a minor. Second: Ahlīyat al-adā' (capacity for performance) depends on the power to understand divine address (qudrat fahm al-khiṭāb, by intellect) and the power to act accordingly (qudrat al-'amal, by body). This capacity is of two levels: deficient (qāṣirah) and complete (kāmilah). Deficient capacity applies when either the intellect or body is deficient; performance by such a person is valid if they perform an act, but it is not obligatory. Complete capacity requires both intellect and body to be fully developed. Since full intellectual maturity is gradual and difficult to ascertain, the Lawgiver has pragmatically set puberty (bulūgh) as the presumptive sign of complete capacity, making taklīf (legal obligation) practical.

Key Terms
الذمة (al-dhimma): The legal personality inherent in every human from birth, making him capable of having rights and obligations. It is a covenant (ʿahd) from the primordial covenant (yawm al-mīthāq).
أهلية الوجوب (ahlīyat al-wujūb): Capacity to be subject to rights and duties, either in his favor or against him. It is based on dhimma and is present from birth.
أهلية الأداء (ahlīyat al-adā'): Capacity to perform legal acts validly. It depends on the power to understand the divine address and to act accordingly. It is of two levels: deficient and complete.
القصاص (al-qisās): Retaliatory punishment, e.g., life for life, limb for limb. It is categorized as 'uqūbah (punishment) and is not obligatory on a minor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for ahlīyat al-wujūb (capacity for obligation)?
A) The attainment of puberty
B) The dhimma (legal personality) present from birth
C) The ability to understand the address
D) The performance of an act

Key Takeaway
Legal capacity (ahlīyah) is twofold: capacity for obligation (ahlīyat al-wujūb) based on dhimma, and capacity for performance (ahlīyat al-adā') based on qudra; the former is present from birth, the latter develops gradually.

Minor's Liability: Penal vs Financial Obligations
Explaining that penal and compensatory obligations are not wajib on a minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling on whether penal and financial obligations apply to a minor, applying the usul principle that punishment requires accountability.

Core Idea
A minor is not liable for punishment or compensation, but financial obligations like 'ushr may be wajib as they are property-based.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi usul: not all obligations fall on a minor equally. While pure acts of worship and punishments require legal capacity, financial rights of Allah (like 'ushr and kharaj) can be wajib because their primary purpose is wealth, not accountability. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of obligations
The passage distinguishes between 'uquba (punishment, specifically qisas), jaza (compensation for harm), and huquq Allah (rights of Allah).
Punishment and compensation are grouped; huquq Allah are further divided.
2
Understand the ruling for each type
For punishments and compensations: they are not wajib on a minor. For huquq Allah: they are wajib if the basis of the ruling is valid (e.g., minor owns wealth that triggers 'ushr).
The condition for huquq Allah is sıhhat al-qawl bi-hukmihi (validity of the ruling's foundation).
3
Analyze the rationale (talil)
Punishments aim at mu'akhadha (taking to task), which requires accountability – a minor lacks this. Pure acts of worship (like salat) aim at performance, also inconceivable for a minor. Financial obligations aim at wealth, which does not require full capacity; thus they apply.
The talil draws on the maqsad (purpose) of each obligation type.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Suppose a minor destroys property: is compensation wajib? According to this passage, no, because it falls under jaza (compensation for harm). However, if the minor owns crops that reach the nisab, 'ushr is wajib because it is a financial right of Allah.
This illustrates the boundary: property-based rights survive lack of capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَا كَانَ عُقُوبَةً أَوْ جَزَاءَ لَمْ يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ. يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُرَادَ بِالْعُقُوبَةِ الْقِصَاصُ وَبِالْجَزَاءِ جَزَاءُ الْفِعْلِ الصَّادِرِ مِنْهُ بِالضَّرْبِ وَالْإِيلَامِ دُونَ الْحُدُودِ وَحِرْمَانِ الْمِيرَاثِ لِيَكُونَ مُقَابِلًا لِحُقُوقِ اللهِ تَعَالَى خَارِجَةً عَنْهَا. وَحُقُوقُ اللهِ تَعَالَى تَجِبُ مَتَى صَحَّ الْقَوْلُ بِحُكْمِهِ كَالْعُشْرِ وَالْخَرَاجِ فَإِنَّهُمَا فِي الْأَصْلِ مِنَ الْمُؤْنَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ تَابِعٌ فِيهِمَا. وَإِنَّمَا الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهُمَا الْمَالُ. وَمَتَى بَطَلَ الْقَوْلُ بِحُكْمِهِ لَا تَجِبُ كَالْعِبَادَاتِ الْخَالِصَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَاتِ فَإِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ الْعِبَادَاتِ فِعْلُ الْأَدَاءِ وَلَا يُتَصَوَّرُ ذَلِكَ فِي الصَّبِيِّ. وَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنَ الْعُقُوبَاتِ هُوَ الْمُؤَاخَذَةُ بِالْفِعْلِ وَهُوَ لَا يَصْلُحُ لِذَلِكَ.
And whatever is a punishment or a compensation is not obligatory upon him. It is appropriate that by 'punishment' is meant qisas, and by 'compensation' is meant the compensation of the act emanating from him by beating and inflicting pain, excluding hudud and deprivation of inheritance, so that it corresponds to the rights of Allah, may He be exalted, being excluded from them. And the rights of Allah, may He be exalted, become obligatory whenever the statement of its ruling is valid, like 'ushr and kharaj, for they are in origin from the maintenance, and the meaning of worship and punishment is secondary in them. And the intended purpose from them is only wealth. And whenever the statement of its ruling becomes invalid, they are not obligatory, like pure acts of worship and pure punishments, for the intended purpose of acts of worship is the act of performance, and that is not conceivable in the minor. And the intended purpose of punishments is the taking to task for the act, and he is not suitable for that.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar explains a key principle in Hanafi usul: penal and compensatory obligations are not wajib on minors. The author defines 'punishment' (uquba) here as qisas (retaliation), and 'compensation' (jaza) as recompense for harmful acts like beating. This excludes hudud and disinheritance, which are purely punitive. The reason is that punishment is meant to hold the person accountable (mu'akhadha), which a minor lacks capacity for. However, obligations that are purely financial, like 'ushr and kharaj, are wajib because they are originally maintenance expenses; the element of worship or punishment is secondary. The intended purpose is wealth, so if the minor's guardian pays them, it is valid. On the other hand, pure acts of worship (like prayer) and pure punishments are not wajib because the minor cannot perform the act with the required intention or be held accountable.

Key Terms
عُقُوبَة (ʿuqūba): Here it refers specifically to qisas (retaliation) as a penal obligation.
جَزَاء (jazāʾ): Here it means compensation for harm inflicted, like beating or pain, not including hudud.
حُقُوق الله (ḥuqūq Allāh): Rights of Allah that become wajib on the minor when the basis of the ruling is valid (e.g., 'ushr).
مُؤَاخَذَة (muʾākhadha): Taking to task or holding accountable, which is the purpose of punishment and requires legal capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is qisas not wajib on a minor?
A) Because qisas is a financial penalty.
B) Because the minor lacks the capacity for accountability (mu'akhadha).
C) Because the minor is not liable for any act.
D) Because qisas is a punishment, but the text includes it under 'compensation'.

Key Takeaway
A minor is not liable for punishments or compensations that require accountability, but financial rights of Allah like 'ushr and kharaj are wajib because their purpose is wealth, not personal responsibility.

Ahliyyat al-Ada: Complete vs Incomplete Capacity in Hanafi Usul
Commentary on Ahliyyat al-Ada and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ahliyyat al-ada qasirah and kamilah, state their respective bases (intellect and body), and derive the legal effect (sihhat vs wujub) for a minor's acts.

Core Idea
Incomplete capacity makes an act valid but not obligatory; complete capacity makes it obligatory.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary defines the two types of legal capacity for performance: qasirah (incomplete) and kamilah (complete). It explains that capacity depends on both intellectual and physical powers, and that only when both are perfected does obligation arise. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when a minor's acts of worship are valid and when they become binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its two types
Locate the term 'ahliyyat al-ada' and note that it is divided into qasirah (incomplete) and kamilah (complete).
The passage first discusses some preliminary rulings before explicitly defining the two types.
2
Analyze the basis of incomplete capacity
Incomplete capacity is said to be based on deficiency in intellect or body. Determine what each deficiency means: partial intellect (like a mumayyiz child) or weak body (like an old or ill person).
The text gives examples: an intelligent minor (body deficient) and an insane adult (intellect deficient).
3
Understand the legal effect of incomplete capacity
The passage states: 'upon it depends validity of performance.' This means an act performed by a person with incomplete capacity is valid (sahih) but not obligatory.
The author adds 'if he intends, it will be valid, though it is not obligatory upon him.'
4
Understand the basis and effect of complete capacity
Complete capacity requires both perfect intellect and perfect body. It is the foundation for obligation (wujub) and being addressed with rulings (khitab).
Puberty (bulugh) is the Sharia's proxy for complete capacity due to ease of determination.
5
Connect to the wisdom (hikmah)
The passage explains that obligation before complete capacity would cause hardship (haraj), which Sharia removes. Gradual acquisition of capacity until puberty shows divine mercy.
The text says 'hardship is negated in Sharia' – a key principle (la haraj).

ثم والنوع الثاني أَهْلِيَةُ أَدَاءِ وَهِيَ نَوْعَانِ قَاصِرَةُ الخ ۔ اور دوسری قسم اہمیت ادام ہے اور اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) اہمیت قاصره (۲) اہلیت کاملہ اول اہلیت قاصرہ اور یہ قدرت قاصر یعنی نقصان عقل عَدِيمُ القَدْرَتَيْن. خلاصہ کلام یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے ابتدائی احوال ( مراحل) میں یعنی شروع پیدائش کے وقت دونوں قدرتوں کا معدوم کرنے والا ہوتا ہے یعنی محروم ہوتا ہے لیکن دونوں قدرتوں کے قبول کرنے کی استعداد موجود ہوتی ہے لہذا دونوں قدر میں بچہ کو تھوڑی تھوڑی کر کے حاصل ہوں گی یہاں تک کہ بچہ حد بلوغ کو پہونچ جائے کالعصمی العاقل جیسے سمجھ بوجھ رکھنے والا نا بالغ بچہ اس کا بدن قاصر اور کمزور ہوتا ہے تو اس کی عقل کمال کا احتمال رکھتی ہے والمحور البالغ خلل دماغ والا بالغ آدمی کیونکہ اسکی عقل قاصر ہوتی ہے (ناقص ہوتی ہے ) تو اس کا بدن کامل ہوتا ہے وتبتني علیہا اور اس پر موقوف ہے یعنی اہمیت قاصر و پر صحة الاداء صحف او او اس معنی کر سکے کہ اگر وہ ارادہ کریگا تو درست ہو گی گو اس پر واجب نہیں ہے۔ وكاملة تَبْتَنِي عَلى القدرة الكاملة - دوسری قسم المبيت کاملہ پر وجوب اداء اور مخاطب بالا حکام ہوا موقوف ہے کیو نکہ کمال قدرت حاصل ہونے سے پہلے اداء کو لازم کرنے میں حرج ہوتا ہے اور حرج کی شریعت میں منفی کی منفی ہے اور چونکہ اس کمال کا صحیح معنی میں اور اک طویل تجربہ کے بعد حاصل ہوتا ہے تو شارع نے اس بلوغ کو اس کی جگہ قائم کر دیا ہے کہ جس پر پہونچ کر عقل اکثر و بیشتر معتدل ہو جاتی ہے کیوں کہ اس عمر میں آدمی کی عقل میں اعتدال اور کمال پیدا ہو جاتا ہے اور اس میں سہولت کے پیش نظر رکھی گئی ہے۔
Beating a child for rudeness and insolence is to teach discipline, not as punishment. And the rights of Allah are obligatory when the statement of its ruling is correct? Among the rights of Allah, only those rulings are obligatory upon a minor whose performance can validly be demanded from him, like 'ushr and kharaj, because originally these are expenses and the meaning of worship or punishment is subsidiary, and the purpose of both is only wealth. And if the 'ushr and kharaj are paid by his guardian on behalf of the child, then it is valid on his behalf. And when the statement of it becomes invalid, it is not obligatory. And those rulings whose performance cannot be validly demanded from minors are not obligatory upon a minor, like pure acts of worship and pure punishments, because in worship the main purpose is the actual performance of the act, and the act of performing is not attained from a child, and in punishments the purpose is to hold the person accountable, and a child does not have the capacity for accountability. Then the second type: legal capacity for performance, and it is of two types: incomplete and complete. And the second type is the capacity for performance, and it has two types: (1) incomplete capacity, (2) complete capacity. First, incomplete capacity: it is based on deficient power, i.e., deficiency of intellect and deficiency of body, because performance of rulings is related to two powers: the power to understand the address, which is obtained from intellect, and the second power is the ability to act upon that address, which relates to the body. Thus, when the existence of power comes through intellect and body, then with the perfection of these two powers, power will also be perfect, and with their deficiency, power will also be deficient. So man in his earliest stages is devoid of both powers. The summary is that man in his initial states (stages), i.e., at the time of birth, is devoid of both powers, but he has the potential to accept both powers. Therefore, the child will acquire both powers gradually until he reaches the age of puberty, like the intelligent minor: his body is deficient and weak, but his intellect has the potential for perfection. And the insane adult: because his intellect is deficient, his body is perfect. And upon it (incomplete capacity) depends the validity of performance, meaning that if he intends, it will be valid, though it is not obligatory upon him. And complete capacity: upon it depends the obligation of performance and being addressed with rulings, because before attaining perfect power, making performance obligatory involves hardship, and hardship is negated in the Sharia. And since this perfection in its true sense is attained after a long experience, the Lawgiver has established puberty in its place, upon reaching which the intellect mostly becomes balanced, because at this age the intellect of the person becomes balanced and perfect, and this is placed for ease.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn discussing the types of legal capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada). It begins with an Urdu commentary on prior rulings about minor's obligations, then presents the Arabic definition: ahliyyat al-ada is of two types: qasirah (incomplete) and kamilah (complete). The incomplete capacity is based on deficiency in intellect (like a minor with partial understanding) or deficiency in body (physical incapacity). The complete capacity requires both full intellect and physical ability, and it is the basis for obligation. The author explains that a minor gradually acquires these powers until puberty, and the insane adult has deficient intellect but perfect body, showing the relationship between capacity and actual ability. The commentary emphasizes that incomplete capacity allows valid performance (sihhat al-ada) without obligation, while complete capacity makes performance obligatory. This distinction is foundational in Hanafi usul for understanding when acts of worship are valid or obligatory for minors.

Key Terms
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada): Legal capacity to perform acts; the ability to execute actions that produce legal effects
قاصرة (qasirah): Incomplete capacity; based on deficient power (intellect or body), allowing valid performance without obligation
كاملة (kamilah): Complete capacity; based on full power of intellect and body, making performance obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul as explained in this passage, what is the legal effect of incomplete capacity (ahliyyat qasirah) on the performance of an act like prayer by a minor?
A) The act is invalid and must be made up after puberty.
B) The act is valid if performed, but not obligatory, and the minor is not required to complete it if he starts.
C) The act is obligatory and the minor is punished for leaving it.
D) The act is valid and mandatory, and he must complete it if he starts.

Key Takeaway
A minor's act performed with incomplete capacity is valid but not obligatory; only complete capacity triggers obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Six Divisions of Rulings for a Minor's Acts
Taxonomy of rulings for a minor's acts with applied disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a minor's act (hasan mahd, qabih mahd, da'ir bayn al-amrayn) and apply the Hanafi ruling on its validity and obligation.

Core Idea
A minor's act is valid if purely beneficial, invalid if purely harmful, and optional if mixed.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar presents a foundational Hanafi taxonomy of rulings for minors based on the intrinsic nature of the act. It distinguishes between purely good acts (like iman), purely evil acts (like kufr), and acts that can be both (like prayer). The commentary provides proofs and addresses key inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes, particularly regarding the worldly effects of a minor's faith and apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main categories
Extract the three categories: hasan la yahtamilu ghayrah (purely good), qabih la yahtamilu ghayrah (purely evil), and da'ir bayn al-amrayn (mixed). Note the examples given: iman, kufr, and prayer.
The passage also hints at an implied fourth side? Actually six divisions are mentioned but only three are detailed.
2
Determine the ruling for each category
For purely good acts: valid with implication of performance (bi-ilzam al-ada). For purely evil: not considered effective (la yuj'alu 'afwan). For mixed: valid without obligation of liability or makeup.
For purely evil, the text says 'apostasy is considered valid for some Hanafis' – note the intra-Hanafi difference.
3
Analyze the proof for the first category
The proof is the saying of Ali (ra) boasting of his early Islam as a child. This is a qawl sahabi used to show that a minor's iman is effective.
The dalil block in the toolbox provides details: zanni al-thubut, zanni al-dalala, but used for tarjih.
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i on minor's faith
Hanafis: a minor's iman is valid for both worldly and afterlife rulings (e.g., inheritance, marital separation). Shafi'is: valid only for afterlife, not worldly effects.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi – child inherits from disbelieving father; Shafi'i – does not.
5
Examine intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold a minor's apostasy valid for all worldly rulings (except execution). Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i hold it invalid for worldly rulings because it is pure harm.
The passage sides with the majority Hanafi view: 'we only rule for validity of faith because it is pure benefit.'

Source Text

وَالأحْكامُ الْمُنْقسمَةٌ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ أَى بَابُ ابْتِنَاءِ صبيحةِ الأَدَاءِ عَلى الأَهْلِيَّةِ أَيُّ الْقَاصِرَةِ دُونَ الأَهْلِيَةِ الْكَامِلَةِ الَّتِى ذُكِرَتْ عَنْ قَرِيبٍ إِلَى سِتَّةِ أَقْسَامِ أَشْيَارَ الْمُصَفِّفُ إِلَيْهَا عَلى التُرْتِيبِ فَقَالَ فَحَقُ اللهِ إِنْ كَانَ حَسَنًا لَا يُحْتَمِلُ غَيْرَهُ كَالإِيْمَانِ وَجَبَ الْقَوْلُ بِصِحَتِهِ مِنَ الصَّبِئ بالألزوم آدَاءٍ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الأَوْلُ وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا بصحة لأن عَلِيًّا رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهُ افْتَخَرَ بِذَالِكَ وَقَالَ شعرٌ سبَقْتُكُمْ إِلَى الإسلام طُرًّا غُلَامًا مَا بَلَغْتَ أوَانَ حُكْمِ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافَمِنْ لا يَصِيحُ إِيْمَانُهُ قَبْلَ الْبُلُوغِ فِى حَقِّ الأَحْكَامِ الدُّنْيَا فَيَرِثُ آبَاهُ الْكَافِرُ وَلَا تَبِيْنُ مِنْهُ امْرَأَتُهُ المشركة لانه مررٌ وَإِنْ صَبَحُ فِي حَق أَحكام الآخِرَةِ لأَنَّهُ مَحْضَ نَفْعِ فِي حَقَّه وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا بِلا لزوم أداء لأنه لواستوصف الصبى وَلَمْ يُصِفِ الإِسْلامَ بَعْدَ لأنَّهُ مَا عَقَلَ لَمْ تَبِنَّ إمْرَانَهُ وَلَوْلَزِمَهُ الأَدَاءُ لَكَانَ امْتِنَاعُهُ كُفْرًا وَإِنْ كَانَ قَبِيحًا لا يَحْتَمِلُ غَيْرَهُ كَالْكُفْرِ لا يَجْعَلُ عَفُوا وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّانِي وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْكُفْرِ هُوَ الردَّةُ يَعْنِي لَوْ ارْتَدْ الصبى تُغبَرُ رِدْتَهُ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ فِي حَق الأحكام الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ حَتى تَبِينَ مِنْهُ امْرَأَتَهُ وَلايَرِثُ مِنْ أَقَارِبِهِ الْمُسْلِمِيْنِ وَلَكِنْ لَا يُقْتُلُ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ تُوجَدُ مِنْهُ الْمُحَارَبَةُ قَبْلَ البُلُوْعَ وَلِوَقَتْلِهِ أَحَدٌ يَهْدِرُ دَمُهُ وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ كَالْمُرْتدِ وَعِقْدَ أَبِى يُؤسف وَالشَّافَعِي لاتَصِيحُ رِدْتُهُ فِى حَقٍّ أحكام الدُّنْيا لأنّها ضَرَر مَحْضٍ وَإِنَّمَا حَكَمْنَا بَصَحَةِ إِيْمَانِهِ لَكَوْنِهِ نَفْعًا مَحْضَا وَمَا هُوَ دَائِرٌ بَيْنَ الْأَمْرَيْنِ أَى بَيْنَ كَوْنِهِ حَسَنًا فِي زَمَانٍ وَقِبِيْحًا فِي زَمَانِ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّالث كَالصَلوةِ وَنَحْوهَا يَصحُ مِنْهُ الآدَاءُ مِنْ غَيْرِ لزوم عَهْدَةٍ وَضِمَانٍ فَإِنْ شَرَعَ فِيْهِ لا يَجِبُ اِثْمَامَهُ وَالْمُضِيُّ فِيهِ وَإِنْ أَفْسَدَهُ لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاهُ وَفِي صِيحَةِ هَذَ الأَدَاءِ بِلالُزُوْم عَلَيْهِ نَفَع مَحْضَ لَهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَعْتَادُ أَدَاء هَا فَلَا يَشْقُ ذَالِكَ بَعْدَ الْبُلُوغ وَالأحْكَامُ الْمُنقَسِعَةُ فِى هَذَ الْبَاب - اور احکام تم ہیں اس باب کے اس جگہ "هذا ترجمہ و تشریح الباب "ست اہمیت قاصرہ پر اداء کی صحت کی بنا ( یعنی صحت موقوف ہونے کے اعتبار سے ) کا باب مراد ہے یعنی انقسام مراد ہے البیت کاملہ کے اعتبار سے مراد نہیں ہے جس کا ذکر آئندہ عنقریب آئے گا۔
And the rulings divided in this chapter, i.e., the chapter on the foundation of validity of performance on capacity, i.e., the incomplete capacity, not the complete capacity which was mentioned shortly before, are six divisions which the author (al-musannif) pointed to in order. He said: So concerning the right of Allah, if it is purely good (hasan) with no possibility of being otherwise, like faith (iman), it is considered valid from the minor with the implication of performance (bi-ilzam al-ada). This is the first division. And we only say it is valid because Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, boasted of that and said in poetry: 'I preceded you all to Islam as a child before I reached the age of judgment.' And according to al-Shafi'i, his faith before puberty is not valid in respect of worldly rulings, so he inherits his disbelieving father and his polytheist wife does not separate from him because it is harm? But it is valid in respect of afterlife rulings because it is pure benefit for him. And we only say without the obligation of performance because if the minor is asked to describe Islam and he does not describe it afterwards, due to his lack of understanding, his wife does not separate from him; and if performance were obligatory, his refusal would be disbelief. And if it is purely evil (qabih) with no possibility of being otherwise, like disbelief (kufr), it is not considered effective. This is the second division. And by 'kufr' is meant apostasy (riddah), i.e., if a minor apostatizes, his apostasy is considered valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in respect of worldly and afterlife rulings, so his wife separates from him and he does not inherit from his Muslim relatives, but he is not killed because he did not commit warfare before puberty, and if someone kills him, his blood is wasted, and nothing is obligatory upon him as a renegade. And according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, his apostasy is not valid in respect of worldly rulings because it is pure harm. And we only rule for the validity of his faith because it is pure benefit. And what is between the two, i.e., sometimes good and sometimes evil, this is the third division, like prayer and similar acts. Performance is valid from him without any obligation of liability or guarantee. If he begins it, he is not required to complete it, and if he spoils it, no makeup is obligatory upon him. And the validity of this performance without obligation upon him is pure benefit for him, as it accustoms him to performing them, so that after puberty it will not be difficult for him. And the rulings divided in this chapter - and this is the end of the translation and commentary on the chapter: the intended meaning is the six divisions regarding the foundation of validity of performance on incomplete capacity (ahliyyah qasirah), not the complete capacity which will be mentioned soon.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on the matn that enumerates six divisions of rulings concerning a minor's performance. The author (al-musannif) categorizes rulings based on their nature: purely good (like iman), purely evil (like kufr), and mixed (like prayer). For purely good acts, the minor's performance is valid and considered as if performed (with effect in worldly matters according to Hanafis, but not obligatory). For purely evil acts, they are not considered valid (the minor's apostasy is effective for some Hanafis but not others). For mixed acts, the minor's performance is valid but not obligatory, and he is not required to complete or make up. The passage provides proof from Ali's statement and discusses the Shafi'i opinion that a minor's iman is valid only for the afterlife, not for worldly inheritance or marital separation, while Hanafis extend it to worldly rulings. The commentary also clarifies that these six divisions are based on incomplete capacity (ahliyyah qasirah), not complete capacity.

Key Terms
حسن لا يحتمل غيره (hasan la yahtamilu ghayrah): Purely good with no possibility of being evil; e.g., iman (faith). Such acts are valid from a minor and effective.
قبيح لا يحتمل غيره (qabih la yahtamilu ghayrah): Purely evil with no possibility of being good; e.g., kufr (disbelief). Such acts are not considered effective from a minor.
دائر بين الأمرين (da'ir bayn al-amrayn): Acts that are sometimes good and sometimes evil, like prayer; valid from a minor without obligation.
إلزام أداء (ilzam al-ada): Implication of performance – the act is considered as if performed by the minor, though not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on the apostasy (riddah) of a minor?
A) It is not considered effective at all, like a child's irrelevant actions.
B) It is valid in both worldly and afterlife rulings, so his wife separates but he is not killed.
C) It is valid only in afterlife rulings, just like faith.
D) It is punishable by execution if he is intelligent.

Key Takeaway
A minor's acts are classified into purely good (valid with effect), purely evil (generally not effective, but apostasy has worldly effect per majority Hanafi), and mixed (valid without obligation).

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Classification of Minor's Acts: Purely Good, Purely Evil, and Mixed
Expands on three categories of rulings for minors based on benefit-harm assessment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three categories of acts (hasan mahd, qabih mahd, da'ir bayna al-amrayn) and apply the Hanafi rule regarding their validity and obligation for a minor.

Core Idea
A minor's purely beneficial act is valid but not binding; a purely harmful act is effective; a mixed act is valid without obligation.

In this passage, the author expands on the classification of rulings for minors with partial legal capacity. He divides acts pertaining to the rights of Allah into three categories: purely good (like iman), purely evil (like kufr/riddah), and mixed (like salah). Understanding these categories is crucial for determining the legal effects of a minor's actions in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Note the three divisions: hasan mahd (purely good, e.g., iman), qabih mahd (purely evil, e.g., kufr/riddah), and da'ir bayna al-amrayn (mixed, e.g., salah). Understand their defining characteristics based on whether the act is always good, always evil, or varies.
2
Analyze the first category: pure good (iman)
For purely good acts, the Hanafi position is that the minor's performance is valid (sahih) but not obligatory (lazim). Examine the proof from Ali (RA) boasting of accepting Islam as a child. Understand the Shafi'i objection (no worldly validity due to harm) and the Hanafi response (benefit outweighs harm; no obligation prevents further harm).
The key distinction is between sihha (validity) and luzum (obligation).
3
Analyze the second category: pure evil (kufr/riddah)
For purely evil acts, the Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the act is not pardoned; it produces worldly effects. For apostasy, the minor's wife separates, he loses inheritance rights, but he is not killed due to his age. Note the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold it invalid for worldly rulings.
This shows that even though the minor is not mukallaf, his acts can have legal consequences.
4
Analyze the third category: mixed acts (salah, etc.)
For acts that can be good or evil depending on time (like prayer), the minor's performance is valid but not binding. He is not required to start, complete, or make up if spoiled. The rationale is that it accustoms him to worship without hardship.
This ruling is purely beneficial for the minor; it facilitates practice after puberty.
5
Summarize the underlying principle
The permissibility and effect of a minor's act depend on the balance of benefit and harm. Acts that are pure benefit are effective and valid, pure harm are effective (worldly), while mixed acts are effective but non-binding.
This principle is specific to huquq Allah; a similar division exists for huquq al-ibad.
